Master product document · v26.4 · May 2026
EvntCue v26.4
The operating layer for private events — where organizer, planner, venue, caterer, and vendors all coordinate in one shared system. Commission transparency, Cue AI, dual-language support, and mobile-first design. Not “we build all event software” — “we make every handoff invisible.”
Next.js · Supabase · Vercel
5 portals + 2 public tools

MVP scopeAll five portals at onceFull platform ships together.

Mood board image upload25MB max per imageJPEG, PNG, WebP, HEIC accepted.

Plnr hiring modelBudget-match + Plnr can applyOrgnz sees matched Plnrs by budget. Plnrs can also apply to events.
Inventory realtimeManual pre/post-event updates onlyNo live websocket connection during events. Locked. Supabase Realtime is in the stack and can be enabled later behind a feature flag with no schema changes — but no plan to revisit until post-launch demand justifies it.

Next.js app structure

app/(public)/ — Budget Calculator, Timeline Planner. No auth required.
app/(auth)/login — Single login. Post-auth redirect by role.
app/(platform)/catr/ — EvntCue Catr. Role guard: catr.
app/(platform)/venue/ — EvntCue Venue. Role guard: venue.
app/(platform)/vndr/ — EvntCue Vndr. Role guard: vndr.
app/(platform)/plnr/ — EvntCue Plnr. Role guard: plnr.
app/(platform)/orgnz/ — EvntCue Orgnz. Role guard: orgnz.
app/(platform)/admin/ — Admin panel. Role guard: admin.
middleware.ts — JWT role check. Unauthorized requests redirect to login.
lib/payment/PaymentService.ts — Abstraction interface. All payment calls go here.
lib/messaging/ — Supabase Realtime handlers + email fallback triggers.

Payment abstraction layer

Rather than integrating a payment processor directly, a PaymentService abstraction layer is built first. All payment-related code calls this interface — never the processor SDK directly. Interface methods: createAccount(), initiatePayout(), getPayoutStatus(), getBalance(), generateTaxDoc(). Swap cost: update the implementation class only — zero changes to portal code. Processor candidates: Stripe Connect (features), Adyen (stability), Dwolla (ACH / US-only).

Platform commission rate by Vndr type

Rates are admin-configurable — not hardcoded. All rates set by admin before launch. Commission rates are set per granular vendor type — not per role category. A wedding can have a DJ, a live band, and a ceremony string quartet as three separate bookings with three separate commission flows. The role categories in §40 and the dashboard UI are display groupings only. They do not drive billing. One event = multiple bookings per role category = each booking charged its own type-level rate.
Architecture clarification (v17.0): Role categories (Audio & Music Experience, Visual Production & Lighting, etc.) are UI grouping labels for the event dashboard and vendor search. They help Orgnzs navigate 50+ vendor types without overwhelm. They are not commission buckets. The platform_comm_rates table rows are granular vendor types below.

DB note: platform_comm_rates table has one row per vendor type (granular). A new column role_category (varchar, display only) groups them for the admin panel UI. The commission engine always reads the granular vndr_type field on each booking — never the role category. Admin panel shows rates grouped by role category for readability, but stores and charges at vendor type level.
04 — Database schema
Core tables — Supabase Postgres with RLS
All tables include tenant_id for multi-tenant isolation enforced via Supabase Row Level Security policies. No cross-tenant data access without explicit joins through an event relationship.
v26.1 schema merge — locked. The legacy host_events table is removed. events is now the single source of truth for all event records and gains the columns previously on host_events: orgnz_tenant_id (replaces host_tenant_id), event_type, budget. plnr_applications.host_event_id is renamed event_id and references events(id). Any RLS policy, query, or seed file referencing host_events or host_tenant_id must be updated. This merge was specced in v20.0's consistency audit (issue 18) and finalized here.

05 — Mood board
Visual inspiration boards with collaborative reactions

Who has mood boards

RoleBoard typeEvent-tied?Can share with
OrgnzFreestanding personal boardsNo — attaches to event when readyHired Plnr, anyone via public link
PlnrEvent-tied boardsYes — always attached to one eventCo-Plnrs, Vndrs on event, public link (optional)
VndrView + react + comment onlyN/ACannot create boards
Catr / VenueNo accessN/ANot applicable

Visibility modes

Private
Owner only. Working draft — no one else can see it until the owner changes visibility.
Shared — invite
Named invitees by email or username. Login required. Assign commenter or editor role per invitee.
Public link
Anyone with the link. No login required. Used for Plnr → Orgnz sharing and Orgnz → family/friends.

Image sources

Copyright note (updated v20.0): Pinterest URL pasting and social media scraping are not supported. When EvntCue facilitates distribution of third-party images (via outbound proposals in §43), the platform is the distributor and bears copyright exposure. Only licensed sources are permitted for any outbound-facing mood board use. For internal pinning (Orgnz personal board, never distributed), URL paste from any public source is permitted with a clear disclaimer. See §47 for full image sourcing spec and §43 for the outbound proposal image rules.
Direct upload
Upload from device (camera roll, file picker). Max 25MB per image. Formats: JPEG, PNG, WebP, HEIC. Stored in Supabase Storage under the board’s folder. Uploader represents they have rights to use the image.
Unsplash / Pexels API
Free commercial license. Integrated via API for in-platform image browsing. Used for mood board discovery and outbound proposal images. No scraping — API calls only. Attribution displayed where Unsplash license requires it.
URL paste — internal boards only
Paste any public image URL for personal inspiration boards. Permitted for internal reference only — these images cannot be included in outbound proposals or exported. Disclaimer shown at pin time: “This image is saved for your reference only. It may not be shared or distributed via EvntCue.”

Vndr interaction rules

Vndrs receive in-app notification + email when shared to a board. Can view all images, react with emoji, and leave text comments per image. Cannot add, remove, reorder, or edit images. Plnr sees all Vndr reactions and comments in real time via Supabase Realtime.
06 — Plnr collaboration & commission sharing
Lead Plnr + Co-Plnr model with configurable splits
Superseded in part by §44 (v18.0): The Co-Plnr permissions table below was written before the full Co-Plnr architecture was specced. §44 is the authoritative spec for Co-Plnr access rights, capability matrix, commission split mechanics, and trusted network. This section remains the reference for commission split type definitions (Overall %, Stream assignment, Mixed) which are not repeated in §44. For all other Co-Plnr behaviour, use §44.

Permissions

ActionLead PlnrCo-Plnr
View all event details✓✓
Edit event details, vendors, timeline✓✓
Create + manage mood boards✓✓
Create + assign tasks✓✓
Configure commission splits✓ (full control)View only
Delete event✓✗
Remove other Plnrs✓✗
Invite additional co-Plnrs✓✗

Commission split types

Overall %
Lead Plnr assigns a flat percentage of total commission to the co-Plnr. Simplest model — used for general collaboration.
Stream assignment
Specific commission streams (e.g. florals referral, AV referral) are assigned entirely to the co-Plnr. Used when each Plnr manages different vendors.
Mixed
Combination of overall % and stream assignments. Most flexible — handles complex multi-Plnr arrangements with different scopes of work.
Orgnz never receives commission splits. Plnr-to-Plnr only. Commission intelligence remains entirely internal — Orgnz sees only their booking costs.

Co-Plnr invite workflow

Collaboration tab → search co-Plnr by username → send invite → co-Plnr accepts → event appears in their dashboard → Lead Plnr sets commission split → co-Plnr views (not edits) split config → both Plnrs create and assign tasks → on settlement, commission distributed per split config via payment layer.
07 — Messaging architecture
In-app threads with email fallback — all event-scoped
In-app (primary)
Built on Supabase Realtime — messages appear instantly without page refresh. Plnr has a unified inbox showing all parties on an event in one thread. Each event has one thread per Plnr. Participants: Plnr + any invited Vndr / Venue / Orgnz. All portal roles can send and receive messages.
Email fallback
When a recipient is not logged in, an email notification is sent via the transactional email provider (TBD — Resend recommended). Email contains message preview and a deep link back to the in-app thread. Reply-by-email: recipient can reply directly — reply is captured and posted to the in-app thread.

Thread model

Thread ownerParticipantsScope
Plnr (unified inbox)Plnr + all Vndrs, Venue, Orgnz on eventOne thread per Plnr per event
VndrVndr + Plnr assigned to eventPer event
VenueVenue + Plnr + OrgnzPer event
OrgnzOrgnz + Plnr + VndrsPer event
Catr ↔ Plnr or OrgnzCatr + Plnr (if assigned) · Catr + Orgnz (if no Plnr)Conditional routing — events.plnr_tenant_id determines thread target. Re-evaluated on Plnr assignment change.
08 — Commission intelligence
Every commission flow — typed, tracked, and disclosed. Service fees separated.
On a typical $300K corporate gala, over $75,000 moves between parties in commission flows. Currently, no single platform tracks all of these simultaneously. EvntCue's commission intelligence system makes every flow visible — for every party — takes a small facilitation fee on each tracked flow, and draws a hard architectural line between commissions (party-to-party incentives) and service fees (professional charges billed to the Organizer).
The fundamental separation: A commission is money that moves between vendors, venues, and planners as an incentive or referral — the Organizer never sees it. A service fee is money the Organizer pays the Plnr for their professional services — fully visible, invoiced, and on the Organizer's receipt. These are different tables, different RLS rules, and different UI surfaces. They must never be merged.

Inside vs outside commissions

TypeDefinitionOrganizer sees?Plnr sees?Example
Inside commissionFlows between vendors, venues, and other non-Organizer parties. Exist regardless of whether a Plnr is involved.NeverYes — full detailVenue charges Catr 12% of F&B revenue. Venue receives kickback from preferred florist.
Outside commissionFlows from a vendor or venue to the Plnr as a referral incentive. The Plnr may optionally disclose these to the Organizer.Toggle — Plnr controls disclosure. When disclosed: "Your planner receives a referral from this vendor." No amount shown.Yes — full detail including rate and amountFlorist offers Plnr 15% referral. Venue offers Plnr 10% sourcing fee.
Platform feeEvntCue's 2.5% facilitation fee on all transactions.Never (charged to vendor/venue side)Yes$1,000 booking → $25 to EvntCue.

Commission flow type enum — full definition

The commission_flows.type column is now a strict enum. Every flow must have one of these types. No generic or untyped flows are permitted.
v26.1 — enum split locked. platform_fee and platform_marketplace_fee are now distinct types. platform_fee is the always-on 2.5% facilitation fee (1% processing + 1.5% platform), applied to every transaction regardless of Vndr tier. platform_marketplace_fee is the tier-variable Vndr commission (8% Listed / 6% Professional). Previously both were stored as platform_fee, making it impossible to distinguish processing revenue from marketplace revenue in finance reports. Migration: any existing platform_fee rows where the rate is > 2.5% must be updated to type=platform_marketplace_fee before the enum constraint is applied.
Type valueFrom → ToInside / OutsideTypical rateDisclosed to Organizer?
vndr_referralVndr → PlnrOutside0–20% of booking (Vndr slider — capped at 20% per v26.1)Plnr toggle — off by default
venue_referralVenue → PlnrOutside8–15% of venue feePlnr toggle — off by default
venue_in_houseOrgnz → VenueInsidePer-event flat or % (cake cutting, corkage)Appears on Organizer invoice as a line item (not labeled as commission)
venue_kickbackVndr → VenueInsideAnnual fee or per-event % for preferred listNever
venue_fb_surchargeCatr → VenueInside10–18% of F&B revenue only (not labor)Never — but Catr sees it deducted from their payout
co_plnr_splitLead Plnr → Co-PlnrInsideConfigured by Lead PlnrNever — Plnr-to-Plnr only
platform_feeAny party → EvntCuePlatform2.5% of transaction (1% processing + 1.5% facilitation)Never to Organizer — visible to vendor/venue paying it
platform_marketplace_feeVndr → EvntCuePlatformTier-variable: 8% on Vndr Listed (free) bookings, 6% on Vndr Professional bookings. Per §66.1 hybrid model: on Plnr-mediated post-hire events the rate splits — EvntCue keeps 1.5% residual; Pro Plnrs earn the remaining 6.5%/4.5%; Solo Plnrs earn half that (3.25%/2.25%) with the other half going to EvntCue. Vndr pays the same total either way.Never to Organizer — visible to Vndr who is paying it
virtual_attendance_feeOrganizer → EvntCuePlatformAdmin-configurable % of virtual ticket revenueShown as platform fee on ticket checkout

Service fees — the clean separation

A Plnr's planning fee is not a commission. It is a professional service charge — the same category as a lawyer's retainer or a consultant's project fee. It is fully visible to the Organizer, invoiced through EvntCue's payment layer, and lives in its own table: service_fees. It must never appear in commission_flows.
What goes in service_fees
Plnr planning fee (flat or %). Day-of coordination fee. Design consultation fee. Any professional charge billed directly to the Organizer for the Plnr's time and expertise. The Organizer sees every service fee on their invoice — no exceptions.
What goes in commission_flows
Referral payments between vendors and Plnrs. Venue kickbacks and surcharges. Platform fees. Co-Plnr splits. Everything the Organizer never sees. RLS ensures Organizer rows in commission_flows return zero results — no query, no join, no API call can expose them.
Why this matters at build time
If service fees are stored in commission_flows, the disclosure toggle logic breaks — a Plnr might accidentally hide their planning fee from the Organizer's invoice. The tables must be separate from day one. Migrations that mix them are not permitted.

service_fees table — full schema

ColumnTypeDescription
iduuid PKAuto-generated
event_iduuid FK → eventsEvent this fee is for
plnr_tenant_iduuid FK → tenantsThe Plnr billing this fee
organizer_tenant_iduuid FK → tenantsThe Organizer being billed
fee_typeenum(flat|percentage)Flat dollar amount or % of total event budget
amountinteger (cents)Dollar amount in cents — always stored, even for percentage fees (calculated at invoice time)
rate_pctnumeric nullableIf fee_type = percentage, the rate (e.g. 15.00 for 15%)
basis_amountinteger nullable (cents)If fee_type = percentage, the amount the rate was applied to
descriptiontextPlain-English label shown on Organizer invoice: "Full-service planning fee", "Day-of coordination", "Design consultation"
statusenum(draft|invoiced|paid|refunded)Lifecycle state. Draft = not yet sent. Invoiced = Organizer has received invoice. Paid = deposit or full payment collected via Stripe.
invoice_urltext nullableSigned URL to PDF invoice stored in Supabase Storage
stripe_payment_intent_idtext nullableStripe PaymentIntent for this fee — separate from booking deposits
paid_attimestamptz nullableWhen payment was confirmed
created_attimestamptzAuto now()

RLS rules for service_fees

RoleCan readCan write

Organizer (own rows)All rows where organizer_tenant_id = own tenantRead only — cannot edit fee amounts

Vndr commission slider — visibility boost model

Vndrs can offer a referral rate to Plnrs on a per-package basis. This is configured as a slider in the Vndr's package setup. The higher the offered rate, the more prominently the vendor is surfaced in Cue's suggestions to Plnrs — a transparent, marketplace-based incentive model rather than a hidden pay-to-play system.
How the slider works
Per service package, the Vndr sets a referral rate: 0–20% of package price (admin-capped at 20% per v26.1). This rate is offered to any Plnr who books the package for a client. The rate is baked into the Vndr's pricing — they absorb it from their margin. The Organizer's quoted price does not change based on the slider position.
How it affects Cue's ranking
In Cue's vendor suggestion algorithm (§26), the referral rate is a ranking signal visible only to Plnrs. A florist offering 15% ranks above an identical florist offering 0%, all else equal. The weight of this signal is admin-configurable (default: 10% of total ranking score — meaningful but not dominant). Style match and performance score still outweigh it.
What the Plnr sees
In the Plnr's marketplace view: "[Vendor name] · 4.8★ · from $800 · 15% referral." The referral rate is displayed as a badge on the vendor card — visible only to Plnrs, never to Organizers. Plnr can filter/sort by referral rate. When Plnr books, the referral amount is calculated: $800 × 15% = $120 flows as a vndr_referral commission_flow record after event completion.
Payout timing: Vndr referral commissions are held in escrow until 48 hours after event completion. This protects against cancellations and ensures the Plnr has actually delivered the booking. The same escrow logic applies to all commission_flows — no commission is paid until the event is complete and no disputes are open.

Commission flow — complete example

v26.4: A $5,000 florals booking, free-tier Vndr, 15% referral slider, Plnr Pro post-hire, disclosing to Organizer:
FlowTypeAmountFrom → ToOrganizer sees?
Organizer pays floristPayment (not a commission_flow)$5,000Organizer → VndrYes — invoice line item
Stripe processingVendor expense (NOT a commission_flow per v26.4)~$155Vndr → StripeYes — receipt line item
Platform feeplatform_fee$125 (2.5%)Vndr → EvntCueYes — receipt line item
Marketplace — EvntCue residualplatform_marketplace_fee · post-hire Pro$75 (1.5%)Vndr → EvntCueNo
Marketplace — Plnr shareplatform_marketplace_fee · post-hire Pro$325 (6.5%)Vndr → PlnrNo
Plnr referral (slider)vndr_referral$750 (15%)Vndr → Plnr"Your planner receives a referral from this vendor." No amount shown.
Vndr nets—$3,570—No
Plnr planning feeservice_fees$2,500 (flat)Organizer → PlnrYes — on invoice as "Full-service planning fee"
v26.4 changes: Marketplace fee now appears as TWO rows (EvntCue residual + Plnr share) per §66.1. Stripe processing is a separate receipt line, not a commission_flow. For self-managed events the marketplace fee is one row at 8% to EvntCue; pre-hire and Solo splits per §66.1 fee table. All amounts computed via calc_fee_cents (migration 013) for half-up rounding. EvntCue/Plnr split uses subtraction (not independent rounding) to guarantee shares sum exactly to total.

Dual-basis catering commission model

Catering commissions run on two independent bases: food & beverage revenue (venue takes 10–15%) and service fee covering labor (venue typically takes 0%). Applying the venue rate to the full invoice including labor costs a Catr $1,200–$1,800 per event unnecessarily. EvntCue enforces the correct split automatically — the venue_fb_surcharge flow type applies only to the F&B component of the BEO, not the total invoice.

Corporate Organizer mode — commission context off

When an Organizer account has commission_context = false (set at account creation or by admin), all commission-related UI is suppressed entirely. No disclosure notes appear. No referral acknowledgments. No commission-adjacent language anywhere in their portal. This is the correct mode for corporate event coordinators whose company employs a salaried planner — commission flows are irrelevant to their workflow and would create confusion. The flag is Organizer-account-level, not event-level.

Disclosure manager

Toggle-based per commission type. State-configurable per account — no digital signature required at launch. Generates plain-English disclosure addendum for contracts. Flags legally sensitive undisclosed flows for CA and NY compliance exposure. Organizer commission visibility is permanently hidden regardless of disclosure settings — disclosure only determines whether the Organizer receives an acknowledgment note ("Your planner receives a referral from this vendor"), never the actual amount.
Platform revenue from commission flows: At 1,000 events/month with $8,240 average commission pool per event, the 1.5% facilitation component of the platform fee on tracked flows generates $990K–$2.97M annually in pure-margin revenue on top of subscriptions.
09 — Cue, the AI assistant
Powered by Anthropic Claude — embedded in every portal
Cue is EvntCue's embedded AI assistant, powered by Anthropic's Claude API. The default model is claude-sonnet-4-5 for routine touchpoints (planning assistant, intake parser, vendor matching) and claude-opus-4-7 is used selectively for high-stakes touchpoints (proposal drafting, post-event ROI report, run-of-show generator) where output quality justifies the cost. The model identifier is held in process.env.CUE_MODEL_DEFAULT and process.env.CUE_MODEL_PREMIUM — never hardcoded — so the model can be upgraded without a deploy. Cue is accessible from every portal and knows the full context of every event file: the guest list, the vendors booked, the budget status, the timeline, the dietary flags, and the full commission structure. The system prompt is the product: it injects full event context so Cue's output is specific and actionable, not generic.
v26.1 — cost pass-through locked. Cue API spend is fully passed through to users via the credit system in §19. Free-tier credits cover trust-building usage; once a user exhausts their tier's credits, the $9.99 / 100 message add-on funds further usage at a ~4× margin over Sonnet 4.5 API cost. The platform never subsidizes heavy AI usage on low-revenue events. Add-on price is admin-configurable per cue_addon_pricing table — model upgrades that raise per-message cost can trigger a price refresh without a code change.
Cue
"I'm watching two open items on tonight's Chen Wedding: the pasta cooker rental hasn't been confirmed, and the ice order is still open. Also — the Grand Ballroom transition window is tight. Nexus Corp ends at 5pm but Chen setup starts at 3pm. Confirm with the venue that the pre-function space is available as a staging area. What do you need from me?"

Nine Cue touchpoints

Vendor matching
Scores and ranks the full Vndr database against an event brief — style, availability, budget, dietary compliance, past performance. Returns ranked recommendations with reasons in under 2 seconds.
~$0.18/call Saves 2–4 hrs
Proposal drafting
Input event type, guest count, budget, venue, service level. Cue outputs a complete scoped proposal with line items, payment schedule, and contract language in under 30 seconds.
~$0.40/call Saves 4–6 hrs
Planning assistant
Context-aware co-planner embedded in every event file. Knows the full event state and answers operational questions in real time — budget status, risk flags, vendor confirmations.
~$0.04/msg Always-on
Run-of-show generator
Given event type, start/end time, guest count, and service style, Cue generates a complete minute-by-minute run-of-show with owner assignments, setup windows, and food safety checkpoints.
~$0.12/call Saves 1–2 hrs
Post-event ROI report
After an event closes, Cue synthesizes attendance, spend, vendor performance, and client feedback into a structured ROI report the Plnr can send directly to the corporate Orgnz.
~$0.22/call
Budget intelligence
Reads historical event data to flag whether a budget is realistic, which line items are overpriced, and where there is room to protect or grow margin.
~$0.10/call
Predictive insights
Surfaces patterns invisible to humans — Vndrs who run late on Saturdays, Catrs with lower satisfaction at 300+ guests, proposal formats that win 74% vs 41% of the time.
Data moat
Client intake parser
When a new inquiry arrives — even a messy email or voice note transcript — Cue extracts structured data: event type, date, guest count, budget, preferences, and red flags. Zero manual entry.
~$0.06/call
Vndr performance scoring
Across all events, Cue reads Vndr feedback, on-time rates, and budget accuracy to generate composite performance scores that power the matching engine's recommendations.
Compounds with data
Plnr recommendation gate
After budget is set, before the first vendor category unlocks, Cue evaluates budget size and vendor category count against admin-configured thresholds. Below threshold: Cue offers to manage bookings directly. Above threshold: Cue suggests matching the Orgnz with a Plnr. Decision switches Cue’s system prompt mode — companion (Plnr hired) or decision-engine (self-managed). See §42 for full spec.
§42 MVP
All-in Cue cost per event: $0.60–$1.10 at Sonnet 4.5 default; $1.80–$3.20 if Opus 4.7 is selected for premium touchpoints. Cost is fully passed through to users via tier credits and the $9.99 / 100 message add-on (§19). Cue's system prompt switches based on whether an Orgnz has hired a Plnr (companion mode — §25) and based on the outcome of the Plnr recommendation gate (§42). Against an average platform revenue of $12,800 per event, even Opus pricing is a 0.025% cost that saves 8–10 hours of human labor. ROI on AI spend is approximately 600× at Opus, 1,500× at Sonnet. The more events on the platform, the smarter Cue gets — compounding moat.
10 — Mobile strategy
Responsive from day one — no native app initially
EvntCue is responsive from day one per the architecture decision in Section 2. Venue managers check bookings on phones. Catrs pull BEOs at the loading dock. Event leads reference run-of-show on-site. The mobile experience is purpose-built, not a shrunk desktop — four core patterns govern every portal.
Sidebar → bottom navigation
Navigation collapses to a 5-item bottom bar with 44px minimum touch targets and badge counts. Moves navigation to the thumb zone where 80% of mobile interaction happens. Single highest-impact change across all portals.
Data tables → stacked cards
Every data table (commission ledger, invoice list, staff schedule, equipment list) converts to a card-per-row format with key-value pairs stacked vertically. Same data, zero horizontal scrolling. Requires HTML restructure — not CSS-only.
Wide grids → horizontal scroll strips
4-column card grids (space listings, Vndr cards, menu items) become horizontally scrollable single-row strips. Works for any card-based content regardless of the underlying data model.
Calendar grid → vertical timeline
The 14-column daily load grid cannot render at 375px. Mobile replacement is a vertical chronological timeline with colored dots, event names, and status chips. Functionally identical — better for on-site use.

12 — Key cross-portal workflows
How the five portals connect in real event scenarios

Workflow A — Orgnz books directly (no Plnr)

StepActorPortalAction
1OrgnzOrgnzCreates event. Sets budget.
2OrgnzOrgnzBrowses marketplace. Selects Venue, Catr, Vndrs.
3OrgnzOrgnzCompletes 4-step booking wizard per service. Bookings confirmed.
4VndrVndrBooking request received. Accepts. Appears on calendar.
5VenueVenueInquiry auto-created. Accepts + holds date.
6CatrCatrEvent appears in BEO list. Catr builds event details.
7OrgnzOrgnzTracks all bookings + payment schedule. Manages mood board.

Workflow B — Orgnz hires Plnr → Plnr manages event

StepActorPortalAction
1OrgnzOrgnzCreates event + sets budget.
2OrgnzOrgnzVisits Plnr Marketplace. Sees budget-matched Plnrs. Sends hire request.
3PlnrPlnrReceives hire notification. Accepts. Event appears in Plnr dashboard.
4PlnrPlnrCreates event mood board. Shares with Orgnz (public link) + Vndrs.
5VndrVndrReceives shared mood board. Reacts + comments on images.
6PlnrPlnrBooks Vndrs on behalf of Orgnz. Manages commission flows.
7PlnrPlnrOptionally invites co-Plnr. Sets commission split.
8AllAll portalsEvent executes. Commissions settle. Payouts via abstracted payment layer.

Workflow C — Plnr invites co-Plnr + splits commission

StepActorAction
1Lead PlnrCollaboration tab → search co-Plnr by username → send invite.
2Co-PlnrReceives invite. Accepts. Event appears in their dashboard.
3Lead PlnrSets commission split: overall % or stream assignment or mixed.
4Co-PlnrViews (not edits) split config. Begins managing assigned Vndrs.
5Both PlnrsCreate + assign tasks. Track status in Collaboration tab.
6Both PlnrsCommission Intelligence shows split amounts per Plnr in By Party view.
7PlatformOn settlement, commission distributed per split config via payment layer.
13 — Resolved decisions
All questions resolved — zero open items. Build-ready.
All 5 previously open questions resolved in v9.3. EvntCue has zero remaining open product, architecture, or business decisions. The platform is fully specced and build-ready.
QuestionCategoryDecisionRationale
Transactional email provider Tech Resend Modern API, native Next.js/React Email integration, 3,000 emails/day free tier, $20/mo for 50K emails. Fastest path to working booking confirmations, invite emails, and messaging fallback. Environment variable: RESEND_API_KEY. Domain verification required before launch.
Payout processor Payments Stripe now · Dwolla + Trustap at Month 3 Launch on Stripe Connect only — fastest path to live payments, lowest integration overhead. At Month 3 (when real vendor payouts begin at scale): add Dwolla for ACH vendor disbursements (lower freeze risk, better payout UX) and Trustap for high-value event escrow ($2K+ bookings). PaymentService abstraction layer already built — processor swap requires no portal code changes. Full hybrid architecture: Stripe for card acceptance + subscriptions, Dwolla for vendor ACH payouts, Trustap for milestone escrow on large bookings.
Paid plan prices Business Set in §19 — fully resolved Orgnz Free / Celebrate $39/mo ($35 annual) · Plnr Solo free / Pro $69/mo ($599 annual, save $229) · Venue Starter free / Professional $149/mo ($129 annual) · Catr Starter free / Professional $89/mo ($79 annual) · Vndr Listed free 8% commission / Professional $49/mo ($39 annual) 6% commission · 2.5% total platform fee (1% processing + 1.5% facilitation) on all transactions all tiers. Lowest combined rate of any multi-portal event platform — below HoneyBook (3% processing-only), Eventbrite (10–14%), and Airbnb (9–15%). See §19 for full feature matrices and Stripe implementation map. v26.1 reconciliation: Plnr Pro now $69/mo with annual option (was $79, no annual) per §66 founding intent. Vendor commission slider cap reduced 25% → 20%.
Inventory realtime tracking during events Catr No realtime — pre/post manual updates Caterers update inventory before and after events. No live websocket connection during events. Rationale: adds significant build complexity for a use case that most caterers handle by prep quantity, not live tracking. Supabase Realtime is already available in the stack — if post-launch demand requires it, enable it with a feature flag and a "Live inventory" toggle in the Catr dashboard. No schema changes needed.
Can Catr message Plnr or Orgnz directly? Catr Conditional — Plnr if assigned, Orgnz if no Plnr Catr messaging follows a conditional routing rule based on whether a Plnr is assigned to the event:

Plnr assigned: Catr messages Plnr only. Orgnz remains shielded — all communication mediated through Plnr. This protects commission arrangements and keeps the Orgnz experience clean.

No Plnr assigned (Orgnz-direct booking): Catr can message Orgnz directly. This is the correct fallback — if there is no Plnr to mediate, the Orgnz is the responsible party and must be reachable.

Logic: Check events.plnr_tenant_id — if populated, Catr thread target is Plnr. If null, Catr thread target is Orgnz. This check runs at thread creation time and is re-evaluated if a Plnr is added or removed mid-event.

DB impact: message_threads.participants[] is built dynamically. Thread model: Catr sees one thread per event, targeted at whichever party is the current responsible contact. If a Plnr is later assigned to a previously Orgnz-direct event, Catr thread target transitions to Plnr and Orgnz is removed from Catr's thread visibility.
Build status: With all decisions resolved, Claude Code can initialize the full EvntCue codebase — repo, Supabase project, schema migrations, auth, role guards, payment abstraction, and portal shells — in a single focused session. No decision gates remain.
14 — Market & business case
The event economy has no operating system. EvntCue is it.
Every event involves five or more parties — a Orgnz, a Venue, a Plnr, a Catr, and multiple Vndrs. Each party runs their own spreadsheets, their own email threads, their own invoicing. Commission flows between parties are tracked nowhere or tracked incorrectly. A $300,000 corporate gala generates over $75,000 in commission flows that nobody has full visibility into simultaneously.
Market size
Global event management software
$34.7B by 2029
17.4% CAGR
AI in events
AI solutions segment specifically
$2.9B by 2030
Fastest-growing segment
Vertical SaaS multiple
Valuation vs horizontal SaaS
12× vs 5.2×
Q4 2025 benchmarks

Competitive position

Cvent serves enterprise buyers at enterprise prices. HoneyBook serves solopreneurs and plateaus immediately. Nobody has seriously built the operating system for the professional event planner scaling from $500K to $5M in revenue — and nobody has built transparent, cross-party commission intelligence at all. That is EvntCue's position.

Platform subscriptionMonthly per-role (Freemium Orgnz · Paid Catr/Venue/Vndr/Plnr). Pricing TBD.Phase 1

15 — Missing features · market-informed additions
12 features added from competitive analysis — v6.0
Source: Competitive analysis against Tripleseat, Planning Pod, Caterease, HoneyBook, Bizzabo, and Cvent — combined with market gap identification. Features are ranked P0 (launch-blocking), P1 (near-term retention), P2 (growth phase), and Future (enterprise/Phase 3).

P0 — Launch-blocking gaps (must ship at launch)

FeaturePortal(s)Why it's P0Build notes
Floor plan & layout tool Venue Tripleseat's primary differentiator is 2D/3D drag-and-drop floor plans. Venues require this before signing — without it, EvntCue Venue loses every RFP head-to-head against Tripleseat from day one. Start with 2D drag-and-drop (tables, chairs, stage, bar). Store layout JSON per space per event in venue_spaces. 3D walkthrough is Phase 2. Share layout as PDF or link with client.
Review & rating system All The Orgnz marketplace won't convert without trust signals. Vndrs show a "rating" field in the schema but there is no mechanism to collect, verify, or display reviews. A marketplace with no reviews is not a marketplace. Post-event trigger: Orgnz receives review request 48hrs after event closes. Star rating (1–5) + text comment per Vndr/Catr/Venue/Plnr. Published on public profile pages. Schema: reviews table with reviewer_id, reviewee_id, event_id, stars, body, verified_booking boolean.
Public discovery pages (SEO) Vndr · Venue · Catr Without SEO-indexable public profiles, EvntCue is invisible to Orgnz users who haven't signed up yet. This is the primary organic acquisition channel and also justifies why Vndrs pay a subscription fee — they get found by new clients. Public URLs: /venue/omni-grand-dallas, /vendor/luna-and-bloom. Show: name, bio, photos, services, reviews, availability calendar (month view), starting price, "Request booking" CTA. Next.js server-side rendered for SEO. No login required to view.
Contract management & e-signature Plnr · Venue · Vndr HoneyBook's dominance among solopreneurs is almost entirely driven by e-signature. Planning Pod users leave for HoneyBook just to sign contracts. This is the single most cited reason professionals maintain parallel tools. Without it, EvntCue requires a second tool for the most legally critical moment in every booking. Template library (per role): venue hire agreement, Plnr services contract, Vndr booking confirmation. Variable insertion from event data. Send for e-signature via email deep link. Status tracking: draft → sent → signed → countersigned. Store signed PDF in Supabase Storage. Schema: contracts table with event_id, template_id, status, signed_at, signed_by.

P1 — Near-term retention features (ship within 60 days of launch)

FeaturePortal(s)Why it mattersBuild notes
Google Calendar & Outlook two-way sync All Event professionals live in Google Calendar. If EvntCue events don't appear there automatically, the platform creates a second calendar to manage instead of replacing the first. This is a churn accelerant disguised as a missing feature. OAuth integration per user. Push events to external calendar on creation/update/delete. Pull availability blocks from external calendar to prevent double-booking. Use Google Calendar API + Microsoft Graph API. Store external_calendar_id per event.
QuickBooks & Xero integration Catr · Venue · Plnr Every professional Catr, Venue, and Plnr uses accounting software. Planning Pod users cite this absence as the top operational friction point. Without it, every EvntCue invoice and payment requires manual re-entry — a significant friction point for the paid professional tiers most likely to churn. Sync invoices and payments via QuickBooks Online API + Xero API. Map EvntCue event categories to accounting chart of accounts. Two-way: push new invoices, pull payment confirmations. Store accounting_ref_id per invoice. Reconciliation view in admin.
Ticketed / public event support Venue · Plnr Venues and Plnrs regularly run ticketed public events — wine tastings, fundraisers, seasonal experiences, charity galas. Tripleseat added this. Without it, Venues must maintain Eventbrite in parallel and EvntCue captures no revenue from the public event side of their business. Event types: ticketed (public) vs. private (booked). Ticketed events: create ticket tiers (general, VIP, early bird), set capacity per tier, generate purchase page. Payment via abstracted payment layer. Guest list auto-generates from ticket purchases. Sold tickets feed into check-in module (see P2). Schema: add event_type enum(private, ticketed) to events, add ticket_tiers and ticket_purchases tables.
Vendor COI & insurance verification Venue · Vndr Most venues require Vndrs to carry liability insurance and provide a certificate of insurance (COI) before working on-site. Currently there is no place in the spec to store, verify, or flag expiring COIs. Venues get caught without proper documentation creating real liability exposure. COI upload per Vndr: PDF upload to Supabase Storage. Fields: insurer, policy number, coverage amount, expiry date. Venue portal: COI status per Vndr per event — valid / expiring (30-day warning) / expired. Email alert to Vndr when COI is expiring. Schema: add vndr_insurance table with tenant_id, doc_url, expiry_date, verified_by_venue.
Multi-currency & tax jurisdiction support All The roadmap targets Gulf and APAC expansion by Phase 2. But the payment abstraction layer and commission ledger are US-centric. Retrofitting currency and tax into a mature schema is extremely expensive. Design it in now. Add currency (ISO 4217) and tax_jurisdiction fields to commission_flows, bookings, and invoices. Default USD. Tax rate table: tax_rates with jurisdiction, rate_type (sales_tax, VAT, GST), rate_pct, effective_date. Display currency symbol based on tenant locale. FX conversion at time of transaction via exchange rate API (store snapshot).

P2 — Growth phase features (Phase 2 roadmap)

FeaturePortal(s)Description
Post-event attendee survey & NPS Plnr · Orgnz Automated post-event survey sent to attendees 24hrs after event close. Star rating + open text. NPS score calculated per event. Feeds Cue's ROI report with real satisfaction data. Gives Plnrs a powerful retention argument with corporate Orgnz: "Here's what your 380 attendees said." Schema: event_surveys, survey_responses. Send via email provider (TBD). Display aggregate NPS in Plnr and Orgnz dashboards.
Guest check-in & on-site management Plnr · Venue Day-of mobile tool: guest list, check-in (tap name or scan QR), dietary flag display per guest, seating assignment. EvntCue's mobile-first design (vertical timeline, bottom nav) is the perfect shell for this. Connects directly to ticketed event purchases and RSVP list. Add guest_checkins table with timestamp, method (manual, QR), checked_in_by.
Sponsorship management module Plnr Tracks sponsor relationships, activation deliverables, and payments for galas, charity events, and conferences. Sponsor CRM within each event: company, contact, tier, contracted deliverables, payment status, activation details. Commission ledger entry type: "sponsorship placement" (Plnr earns % of sponsor fee for brokering). Schema: event_sponsors, sponsor_deliverables.

Future — Enterprise / Phase 3 features

FeatureDescription
DMC / destination management company portal DMCs manage all vendors on behalf of a corporate client and earn on both sides simultaneously — they are neither a pure Plnr nor a pure Vndr. They need a hybrid portal combining marketplace sourcing, multi-Plnr coordination, commission management at scale, and client-facing event microsites. This is the natural Phase 3 enterprise offering and the portal that handles the $300K+ corporate events that EvntCue is positioning toward. Schema additions: dmc_tenants, dmc_managed_events, dmc_commission_pools.
Accessibility compliance reporting Venue ADA compliance status per space (wheelchair access, hearing loop, accessible restrooms). Dietary and medical accessibility flags per guest. Compliance report exportable for corporate event planners who must submit accessibility documentation to their legal teams. Increasingly required for government and education sector events.
Carbon & sustainability tracking Estimate event carbon footprint from: catering (food miles, dietary choices), transportation (attendee travel), venue energy consumption, waste. Display per-event sustainability score. Generate client-facing sustainability report. Feeds ESG reporting for corporate Orgnz accounts. Vendor sustainability ratings (local sourcing, renewable energy, certified suppliers) factor into Cue's matching score.
Event insurance marketplace Embedded insurance products at the booking confirmation step: event cancellation insurance, liability coverage for Plnrs, equipment insurance for AV Vndrs. API integrations with specialist event insurers. EvntCue takes referral fee per policy. Reduces the biggest financial risk in the event industry — cancellations — while generating a new revenue stream with zero marginal cost.

16 — Technical additions · from competitive analysis
8 technical specs added in v7.0
Source: 2026 competitive market analysis against RainFocus Nexus, Cvent, Bizzabo, and enterprise SaaS standards. Each addition is sequenced by priority: build before launch, start immediately, or design now and build in Phase 2.

Build before launch (2–6 weeks each)

FeatureEffortWhy nowTechnical approach
Public REST API + webhook system 2–4 weeks Everything else builds on it. QuickBooks, Salesforce, Google Calendar, and Zapier connectors all become 1–2 day builds once the API exists. Without it every integration is bespoke forever. Supabase already exposes REST and GraphQL on all tables — wrap with API key management (api_keys table: tenant_id, key_hash, scopes[], created_at, last_used_at), rate limiting middleware (Upstash Redis), and versioned route prefix /api/v1/. Webhook delivery via Svix — add webhook_endpoints table per tenant, emit events on: booking.confirmed, commission.settled, review.submitted, event.closed, invoice.paid. Public documentation via Swagger/OpenAPI auto-generated from route handlers.
PWA offline mode + "Save for event day" button 3–4 weeks On event day, the venue WiFi fails, the loading dock has no signal, the kitchen is a dead zone. BEO, run-of-show, guest list, vendor contacts, floor plan, and equipment list must be accessible without internet. This is a safety net for the most important day. A single prominent button makes this explicit and user-controlled — no settings to find, no setup required. The button: "Save for event day" appears on every event detail page and in the Cue chip suggestion panel when an event is within 48 hours. One tap. No confirmation dialog needed — it is non-destructive.

What gets saved (read-only offline bundle):
  • Run-of-show (full timeline, times, responsible party per item)
  • BEO (complete — courses, quantities, dietary flags, service notes)
  • Guest list (name, dietary flag, table/seat — no payment data)
  • Vendor contact sheet (name, phone number, role — phone only, not email)
  • Floor plan SVG (current layout, table labels)
  • Equipment checklist (auto-generated from BEO menu)
  • Event summary card (venue address, start/end times, guest count, Plnr contact)
What never goes offline (server-authoritative only): commission ledger, payment records, booking financials, contract documents. These must not be editable without connectivity to prevent conflicting records.

Technical implementation: Next.js service worker via next-pwa. On button tap, dispatch a CACHE_EVENT_BUNDLE message to the service worker with the event ID. Worker fetches all bundle endpoints, writes responses to a named Cache Storage bucket: evntcue-event-{eventId}. Subsequent loads of those pages are served from cache regardless of connectivity. Cache includes a timestamp so users know when it was last synced.

Auto-trigger (smart default): Service worker monitors event dates. When an event is within 48 hours and the user opens any page in that event, automatically begin background caching without requiring the button tap. Button changes to "Saved — tap to refresh" with the sync timestamp.

Mutation queue (on-site actions): Write actions taken while offline — guest check-in, course marked served, vendor arrival noted, run-of-show item completed — are stored in IndexedDB as a mutation queue. Each entry: {eventId, action, payload, timestamp, synced: false}. On connectivity restore, queue replays against Supabase in order. Conflict resolution: last-write-wins on status fields (check-in, served), flag as "needs review" on any field that changed on the server while offline.

Offline status indicator: A persistent chip in the mobile nav bar shows connectivity state. Online: teal dot + "Live". Offline: amber dot + "Offline · Saved [time]". Syncing: animated dot + "Syncing...". Users always know their current state.

PWA installation: iOS/Android "Add to Home Screen" prompt shown on first Plnr and Catr login with a clear explanation: "Install EvntCue for offline event day access." Once installed, runs full-screen with app icon — indistinguishable from a native app on the home screen. No App Store required.
Cross-event analytics layer 2–3 weeks per portal The data is already in Postgres — it just isn't surfaced across events. Turning EvntCue from operational software into business intelligence dramatically increases perceived value and reduces churn. Planners who can see 12-month margin trends don't leave. Supabase materialized views aggregated per tenant: plnr_event_summary (avg commission per event type, margin trend, top vendors by referral revenue), venue_occupancy_summary (occupancy rate by space and month, revenue per sq ft, inquiry-to-booking conversion), catr_financial_summary (food cost % trend by category, labor % of revenue, profit per guest over time). Views refresh nightly via Supabase cron. Frontend: Recharts line + bar charts embedded in a new "Insights" tab per portal. No third-party BI tool needed at this stage.
Usage-based pricing dimension 1–2 weeks 59% of SaaS buyers prefer usage-based or hybrid pricing models. A caterer doing 3 events/month has very different economics than one doing 30. A metered tier lowers signup friction for lower-volume professionals and aligns EvntCue's revenue with customer volume. Stripe Billing metered usage. Each portal subscription plan gets a base event allowance (e.g. Catr Starter: 10 events/month included). Events above threshold: increment Stripe metered usage item on event creation. EvntCue charges a per-event overage fee (TBD, e.g. $8–15/event depending on role). Commission facilitation already works this way — use identical pattern. Add usage meter widget to portal dashboards showing events used / included this month.

Start immediately — 6–9 month program

SOC 2 Type II certification program
75%+ of Fortune 500 companies require a SOC 2 report before engaging a vendor. The $300K Dallas corporate event, any hotel group, any hospitality chain — all will have procurement processes that block a vendor without it. Enterprise expansion is gated on this. The clock only starts when evidence collection begins — every month of delay is a month longer before the first enterprise contract can close.

Engineering work (4–6 weeks)

ControlImplementation
Audit loggingLog all write operations (INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE) on financial and PII tables to an immutable audit_log table: table_name, record_id, operation, old_values (jsonb), new_values (jsonb), actor_id, ip_address, timestamp. Never deleted — archived to cold storage after 90 days.
PII encryptionField-level encryption on: user email, phone, address, payment details. Use Postgres pgcrypto with AES-256. Encryption key managed via Supabase Vault (backed by AWS KMS). Search on encrypted fields via deterministic encryption or tokenization.
SSO / SAMLSupabase Auth supports SAML 2.0 — enable for Enterprise tier. Map corporate IdPs (Okta, Azure AD, Google Workspace). Role assignment on SSO login via SAML attributes.
Data retention policyPublish: event data retained 7 years (tax / legal). User PII deleted within 30 days of account deletion request. Commission records retained indefinitely (financial). Implement deletion pipeline via Supabase edge function triggered on account delete.
Penetration testingAnnual third-party pen test. Engage firm (e.g. Cobalt, Synack) before SOC 2 audit begins. Resolve critical and high findings before audit window.
Audit tooling: Use Drata or Vanta (~$12–18K/year) to automate evidence collection, continuous control monitoring, and auditor report generation. Engage a AICPA-certified SOC 2 auditor for the Type II audit after 6 months of evidence collection. Type II report covers a minimum 6-month observation period. Budget: $25–40K all-in for Year 1.

Design now — build in Phase 2

FeatureScopeArchitectural notes
Cue v2 — agentic AI framework Phase 2 · Year 3 Cue v1 is reactive (prompt → answer). Cue v2 is proactive (goal → multi-step actions). Architecture: define a set of Cue-callable tool functions using Anthropic's tool use API: send_message(thread_id, body), update_booking_status(booking_id, status), create_contract(event_id, template_id, parties), flag_commission_anomaly(flow_id, reason), schedule_followup(event_id, delay_hours, message). Governance model: classify actions as autonomous (send notifications, flag anomalies, generate drafts) vs. human-confirmed (update financial records, send contracts, change booking status). Human-confirmed actions enter an "approval queue" in the portal with one-click approve/reject. This is the same MCP + tool use pattern RainFocus Nexus uses — the infrastructure is identical, the data EvntCue trains on (commission flows, catering margins, vendor performance) is the differentiator.
Hybrid / virtual event layer Phase 2 · Year 3 Add event_format enum(in_person, hybrid, virtual) to events table. For hybrid/virtual: add virtual_platform enum(zoom, teams, meet, custom), stream_url, virtual_capacity int, virtual_attendee_count int. Ticket tiers: add tier_format enum(in_person, virtual) to ticket_tiers. Commission ledger: add virtual_attendance_fee flow type (platform takes % of virtual ticket revenue). Zoom SDK embed for Plnr and Orgnz portals — one-click join from event page. Virtual attendee list synced from Zoom/Teams attendance report post-event into guest_checkins with method = "virtual". This unlocks corporate and conference markets — the fastest-growing segment at the highest CAGR — with 3–4 weeks of build.
Open developer platform + partner API Phase 2–3 · Year 4 Once the public API exists (Phase 1), extend it into a developer platform: versioned SDK packages (npm: @evntcue/sdk), webhooks documentation with payload schemas, a developer portal at developers.evntcue.com, sandbox environment per developer account, OAuth 2.0 for third-party app authorization, and a partner program for DMCs and large event agencies who want to white-label or extend EvntCue. This is how the platform transitions from software to infrastructure — the same progression Stripe, Twilio, and Plaid made. Each certified partner integration becomes a distribution channel. Commission structure: certified partners earn a revenue share on clients they bring onto the platform.

18 — Brand identity · v1.0
The Constellation — Direction B
Design decision: Direction B selected — deep navy with electric rose-coral accent and the constellation mark. Warmth and celebration expressed through deep drama, not lightness. The dark field makes the coral glow. The constellation mark carries meaning: five connected dots, five portals, one event. The mark is rotated ~18° clockwise from vertical so no dot sits at true north or south — this breaks any pentagram association while preserving the constellation read and giving the lead dot (Plnr, brightest) a forward-leaning 10 o'clock position.

The mark — meaning

Five dots connected by lines forming a pentagon constellation. Each dot represents one party on the platform: Catr, Venue, Vndr, Plnr, Orgnz. The lines between them are the commission flows, messages, and bookings that EvntCue makes visible. The top dot — always slightly larger and brighter — is the Plnr: the orchestrator at the center of every event. The constellation is not decorative; it is the product diagram made into a mark.

Color system

v26.1 — token bridge documented. The brand spec uses prefixed export names (--ec-ink, --ec-primary) appropriate for shipping as an npm token package. This master document uses unprefixed shorthand (--ink, --pri) for legibility inside a 6,000-line spec. Hex values are identical between the two — and were re-aligned to this table in v26.1 (the doc previously had --ink: #0E1628, now corrected to #0B1220). When porting tokens to the Next.js portals, use the --ec-* names below as the source of truth and provide a tokens.css export at build time.

2026-05-05 — surface ramp expanded. Three-step dark surface system: --ink (#050A14, deepest page bg) → --ink2 (#0B1220, card surface — the existing master plum ink) → --ink3 (#111928, raised / hover). The shorthand --ink-raised (#180F28) remains the icon-square fill — distinct from --ink3.

Typography — v26.1 added

The brand voice ("warmth and celebration through deep drama, not lightness") is carried by the typography pairing as much as the color system. The system font stack used in v26.0 and earlier — -apple-system, Segoe UI, sans-serif — was indistinct and undermined the brand statement. v26.1 commits to a deliberate pairing.
RoleFamilyTokenWhere it appearsWhy
DisplayFraunces (variable, opsz 9–144)--font-displayCover wordmark · all .sec-h headlines · proposal cover pages · pitch deck H1sEditorial serif with optical-size axis. Carries the "deep drama" of the brand without being precious. Free via Google Fonts.
BodyInter Tight (400 / 500 / 600)--fontAll paragraph text · table cells · UI labels · buttonsTight humanist sans with excellent screen rendering at small sizes. The "Tight" variant runs ~5% narrower than Inter, giving denser data tables without sacrificing legibility. Free via Google Fonts.
Loading note: Both fonts are loaded from Google Fonts via <link> tags in the document head with preconnect hints. For the Next.js portals, use next/font/google with display: 'swap' for both families and variable: true on Fraunces to avoid layout shift on slow connections. Local font files are not required at launch but should be added in Phase 2 for offline portal use.

Stacked lockupSquare social posts, app store screenshots, contexts where horizontal space is limited80px wide
Wordmark onlyWhen the mark has already been established nearby (e.g. inside the app, after the topbar appears). Never use as the primary mark without the icon present elsewhere.100px wide

Usage rules

On dark backgrounds
"Evnt" in blush rose #E8A0B0, "Cue" in lavender white #EDE8F5. Constellation outer dots in dusty rose #D4778A, lead dot triple-ring: outer blush, mid pearl, white core. Always use the plum icon square background #180F28, never a colored square.
On light backgrounds
"Evnt" in plum #0B1220, "Cue" in dusty rose #D4778A. Constellation dots in dusty rose. Icon square in plum #180F28. Tagline in #4A4060. The light background version is for printed materials, white decks, and light-mode portal headers.
Clear space
Minimum clear space around any logo variation: equal to the height of the "E" in the wordmark. Never place competing design elements, text, or illustrations within this zone. For the icon-only mark, clear space equals the icon's border radius on all sides.
What never to do
Never recolor the constellation dots to any color other than rose/coral/blush. Never rotate the mark. Never use a colored (non-navy, non-white) background for the icon square. Never stretch or scale x/y independently. Never place the wordmark without the icon in primary brand contexts.

Tagline

"Your event. On cue." — unchanged. Set in regular weight, sentence case. Never bold, never all-caps. On dark backgrounds: #3A5278. On light backgrounds: #4A6090. Minimum size: 10px. The tagline is optional in small applications (icon-only, pill) but required on the full horizontal lockup.

The Cue AI chip

The "Ask Cue" chip that appears in every portal topbar uses a miniaturized constellation mark (8–10px) in rose, followed by "Ask Cue" in coral weight-500 text, on a warm-white tint background with a blush border. This chip is standardized across all five portals — identical placement (top-right app bar), identical design. It is the one consistent Cue entry point regardless of which portal the user is in.

Document version where brand applied

Brand Direction B (The Constellation) applied to this master document in v8.0. The pitch deck, sales deck, and all portal prototypes should be updated to match these tokens in their next revision cycle. The CSS token table above is the authoritative reference for all future portal builds.
19 — Pricing & tiers
Five portals. Eight plans. The most competitive fees in the industry.
Pricing philosophy: Gate on scale and collaboration, not on core functionality. Every portal has a free tier that delivers genuine value — enough for a professional to trust the platform before paying. Paid tiers unlock volume, collaboration, and advanced tooling.

Fee philosophy: EvntCue charges a 2.5% total platform fee on every transaction — structured as 1% payment processing + 1.5% platform facilitation. This is a deliberate market position: HoneyBook charges 3% for processing alone with no marketplace, no commission intelligence, and no AI. Eventbrite charges 10–14%. Airbnb charges 9–15%. EvntCue delivers more and charges less — by design. At launch, this is how we make every competitor's switching cost feel irrelevant.

Orgnz portal

Orgnz pricing philosophy: Three tiers built around how people actually plan events. Free is a discovery and trust tool — enough to see the platform's value, not enough to plan a real event without paying. Pay-per-event ($19) is for the occasional planner who uses EvntCue once or twice a year and should not be locked into a monthly subscription. Celebrate ($39/mo) is for the active planner — corporate coordinators, serial entertainers, anyone running more than two events a year. Cue AI is a paid feature at all tiers — it generates real API costs and delivers real value. Vendor contact information is never displayed — all communication flows through EvntCue until a booking is confirmed.

Pay-per-event conversion math

The $19 event fee is the primary conversion gate. It fires when an Orgnz clicks "Create Event" after exhausting their one free event. On a $5,000 birthday party, $19 is 0.38% of total spend. The $19 event fee is never the reason someone doesn't plan their event.

Celebrate break-even: 3 events per month. An Orgnz purchasing 3 pay-per-events at $19 spends $57 — more than Celebrate at $39/mo. Cue AI credit system — all portals

Cue is powered by the Anthropic API. Every message carries a real cost. The credit system ensures EvntCue never subsidizes heavy AI usage from free-tier users on low-revenue events. Credits are per-event for Orgnz and Plnr, per-month for Vndr, Catr, and Venue. A progress bar ("14 of 20 Cue messages used") is always visible. When a user approaches their limit, Cue proactively summarizes the conversation and suggests what to ask next to make remaining messages count. The add-on is one tap from the limit warning.

Revenue model — 100 active users

Projected MRR at 100 active users (representative mix): 20 Plnr Pro ($1,580) + 15 Venue Professional ($2,235) + 15 Catr Professional ($1,335) + 20 Vndr Professional ($980) + 20 Orgnz Celebrate ($780) + 15 Orgnz Pay-per-event (est. 2 events/mo avg = $570) = $7,480/mo subscription + event fee MRR + ~$5,000/mo platform fees (est. $200K GMV × 2.5%) + ~$3,200/mo booking commissions (est. $80K Vndr GMV at blended ~4%) + ~$400/mo Cue add-on revenue (est. 40 add-on purchases/mo) = ~$16,080/mo total · ~$193K ARR. The Cue credit system converts AI cost from a margin risk into a revenue stream. The pay-per-event tier captures occasional planners who would never subscribe monthly. Platform MRR is now diversified across four streams: subscriptions, event fees, transaction fees, and Cue add-ons.

49 — Contact visibility & marketplace leakage protection
How EvntCue prevents browse-and-bail — the architecture that protects booking revenue
Every open marketplace faces the same risk: a user browses vendor profiles, finds someone they like, then contacts them directly and transacts off-platform. EvntCue closes this loop at the architectural level — not through policy alone, but through data model decisions that make going around the platform more work than using it.
The core rule: Vendor contact information — phone number, email address, personal website, and social handles — is never displayed to any user on the EvntCue platform at any tier. The only available action on a vendor profile is "Inquire via EvntCue" or "Book via EvntCue." All communication happens inside the platform until a booking deposit is confirmed. Post-confirmation, the vendor's day-of mobile number appears in the final packet for coordination purposes only.

Three-layer leakage protection

Layer 1 — Contact data never renders
Vendor phone, email, website, and social handles are stored in the tenants table but the contact_visibility flag defaults to platform_only. The application layer never renders these fields on public profiles. Even if a developer queries the API directly, the RLS policies restrict contact field exposure to the owning tenant and admin only. There is no way to surface contact info through the platform UI.
Layer 2 — Cue message limits
Free Orgnzs get 5 Cue messages per event — enough to orient, not enough to complete a full vendor selection process. When they hit the limit, the conversion prompt fires: "Pay $19 to continue planning this event." The marketplace is the hook. The message limit is the gate. Orgnzs who are serious about planning will pay $19. The ones who were just browsing were never going to book anyway.
Layer 3 — Vendor Terms of Service
Vendors agree at onboarding that soliciting or accepting off-platform payment for bookings originating from EvntCue inquiries is a Terms of Service violation. First offense: warning. Second offense: 30-day booking suspension. Third offense: account terminated. The vendors who matter — those doing $50K+ annually through the platform — will not jeopardize that relationship for one off-platform transaction.

contact_visibility field — DB enforcement

StateValueWhat is visibleWhen it applies
Defaultplatform_onlyPortfolio, bio, service packages, ratings, availability, style tags. No phone, email, website, or social.All vendor profiles at all times for all browsing users.
Post-bookingpost_bookingDay-of mobile number only — surfaced in the final packet for the specific Orgnz and Plnr on that confirmed booking.Automatically unlocked per booking when deposit clears. Scoped to the specific event — does not expose contact to the Orgnz's account globally.
Adminadmin_visibleAll contact fields visible for support and dispute resolution.Admin portal only. Never accessible via Orgnz, Plnr, Vndr, Catr, or Venue portal.

What vendors get in return

The contact restriction is the trade for discovery. Vendors accept it because EvntCue delivers something no directory or listing service can — a pre-qualified Orgnz who has set a real budget, confirmed an event date, and is actively in booking mode with a credit card attached to the platform. That is not a cold lead. That is a warm prospect. The referral commission slider (§32) amplifies this further: a vendor offering a 10–15% referral rate to Plnrs is paying for warm introductions from professionals who trust them. That is worth more than any directory listing fee.
The honest reality: You will never stop 100% of leakage. Some vendors and Orgnzs will find each other and transact offline. That is true of every marketplace — Airbnb, OpenTable, and Uber all face it. What you can do is make EvntCue so frictionless, so trustworthy, and so valuable — contracts, escrow, commission intelligence, Cue, the final packet — that going around it feels riskier and more work than using it. Build the platform vendors depend on and the leakage problem largely solves itself.

Subscription activation model — locked v26.7

PhaseStateTrigger
Phase 1 — Free profileNo card on file. Full Starter feature access. No monthly charge.From signup until first confirmed booking clears escrow.
Phase 2 — 60-day graceSubscription model presented in dashboard. User chooses tier. Card collected but not charged.Day 1 = first booking clears. Day 60 = subscription activates.
Phase 3 — Active subscriptionCharged at chosen tier. Standard renewal cycle.Day 60+. User can downgrade to Starter (free) at any time, but Starter is feature-limited per the existing tier table.
Rationale. The platform earns trust before it asks for money. A venue manager who has booked through EvntCue knows the platform works; they can decide whether the Pro tier is worth it from a position of evidence, not hope. This is the inverse of Tripleseat ($250–$500/mo subscription required before any value delivered) and The Knot Pro ($300+/mo subscription, leads not guaranteed). Acquisition friction at zero; activation gated by demonstrated value.

Pro tier pricing — open decision

The original $149/mo · $129/mo annual was set against a feature bundle that has since grown. v1 Pro now includes: CRM, proposals/BEO, scheduler, deposit schedules, client communication portal, preferred vendor directory, earnings/ledger reporting, COI alerts, ticketed events, multi-location tools. Comparable products: HoneyBook $39–$129/mo (CRM + proposals only, no marketplace demand); Tripleseat $250–$500/mo (full venue ops, per-seat pricing). Recommended Pro v2 pricing: $199/mo · $169/mo annual. Lock pending decision; should be set before public launch. Enterprise stays custom.

Acquisition surface rule — locked v26.7

Pricing numbers do not appear on landing pages or onboarding flows. The free-until-first-booking phrasing is the only commercial language acquisition surfaces are allowed to carry. Pricing is introduced in-product, in the dashboard, at the moment subscription becomes relevant. This rule prevents the landing-page-as-pricing-page failure mode (decision-makers bouncing on dollar figures before they understand value).
25 — Orgnz portal
What the Orgnz sees and does when a Plnr is assigned
When a Plnr is hired, the Orgnz's relationship with the platform changes fundamentally. Vendor decisions become the Plnr's domain — that is precisely why the Orgnz hired them. The Orgnz portal shifts from a decision engine to an experience layer. Four distinct zones replace the full planning dashboard.
Entry point: An Orgnz reaches this state via the Plnr recommendation gate (§42). After budget is set, Cue evaluates complexity and either offers to manage bookings directly or suggests matching with a Plnr. If a Plnr is hired, the Orgnz dashboard switches to the four-zone experience documented here. If the Orgnz declines, Cue runs in decision-engine mode instead.
Core principle: The Orgnz hired a Plnr so they don't have to make vendor decisions. The platform respects that contract. Vendor browsing, quote comparison, and booking mechanics are hidden from the Orgnz view when a Plnr is active. The Orgnz's job is to contribute the three things only they can provide — aesthetic vision, guest data, and budget authority — and to feel informed and celebrated throughout.

Zone 1 — Planning progress tracker (read-only)

The most important element in the Orgnz view. Answers the question every Orgnz has constantly: "What has my Plnr actually done?" Each vendor category has a status bar and a plain-English label. The Orgnz sees results — never the underlying workflow, quotes, or deliberation.
StatusLabel shown to OrgnzBar stateNotes
Not startedNot yet startedEmptyPlnr hasn't opened this category yet
SearchingYour Plnr is finding options25% animated pulsePlnr has opened search but no quotes yet
Quotes inOptions are being reviewed60% amberAt least one inquiry sent, awaiting response or deliberating
Decision pendingFinal selection in progress80% amberPlnr has a preferred vendor, completing due diligence
ConfirmedConfirmed — [Vendor name]100% greenBooking confirmed, deposit collected
The vendor name is revealed only when confirmed — never before. The Orgnz never sees who was considered and rejected. This protects the Plnr's professional judgment and prevents Orgnz interference in the negotiation process.

Zone 2 — The three things the Orgnz owns

Mood board
Every image the Orgnz pins is data the Plnr uses to brief vendors and the vendor suggestion engine uses for style matching. The Orgnz isn't decorating — they're communicating. Each image narrows what "my vision" means from abstract to concrete.
Guest list
Only the Orgnz knows who's coming. RSVP tracking, headcount confirmation, and dietary flags are Orgnz-entered data the Plnr and Catr genuinely need. This isn't busywork — an unconfirmed headcount blocks BEO finalization. The Orgnz's guest list is load-bearing.
Budget approval
When the Plnr proposes a vendor booking above a set threshold (configurable, default $500), the Orgnz receives an approval request with the vendor name, what they provide, and the cost. One tap to approve or send back. The Orgnz never loses financial veto power — ever.

Zone 3 — Cue in companion mode

Without a Plnr, Cue is a decision engine — it surfaces vendor options and helps the Orgnz choose. With a Plnr assigned, Cue shifts role entirely. It becomes a knowledge companion: answering "what does that mean?", "is that a good price?", "what's a BEO?", "what flowers are in season in April?" — without surfacing operational decisions or vendor options that belong to the Plnr.
Without Plnr — decision engine
"Here are three florists that match your style and budget. Bloom & Co has the best reviews. Want me to send them an inquiry?"
With Plnr — knowledge companion
"Peonies and garden roses are both in season in April — beautiful choice. Your Plnr will know exactly which local florists work with them. Anything else you're curious about?"
The system prompt injected to Cue for Orgnz sessions checks events.plnr_tenant_id. If populated, Cue receives explicit instruction: do not recommend vendors, do not surface booking options, do not reference the planning workflow. Be curious, warm, and educational. If the Orgnz asks a planning question that belongs to the Plnr, Cue says "that's a great one for your Plnr — want me to send them a note?"

Zone 4 — Milestone notifications

Every confirmed booking triggers a milestone notification to the Orgnz. The copy is written to feel like a gift, not a system event. The Orgnz's emotional experience of planning is made of these moments.
EventNotification copyChannel
Venue confirmed"Your venue is locked in. [Venue name] is yours on [date]."Push + email
Photographer confirmed"Your photographer is confirmed. [Name] will be there to capture everything."Push + email
Catr confirmed"Your caterer is set. [Name] is handling the food and it's going to be incredible."Push + email
All vendors confirmed"Everything is confirmed. Your Plnr has locked in every vendor. You're ready."Push + email + in-app banner
Event finalized"Your event is finalized. The full plan is in your inbox and saved to your device."Push + email + SMS if enabled
Budget approval request"Your Plnr recommends [Vendor] for [category] — [amount]. Tap to approve or ask a question."Push + email — requires response
Notification copy is templated but personalized with vendor names, event date, and the Orgnz's first name. Generic system messages ("booking_id_4892 status updated") never appear in the Orgnz experience. Every touchpoint is human.
26 — Event intelligence
Event type templates, system-generated timelines, and vendor suggestion engine
When a Orgnz or Plnr creates a new event, the platform doesn't present a blank canvas. It presents a smart starting point — a pre-built timeline, a vendor checklist, and a ranked vendor shortlist — all derived from the event type selected. The system knows what a wedding needs. It knows what a corporate gala needs. It knows what a quinceañera needs. The human's job is to edit, not to start from scratch.

Event type library — system templates
