Destination eventVenue (remote), Catr, Photography & Media, Transportation & Logistics (travel coordinator required), Guest Experience (hotel room block, welcome gifts), all other categories per event type9–18 monthsTimeline, travel logistics sheet, hotel room block tracker, passport/travel document reminders. Cue geographic proximity weighting disabled — switches to destination-mode matching (vendor type expertise + travel willingness flags). See vendor matching note below.
CustomOrgnz or Plnr selects manuallyUser-definedBlank timeline, empty checklist

System-generated timeline — how it works

When an event type and date are selected, Cue generates a backward-planned timeline working from the event date. Each milestone is a specific task with an owner (Orgnz, Plnr, or vendor-dependent), a due date, and a status. The timeline is immediately editable by both Orgnz and Plnr. Cue's version is the starting point, not the final word.
Phase 1 — Lock the anchors
Venue confirmation first. Nothing else can be booked until venue is confirmed — date, capacity, and location determine everything downstream. Timeline shows this as a hard gate with visual blocking on all other categories.
Phase 2 — Book the high-demand vendors
Photographer, band/DJ, and specialty vendors with limited availability book out furthest. Cue surfaces availability warnings: "Top-rated photographers in your area book 14 months out. This is a priority." Due dates auto-calculated from event date.
Phase 3 — Complete the roster
Florist, catering finalization, hair & makeup, transportation. Tighter windows, more flexibility on replacements. Timeline shows which vendors can wait vs. which have urgency flags.
Phase 4 — Details and confirmations
Menu finalization, guest list lock, final headcount to Catr, BEO approval, run-of-show review, final payments, day-of logistics.
Phase 5 — Event week
Delivery confirmations, setup coordination, vendor arrival windows, offline bundle download reminder, final run-of-show distribution to all parties.
Post-event
Payment settlement, review requests, ROI report generation, archive. Commission flows finalized and distributed. Vndr withdrawal tracking updated.

Vendor suggestion engine — how Cue ranks and surfaces matches

For each vendor category on a new event, Cue runs a matching pass against the full Vndr and Catr database. The ranking algorithm weights six factors, each admin-configurable by weight.
FactorDefault weightData source
Availability on event dateHard gate — must passVndr calendar / booking records
Style match to mood board30%Cue image analysis of mood board tags vs. Vndr portfolio tags
Budget fit25%Vndr package pricing vs. event budget line item allocation
Past performance score20%Cue composite score from reviews, on-time rate, budget accuracy
Geographic proximity15%Venue location vs. Vndr service area
Tier preference10%Orgnz/Plnr-set preference signal (luxury, budget, mid-market)
Destination event — vendor matching mode switch: When event type is “Destination event,” Cue disables the geographic proximity factor (normally 15% weight) and replaces it with two destination-specific signals: (1) vendor’s travel_willing profile flag (hard gate — must pass) and (2) vendor’s past destination event count (replaces proximity in the ranking weight). Admin-configurable. All other matching factors remain unchanged.

Overlap detection — Cue warns before double-booking

The vendor ecosystem research (§40) identified 7 structural overlap zones where clients commonly pay twice for the same function. Cue monitors active bookings against these zones and surfaces a warning before a second booking is confirmed that duplicates a covered need.
Overlap zoneWhat Cue checksWarning shown
Audio double-chargeDJ booked + AV company also quoting sound equipment“Your DJ includes sound equipment. Confirm whether the AV company quote covers lighting only — you may not need both.”
Tables & chairs triple overlapVenue includes tables/chairs + Catr quotes same + rental company also quoted“Your venue includes tables and chairs for [N] guests. The Catr and rental quotes may duplicate this. Confirm what’s actually needed.”
Florals vs. décorFlorist booked + Décor company also quoting centerpieces“Your florist and decor vendor both appear to cover centerpieces. Confirm scope with each before both deposits are collected.”
Venue valet vs. external valetVenue includes valet in contract + Transportation vendor also quotes valet“Your venue contract includes valet service. The transportation vendor quote may duplicate this.”
Venue coordinator vs. PlnrVenue includes day-of coordinator + Plnr also hiredNo warning — these are genuinely different roles. Cue adds an educational note: “Venue coordinators manage the space. Your Plnr manages the full event.”
Photographer vs. content creatorBoth booked for same eventNo warning — legitimately different deliverables. Cue confirms scope: “Confirm whether your photographer is also delivering social content or if the content creator covers that.”
Catr portal vs. Food & Beverage VndrA Catr portal booking exists + a Food & Beverage Vndr also booked for same event“You have a Catr booking and a separate F&B vendor booking for this event. Confirm there is no scope overlap in what each is serving.”

Affiliate vendor links — the marketplace extension

Not every vendor category has an EvntCue-registered Vndr. For categories where the platform's marketplace is thin (wedding attire, party supplies, custom décor, specialty rentals), Cue surfaces affiliate product links alongside registered vendors. These are clearly distinguished in the UI.
When affiliate links appear
When fewer than 3 registered Vndrs match a category in the event's geographic area. Affiliate links supplement, never replace, registered vendors. If 3+ registered matches exist, no affiliate links are shown. Threshold is admin-configurable.
Affiliate categories at launch
Wedding attire (tuxedo rentals, bridal accessories), party décor (balloon kits, table supplies), specialty rentals (photo booths, candy bars, lawn games), invitations & stationery, favors & gifts, custom cake toppers.
Revenue model
Standard affiliate commission (typically 5–15% of purchase price) tracked via UTM parameters and affiliate network integration (Amazon Associates, ShareASale, or direct brand partnerships). Revenue logged separately from platform subscription and transaction fee revenue.
UI treatment
Affiliate results carry a "Shop online" badge, clearly distinct from "Book on EvntCue" for registered vendors. Clicking opens affiliate link in new tab. No inquiry or booking flow — it's a shopping handoff. Orgnz and Plnr can both see and share affiliate suggestions.

Vendor booking status bar — the full flow

Every vendor category on the event dashboard has a visual status bar that tracks the complete booking lifecycle. Both the Plnr dashboard (full detail) and the Orgnz dashboard (result-only) use the same underlying state — different views, same data.
StepActionStatus bar stateWho sees full detail
1Event created, category auto-populated from templateEmpty — "Not started"Plnr + Orgnz
2Plnr/Orgnz opens vendor suggestions — Cue returns ranked matches25% — "Finding options"Plnr only (Orgnz sees "Your Plnr is finding options")
3Orgnz/Plnr selects up to 3 vendors to shop — sends inquiry40% — "Inquiries sent"Plnr only
4Vendor(s) respond with pricing and availability60% — "Quotes received"Plnr only
5Plnr/Orgnz selects winning vendor — sends acceptance75% — "Contract accepted"Plnr only
6Deposit collected via Stripe/Trustap — booking confirmed100% — "Confirmed: [Vendor]"Plnr + Orgnz (vendor name revealed)
7Timeline auto-updates — booking slot shows confirmed stateGreen chip on timeline itemPlnr + Orgnz
8Orgnz receives milestone notification — "Your photographer is confirmed"N/AOrgnz only
The status bar is the heartbeat of the Orgnz experience. Watching categories move from empty to green over weeks and months is the visual proof that the event is coming together. Each green bar is a small celebration before the big one.
27 — Venue gate
Venue confirmation required before booking — with a bypass for private venues
Nothing in EvntCue can be booked until a venue is confirmed. This is a hard architectural rule, not a soft recommendation. Date, capacity, and location are the three inputs every other vendor needs to confirm availability and scope their services. Without them, vendor bookings are provisional at best and waste everyone's time at worst.
The gate: All vendor category cards on a new event are visible but locked — "Venue must be confirmed before booking vendors." The vendor suggestion engine runs in preview mode: Cue surfaces matches and the Orgnz/Plnr can browse and save favorites, but inquiry buttons are disabled. The moment venue is confirmed, all categories unlock simultaneously.

Venue confirmation — two paths

Path A — Book via EvntCue Venue portal
Orgnz or Plnr finds a venue in the EvntCue marketplace. Sends inquiry. Venue responds with contract. Deposit collected via Trustap. Venue status updates to "Confirmed" automatically when deposit clears. All other vendor categories unlock. Event date is now locked — changing the date triggers a re-confirmation prompt for all confirmed vendors.
Path B — Private venue bypass
Orgnz selects "I have my own venue" — examples: backyard, family property, community space, company office. Enters venue details manually: address, name (optional), indoor/outdoor, max capacity, parking notes. One-tap confirmation: "Confirm this as my venue." Venue status flips to "Confirmed — Private venue." All other vendor categories unlock identically to Path A.

Private venue bypass — what it does and doesn't unlock

FeatureEvntCue venue bookingPrivate venue bypass
Vendor category unlockYes — on deposit confirmationYes — on manual confirmation
Venue appears on run-of-showYes — from booking recordYes — from manual entry
Floor planYes — venue uploads via Venue portalOrgnz uploads manually (PDF, image)
BEO venue sectionAuto-populated from bookingManually entered by Orgnz or Plnr
Venue contact on emergency sheetAuto-populatedOrgnz enters manually (optional)
Platform venue commissionApplies (2.5% on booking amount)Does not apply — no transaction

Pre-gate vendor browsing — "shopping mode"

Before venue is confirmed, Orgnzs and Plnrs can browse the full vendor marketplace in shopping mode. Cue runs the suggestion engine in preview — returning ranked matches based on event type, approximate location, and budget range. The Orgnz or Plnr can save vendors to a shortlist, share vendor profiles externally, and even request a quote (which is queued but not sent until venue is confirmed).
The shopping mode UI makes the gate visible but not frustrating: a soft banner reads "Browsing as guest — confirm your venue to start booking." Saved vendors and queued inquiries persist. The moment venue confirms, all queued inquiries fire simultaneously and the Plnr/Orgnz is notified: "Your venue is confirmed. We've sent inquiries to your 4 shortlisted vendors."

Changing venue after confirmation

If a venue is replaced after confirmation (including the force majeure Scenario 3 from §24), all confirmed vendor bookings receive a notification: "The venue for [event name] has changed to [new venue / TBD]. Please confirm your availability for the updated location." Vendors have 48 hours to re-confirm or withdraw. The Plnr receives a real-time dashboard of re-confirmation status per vendor.
21 — Catr portal
Hard definition, certification gates, and listing rules
Catr is defined as any person or business providing food or beverage product consumed at the event. This is a hard boundary — not a soft category. A full-service caterer, food truck, private chef, dessert bar, bartender, beverage service, or specialty station all route through the Catr portal. If food or drink touches the event, it is Catr. There are no exceptions.
Listing gate — hard requirement: A Catr account can be created and configured at any time, but the profile does not appear in marketplace search results and cannot accept bookings until all required certifications are uploaded and marked valid. This is not a soft nudge — it is a system gate enforced at the database level via a listing_active boolean that only flips true when all cert records pass validation.

Required certifications — all three mandatory before listing activates

General liability insurance
Minimum $1M per occurrence. Certificate of Insurance (COI) uploaded as PDF. Expiry tracked — Catr notified 30 days before expiry, listing suspended on expiry date if not renewed.
Food handler certification
ServSafe, state health department cert, or equivalent. Applies to all food preparation and service staff. At least one cert for the account holder required. Expiry tracked identically to COI.
TABC certification
Required for any Catr that serves, pours, or handles alcohol. Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission certification. If a Catr account is food-only with no alcohol service, this field is marked N/A and the listing gate opens without it. Catr self-declares scope at onboarding.

Platform verification model

EvntCue does not independently verify certifications. The platform stores documents, tracks expiry dates, and surfaces cert status to Orgnzs and Plnrs at booking time. Liability for valid and current certifications rests entirely with the Catr. This is the same model used by Vndr Professional COI upload. A "Verified docs on file" badge appears on the Catr profile card in marketplace search — it means documents were uploaded, not that EvntCue audited them. This distinction should be documented in the Catr onboarding flow and Terms of Service.

Listing suspension rules

TriggerActionNotification
Cert expiry — 30 days outWarning banner on Catr dashboardEmail + in-app alert
Cert expiry — 7 days outSecond warning, urgent flagEmail daily
Cert expiredlisting_active = false — removed from searchEmail + SMS if enabled
Cert renewed and uploadedlisting_active = true — restored automaticallyConfirmation email
Active booking exists at suspensionListing suspended but existing confirmed bookings are not cancelled — Orgnz and Plnr are notified of cert expiryOrgnz + Plnr alert

Plnr certification uploads — trust badge model

Plnrs can upload professional credentials to their marketplace profile. Unlike Catr certs, these are optional trust signals — not listing gates. A Plnr without credentials still has full platform access. When credentials are present, a verified badge appears on their public profile card and marketplace listing. The badge is a meaningful signal to Orgnzs choosing between Plnrs — and a clear incentive for professional Plnrs to complete their profile.
Key distinction from Catr certs: Catr certs are a hard gate — no upload, no listing. Plnr certs are a trust amplifier — no upload means no badge, but the Plnr still operates normally. The badge drives conversion from Orgnzs browsing the Plnr marketplace. Plnrs who complete cert upload should rank higher in Cue's Plnr marketplace suggestions (admin-configurable weight, default: +10% ranking boost per verified cert, capped at 2 certs = +20% max).

Accepted credential types

CredentialIssuing bodyHas expiry?Notes
WPICCWeddings Beautiful / WPICYes — annual renewalWedding & Event Planning Certificate. North America's oldest designation.
CWPLovegevity's Wedding Planning InstituteYesCertified Wedding Planner. Widely recognized in social event space.
CSEPISES (International Live Events Association)Yes — biennial renewalCertified Special Events Professional. Gold standard for full-service event professionals.
CMPEvents Industry CouncilYes — 5-year cycleCertified Meeting Professional. Strongest for corporate/conference Plnrs.
State event licenseVaries by stateYes — annualTexas has no state licensing requirement, but other states do. Accepted if verifiable.
Relevant degreeAccredited institutionNo expiryHospitality management, event management, tourism. Transcript or diploma accepted. Displayed as "Hospitality degree — [Institution]."
Portfolio referenceSelf-submittedNoNot a certification — listed separately on profile as "Featured events." Does not trigger a badge. Capped at 6 events with images and brief description.

Upload flow — full spec

Step 1 — Access
In the Plnr portal under Profile → Credentials. "Add credential" button. Available on both Plnr Solo (free) and Plnr Pro tiers — the badge motivates free-tier Plnrs to complete their profile and signals quality to Orgnzs regardless of subscription level.
Step 2 — Credential form
Select credential type from dropdown (populated from the accepted types table). Enter issuing body name (pre-filled if recognized type). Enter issue date (required). Enter expiry date (required if credential has expiry — field shows "No expiry" toggle for degree types). Upload document: PDF, JPG, or PNG, max 10MB.
Step 3 — Storage & activation
File uploads to Supabase Storage at plnr-certs/{plnr_tenant_id}/{uuid}.{ext}. Row written to plnr_certifications table with status active. Badge appears on public profile within 60 seconds of upload confirmation. No admin approval required — EvntCue stores the document and tracks expiry; verification responsibility rests with the Plnr per ToS.

Badge display — public profile card

Marketplace listing card
Up to 2 credential badges displayed inline below the Plnr name. Format: "✓ CSEP" and "✓ CMP" — small green-tinted chips. If more than 2 active credentials exist, the top 2 by prestige rank (CSEP > CMP > WPICC > CWP > other) are displayed, with a "+N more" indicator linking to the full profile.
Full Plnr profile page
All active credentials listed in a "Credentials" section with name, issuing body, and issue year. Expiry year shown if applicable. Document itself is never public — only the metadata. "Verified docs on file" sub-label matches the Catr trust model for visual consistency across the platform.
22 — Guest management
MVP scope — functional and shippable, with a defined growth path
EvntCue's guest management module is scoped to ship a real, usable product without scope creep into territory that dedicated platforms like Zola or The Knot own. The MVP is functional — it does everything an event needs to execute successfully — with a defined growth path for features that make sense after the core platform is live and validated.
The primary functional dependency: Dietary flags entered in guest management cascade automatically to the Catr's BEO. The Catr sees counts and flags — not guest names. "6 vegan, 2 severe nut allergy, 1 kosher" appears in the BEO kitchen summary without exposing individual guest identity to the catering company. This cascade is the primary reason guest management exists in the platform at all.

MVP — what ships at launch

Guest list
Name, email (optional), RSVP status (invited / confirmed / declined / pending), plus-one (yes/no + name), headcount totals shown live. Bulk import via CSV (name + email columns minimum). Manual add one at a time. Edit and delete individual guests.
RSVP collection
Shareable RSVP link generated per event — a simple public page (no login required) where guests enter their name, confirm attendance, and select dietary flags. Responses appear in the guest list immediately. Orgnz sets an RSVP deadline; headcount is locked after deadline unless manually overridden.
Dietary & accessibility flags
Standard options: vegan, vegetarian, gluten-free, nut allergy (mild/severe), kosher, halal, dairy-free, other (free text). Accessibility: mobility, hearing, visual. Flags cascade to BEO automatically as counts (never names). Catr sees "6 vegan, 2 nut allergy (severe)" — not which guest has which flag.
Headcount cascade
Confirmed headcount drives catering minimums, venue capacity checks, and vendor scope estimates throughout the event record. Updates automatically as RSVPs change. Venue sees live headcount against their capacity. Catr BEO auto-updates guest count field.
Basic table assignment
Text-based only at launch: create named tables with seat capacity, drag guests into tables. No visual seating map — that's §15 floor plan. This is enough to hand a venue a printed seating chart. Output: printable seating list sorted by table, available in the final packet.
Guest list export
CSV export of full guest list with RSVP status, dietary flags, table assignment, and plus-one. PDF export of seating chart (same Puppeteer pipeline as mood board). Both available on demand and included in the final packet for Orgnz and Plnr.

DB schema — guests table (MVP)

ColumnTypeDescription
iduuid PKAuto-generated
event_iduuid FK → eventsEvent this guest belongs to
nametextGuest display name
emailtext nullableOptional — used for RSVP link delivery
rsvp_statusenum(invited|confirmed|declined|pending)Default: pending
plus_onebooleanWhether guest is bringing a plus-one
plus_one_nametext nullablePlus-one name if provided
dietary_flagstext[] (array)Selected from controlled list: vegan, vegetarian, gluten_free, nut_allergy_mild, nut_allergy_severe, kosher, halal, dairy_free, other
dietary_notestext nullableFree text for "other" dietary flag or additional context
accessibility_flagstext[] nullablemobility, hearing, visual
table_iduuid nullable FK → event_tablesNull until assigned
rsvp_tokenuuid uniqueUsed in shareable RSVP link — guests don't need an account
rsvp_responded_attimestamptz nullableWhen guest submitted their RSVP response
created_attimestamptzAuto now()

What's out of scope at MVP — and why

Wedding website hosting
Not EvntCue's product. Orgnzs link externally to The Knot, Zola, or their own site. EvntCue's RSVP page is a lightweight collect tool, not a wedding website replacement.
Gift registry
Entirely out of scope — permanently. Orgnzs link to Amazon, Zola, or any registry externally from their event details page.
Advanced visual seat mapping
Drag-and-drop floor plans with visual table placement are the §15 floor plan feature (P1). MVP table assignment is text-based only. Visual seating is a separate module that layers on top.
Guest communication / email blasts
EvntCue does not send marketing or personal messages on behalf of Orgnzs. The RSVP link goes out manually — the Orgnz copies it and sends via their own channel. Automated reminders to guests are a V2 growth feature.
Advanced ticketing / box office
Reserved seating maps, ticket tiers, on-site scanning are a Phase 2 path — ShoWare webhook ingestion if the Venue is already a ShoWare customer (§16). EvntCue's MVP does not compete with Eventbrite or ShoWare.
Dietary meal tagging at the plate level
Matching specific dietary flags to specific guests for plated service is a V2 feature. MVP tracks counts and flags only. The Catr coordinates plate-level detail outside the platform if they require it.

Growth path — V2 guest features (post-launch validation)

FeaturePhaseWhy it waits
Automated RSVP remindersV2Requires email sender reputation management. Don't ship before RSVP link is validated as working by real users.
Guest meal ticket / place card exportV2Plate-level dietary matching tied to a specific guest — useful for plated dinners. Needs floor plan integration to be useful.
Day-of mobile check-inV2PWA QR code check-in already specced in §15 P1. Guest record links to check-in status. Real-time headcount feeds BEO on event day.
Guest messaging from OrgnzV2Orgnz sends event updates to confirmed guests via EvntCue. Requires CAN-SPAM compliance, unsubscribe handling, and email reputation groundwork.
Visual seating mapV2Tied to §15 floor plan feature. Text-based table assignment ships first; visual drag-and-drop is built on top of the same data model.
23 — Final packet
Finalization trigger, packet contents, and 48-hour offline reminder
When an event is marked Finalized by the Orgnz (or Plnr with Orgnz approval), EvntCue automatically composes and distributes a final packet to all confirmed parties. The finalization state is a deliberate one-way gate — it signals that planning is complete and execution is beginning. It can be un-done by the Orgnz, but doing so sends a notification to all parties.

Finalization trigger conditions

ConditionRequired?Notes
All vendor bookings confirmedYesNo pending or provisional bookings
Run-of-show existsYesAt least one item in timeline
Headcount confirmedYesRSVP deadline passed or Orgnz manually confirms
BEO approved by Orgnz or PlnrYesCatr BEO must be in "approved" state
Mood boardNoIncluded in packet if it exists; not a blocker
Payment schedule settledYesAll deposits collected, final payment schedule set

Final packet contents — sent to all parties

All parties receive
Event summary card (date, venue, headcount, key contacts) · Run-of-show / timeline (full) · Emergency contact list (all vendor primary contacts with mobile numbers) · Offline download prompt with PWA install CTA.
Role-specific additions
Orgnz + Plnr: Full BEO · Mood board (PDF export) · Guest list summary · Budget snapshot · Full vendor contact sheet.
Catr: BEO only · Dietary summary (counts, not names) · Kitchen timeline.
Venue: Floor plan · Setup timeline · Vendor arrival schedule.
Vndr: Their individual timeline slots · Load-in/out details · On-site contact.

Mood board export format — resolved

Decision locked: Mood board exports as a server-side PDF rendered via Puppeteer (running in a Vercel serverless function or a dedicated microservice if render time exceeds 10s). This is the correct choice for three reasons: (1) universally openable — every party receives a file that works without an EvntCue account or app installed, (2) the mood board at finalization is a snapshot in time — it represents what was planned, not what might change later, and (3) PDF is the industry standard format for BEO packets and planning documents — it fits naturally alongside the other packet contents.
Render trigger
PDF is generated once at finalization — not on demand and not in real time. If the mood board is edited after finalization, a "Mood board updated" flag appears on the event record and a re-render is queued automatically. All parties who received the original packet receive an updated PDF via email with a note: "The mood board for [Event Name] has been updated. See attached."
Render spec
Puppeteer headless Chrome renders the mood board's HTML view (same component used in-app, without interactive controls) to a letter-format PDF at 1x resolution. Images fetched from Supabase Storage signed URLs at render time. Output stored in Supabase Storage at event-packets/{event_id}/moodboard.pdf. Signed URL included in final packet distribution.
Fallback
If no mood board exists at finalization, the PDF slot in the packet is skipped silently — no error, no empty page. The finalization checklist (§23) marks mood board as "Optional — not required." If render fails (Puppeteer timeout, broken image URL), the packet sends without the mood board and admin is flagged. A retry is queued for up to 3 attempts before admin intervention.

48-hour offline download reminder

At 48 hours before the event start time, EvntCue sends an automated reminder to Orgnz, Plnr, and any on-site vendor contacts prompting them to download the offline bundle. The reminder includes a one-tap deep link that opens the app directly to the "Save for event day" flow. Push notification (PWA), email (Resend), and in-app banner are all triggered simultaneously.
The offline bundle matches the PWA spec from §16: run-of-show, BEO, guest list, vendor phone contacts, floor plan, equipment list, event summary card. Financial records are never included in the offline bundle — server-authoritative only. The 48-hour window ensures the bundle is current without being so early that material changes have not yet been made.

Timeline and run-of-show editing — collaborative model

Both Orgnz and Plnr have full write access to the timeline and run-of-show at all times, including after finalization (with a confirmation prompt). Editing rules:
ActionOrgnzPlnrNotes
Add/edit non-vendor itemsYesYesFree edit, change logged with author + timestamp
Edit timing of vendor slotYesYesVendor is notified of time change
Delete a confirmed vendor slotConfirm promptConfirm promptTriggers cancellation flow for that booking — cannot be done silently
Add new vendor slotYesYesOpens vendor search/booking flow inline
Edit after finalizationYes — with promptYes — with prompt"You are editing a finalized event. All parties will be notified." Change log entry created.
Change history is visible to both Orgnz and Plnr in a collapsible audit log on the timeline view. Each entry shows: who made the change, what changed, and when. Vendors see only their own slot history, not the full event log.
24 — Cancellation
Three scenarios — one deposit rule, two vendor paths
Cancellation on EvntCue follows a single governing financial rule and two distinct vendor-side scenarios. The platform routes notifications, triggers the correct financial flows via Trustap/Stripe Connect, generates documentation, and surfaces next actions to all parties. It does not mediate disputes — those are contractual matters between the parties.
The deposit rule — non-negotiable and platform-enforced: If an Orgnz cancels a confirmed booking, their deposit is forfeited. There are no refund tiers, no 30-day grace windows, no platform-level exceptions. The deposit exists precisely because it creates commitment — it protects vendors who have held the date, declined other work, and incurred preparation costs. If an Orgnz wants to cancel and rebook, they start fresh. This is enforced via Trustap escrow — the deposit releases to the vendor on cancellation, not back to the Orgnz.
Immutability rule: The cancellation_policy JSONB field on each booking record is written and frozen at booking time. If a vendor updates their policy after a booking is made, the original policy governs that booking. This is enforced at the database level — it prevents vendors from changing policy after collecting a deposit.

Scenario 1 — Orgnz cancels the full event

The Orgnz initiates full event cancellation. Only the Orgnz can trigger this — the Plnr cannot unilaterally cancel an event. All deposits are forfeited. Orgnz must rebook from scratch if they wish to hold a new event.
Step 1 — Confirm intent
Orgnz sees a confirmation modal listing all confirmed bookings and their deposit amounts. Explicit language: "Cancelling this event will forfeit all deposits. This cannot be undone." Orgnz must type "CANCEL" to confirm. No accidental cancellations.
Step 2 — Simultaneous notification
All confirmed vendors (Venue, Catr, all Vndrs) receive cancellation notice simultaneously via email + in-app within 60 seconds. Plnr receives separate notification. Notifications include the date, event name, and confirmation that deposits have been released to the vendor.
Step 3 — Financial resolution
All deposits transfer to vendors via Trustap escrow release — no refund to Orgnz. Commission ledger updated: pending commission flows are reversed (Plnr does not earn commission on a cancelled event). Platform fee (2.5%) retained on collected deposits per Terms of Service.
Step 4 — Documentation
Cancellation summary auto-generated: event ID, cancellation timestamp, all bookings and their deposit amounts released, commission reversals. Available to Orgnz for 12 months. Vendors receive their own confirmation with the deposit release amount.
Step 5 — Archive
Event record moves to "Cancelled" status. Run-of-show, BEO, guest list, and timeline are archived (not deleted) for 24 months. Financial records retained per compliance timeline (7 years). The Orgnz's account is not suspended — they can create a new event immediately.
Rebook path
After cancellation, Orgnz is shown a soft prompt: "Planning a future event? Start a new event and your saved vendor shortlist is ready." Previously favorited vendors are preserved in the Orgnz's saved list — not in a booking or escrow state. This reduces friction for Orgnzs who reschedule rather than abandon.

Scenario 2A — Vendor cancels: scheduling conflict (not the event's fault)

A Catr, Vndr, or Venue discovers a scheduling conflict and must withdraw from a confirmed booking. This is distinct from a vendor simply backing out — it is a good-faith availability failure. The event is not cancelled; a slot needs backfilling. The platform treats the vendor fairly while protecting the Orgnz.
Financial treatment
The vendor's deposit is returned to the Orgnz in full. This is the inverse of Scenario 1 — when the vendor is the cause of cancellation, the Orgnz is made whole on the deposit. Commission flow for this booking is fully reversed in the ledger. The vendor absorbs any platform transaction costs — they are not passed to the Orgnz.
Vendor scheduling conflict declaration
The vendor selects "Scheduling conflict" as their withdrawal reason in the platform. This triggers the favorable-to-Orgnz deposit return automatically. The declaration is logged on the vendor's account. Vendors who declare scheduling conflicts more than twice in 12 months are flagged for admin review — this prevents the "conflict" label from being used as a soft cancellation loophole.
Replacement flow
Timeline slot updates to "Needs replacement" with urgent visual flag. Cue re-runs vendor suggestion engine for that category. If cancellation is within 72 hours: Distress match panel surfaces vendors with confirmed availability. Pre-filled urgent availability request template available for Plnr/Orgnz to send immediately.
Vendor account impact
A scheduling conflict withdrawal is logged but not penalized at the first occurrence. It is visible in admin review only — not on the vendor's public profile. At 2 scheduling conflict withdrawals in 12 months, a review flag is set and the vendor is contacted by the EvntCue team before their next booking is confirmed. At 3 total withdrawals (any reason), new bookings are held pending review.

Scenario 2B — Vendor withdraws without cause (event continues)

A vendor backs out of a confirmed booking without a documented scheduling conflict — they simply choose not to fulfill the commitment. This is the worst-faith scenario and is treated accordingly.
Financial treatment
The vendor's deposit is returned to the Orgnz in full — same as a scheduling conflict. The difference is in the vendor's account standing, not the Orgnz's financial outcome. The Orgnz is always made whole when a vendor is the cause of a cancellation.
Vendor account impact
Withdrawal without cause is logged prominently on the vendor's internal record. First occurrence: warning notification from EvntCue. Second occurrence: 30-day booking hold (vendor cannot accept new bookings while hold is active). Third occurrence: account suspended pending full admin review. This is disclosed to vendors in the Terms of Service at onboarding — the consequences are known upfront.

Scenario 3 — Force majeure / venue cancellation (full cascade)

The venue becomes unavailable or a force majeure event makes the event impossible as planned. All vendor bookings are contingent on venue. Three resolution paths are offered to the Orgnz — the deposit rule is waived for force majeure per platform Terms of Service.
PathWhat happensVendor bookingsDeposits
RescheduleOrgnz selects a new date. All confirmed vendors are notified and asked to confirm availability for the new date within 72 hours. Bookings that cannot transfer are individually cancelled with deposit returned to Orgnz (force majeure exception).Paused — vendor must re-confirm within 72hrsHeld in escrow during reschedule window. Released to Orgnz if vendor cannot reschedule.
RelocateOrgnz triggers venue re-search. All other vendor bookings remain active. New venue booking flow opens inline. Once new venue confirmed, timeline and BEO update. All other vendor deposits held in escrow throughout.Remain activeVenue deposit released per venue policy (force majeure); all other escrow held
Cancel in fullFull Scenario 1 cascade — all bookings cancelled, all vendors notified. Force majeure exception applies: deposits returned to Orgnz, not forfeited. Vendor receives deposit return, not retention. Platform fee retained on processed amounts per ToS.All cancelledReturned to Orgnz (force majeure exception to deposit forfeiture rule)
Force majeure declaration: Force majeure status must be declared by the Orgnz and confirmed by admin before the deposit exception applies. Accepted triggers: documented venue closure, natural disaster, declared public emergency. A vendor scheduling conflict does not qualify as force majeure — that follows Scenario 2A. EvntCue does not adjudicate whether a situation qualifies — admin reviews and approves within 24 hours of declaration.
28 — Competitive analysis
Full marketplace comparison — what every competitor does, where they break, and what EvntCue must add
The event software market is projected to reach $16.1B in 2026. No single platform owns the full stack from Orgnz to Catr to Vndr to Venue to Plnr in one connected system. Every competitor is either a point tool (great at one thing, nothing else) or an enterprise behemoth (great at everything, inaccessible to the market EvntCue serves). The gap is real and large.

The structural gap EvntCue fills: Every competitor serves one side of the equation. HoneyBook serves the Plnr's business admin. Tripleseat serves the Venue's operations. WeddingWire serves the couple's discovery. Eventbrite serves the public ticket buyer. GigSalad serves the entertainer. No platform connects all five parties — Orgnz, Plnr, Venue, Catr, Vndr — in a single shared event record with live commission intelligence, a unified BEO, and a collaborative run-of-show. That is EvntCue's structural moat.

The two features no competitor has at all

Commission intelligence — EvntCue exclusive
No competitor tracks, calculates, discloses, or splits vendor-to-planner commissions in a structured system. HoneyBook ignores it. Planning Pod has no commission concept. WeddingWire profits from it opaquely. EvntCue makes it transparent, calculable, and distributable — and takes a 1.5% facilitation fee for doing so. Platform-level moat with no competitive analog.
Unified 5-party event record — EvntCue exclusive
Every competitor manages one side. Venue uses Tripleseat. Plnr uses Planning Pod. Catr uses a spreadsheet. Orgnz uses email. EvntCue puts all five parties on the same live event record — same BEO, same run-of-show, same timeline, same guest list — with role-appropriate views. No competitor has attempted this architecture.
