29 — P0 launch features
Five features that must ship at launch — marketplace won't function without them

29.1 — Instant quote and instant booking

Vndrs and Catrs can publish fixed service packages with instant book enabled. When instant book is on, the Orgnz or Plnr selects the package, the deposit auto-collects via Stripe, and the booking is confirmed with no inquiry/quote cycle required. The inquiry flow remains available for custom scopes — instant book is an opt-in per package, not a platform mandate.
Vndr package setup
Vndr creates named packages (e.g. "Standard coverage — 8hrs", "Premium — full day + second shooter"). Each package has a fixed price, deposit percentage, cancellation policy (frozen at booking per §24 rule), and an instant book toggle. Packages can be hidden, published, or archived.
Booking flow
Orgnz/Plnr selects package → reviews package details and cancellation terms → confirms date against real-time availability calendar (§29.2) → pays deposit → booking confirmed. Total time: under 90 seconds. Vndr receives notification and booking appears on their calendar. No back-and-forth.
DB impact
New columns on vndr_packages: instant_book_enabled boolean, deposit_pct integer, cancellation_policy jsonb (frozen at booking time per §24). New table: instant_bookings — id, event_id, package_id, vndr_tenant_id, host_id, amount, deposit_amount, status, booked_at.

29.2 — Real-time vendor availability calendar

Every Vndr, Catr, and Venue publishes their availability. Dates with confirmed bookings are automatically blocked. When a Orgnz or Plnr searches for vendors for a specific event date, only available vendors appear — the "are you available?" email cycle is eliminated entirely.
Vendor side — availability management
Vndr dashboard shows a monthly calendar. Blocked dates (from confirmed bookings) auto-populate. Vndr can additionally block personal unavailability dates (vacation, hold periods). Two-way sync with Google Calendar when §30.2 calendar sync is enabled. Availability displayed publicly on marketplace profile as a "Next available" indicator.
Orgnz/Plnr side — filtered search
When searching vendors, event date is a required filter. Results show only available vendors. Unavailable vendors appear in a collapsed "Not available for your date" section — useful for saving to a future event shortlist. Cue's vendor suggestion engine skips unavailable vendors entirely (hard gate in ranking algorithm — §26).
DB tableKey fieldsNotes
vendor_availabilityid, tenant_id, date, status (available | blocked_booking | blocked_personal), booking_id (nullable)One row per date per vendor. Populated automatically on booking confirmation. Manual blocks via dashboard.
vendor_holdsid, tenant_id, date, held_by_event_id, expires_atOptional 24-hr soft hold when a quote is in progress — prevents double-booking during negotiation.

29.3 — Verified review system

Reviews are the trust layer of any marketplace. Without verified reviews, new Orgnzs cannot assess vendor quality, and high-performing vendors have no way to differentiate themselves from unproven ones. Every review on EvntCue is verified-purchase only — no anonymous reviews, no review bombing.
Trigger and timing
Review request auto-sent 48hrs after event close date. Sent to Orgnz (reviews Catr, Venue, Vndrs) and to Plnr (reviews Vndrs). Vendor cannot respond until Orgnz review is submitted — prevents pressure. Review window closes 30 days after event if not completed.
Review structure
Overall star rating (1–5). Four structured categories: punctuality, quality of work, communication, value for money — each rated separately. Free-text field (50–500 chars). Photo upload optional (supports portfolio on vendor profile). All fields required except photo.
Vendor response
Vendor can post one public response per review. Responses appear below the review on the profile. No editing after submission — both parties are locked in. Admin can flag/remove reviews for policy violations only.
Review data feeds directly into Cue's vendor performance scoring algorithm (§9 — Vndr performance scoring touchpoint). The composite score weights: overall rating 40%, punctuality 20%, communication 20%, quality 20%. Vendors with fewer than 3 reviews show "New — no reviews yet" rather than a partial score.
DB tableKey fields
reviewsid, event_id, booking_id, reviewer_id, reviewee_tenant_id, overall_rating, punctuality, quality, communication, value, body, photo_url, vendor_response, submitted_at, response_at
review_requestsid, event_id, reviewer_id, reviewee_tenant_id, status (pending|submitted|expired), sent_at, expires_at

29.4 — Rich vendor portfolio profiles

A vendor profile with no photos gets no bookings. Every Vndr and Catr profile must support rich media — real past event work, tagged by event type, style, and service category — so both Orgnzs/Plnrs and Cue's matching engine have meaningful data to work with.
Portfolio media
Unlimited photo uploads (JPEG, PNG, WebP, HEIC — 25MB max per image). Video embed support (YouTube, Vimeo URLs). Each item tagged: event type (wedding, corporate, quinceañera...), style tags (rustic, modern, maximalist, minimal, garden...), and service category. Items reorderable via drag-and-drop. Featured image (first in order) shown on marketplace card.
Profile completeness score
A completeness percentage drives marketplace search ranking — complete profiles rank higher. Score components: profile photo (10%), bio (10%), service area defined (10%), at least 5 portfolio items (20%), pricing/packages published (20%), availability calendar populated (20%), certifications uploaded (10%). Displayed as a progress bar on the vendor dashboard with action prompts for each incomplete item.
Portfolio image tags feed directly into Cue's style-match algorithm (§26 — vendor suggestion engine, style match factor 30%). When a Orgnz adds images to their mood board, Cue extracts style tags via image analysis and cross-references them against Vndr portfolio tags to compute the style match score. A florist whose portfolio is tagged "garden, romantic, peony, pastel" ranks higher for a mood board containing garden ceremony images than one tagged "modern, tropical, bold."

29.5 — Lead CRM for Plnrs

Plnrs will not migrate from HoneyBook or Dubsado unless EvntCue handles their lead pipeline. This is the feature that converts a Plnr from "interested" to "all-in." Without it, Plnrs use EvntCue for active events and their existing CRM for new business — a split that kills retention.
Pipeline stages
New inquiry → Consultation scheduled → Proposal sent → Contract signed → Deposit collected → Event active → Completed → Archived. Each stage is a column in a Kanban view or a row in a list view — Plnr switches between layouts. Drag a lead card to advance the stage.
Lead record
Auto-created when an inquiry arrives (email parse via Cue client intake parser — §9). Fields: contact name, email, phone, event type, event date, guest count, budget range, venue (if known), notes, source (website, referral, EvntCue marketplace, direct). All fields editable. Activity log shows every touch: emails sent, calls logged, proposals viewed.
Conversion analytics
Per-Plnr dashboard: leads by stage, conversion rate per stage, average time-in-stage, revenue in pipeline, closed-won revenue YTD. Cue surfaces: "You have 3 leads that haven't moved in 14+ days — want me to draft a follow-up for each?" Conversion data improves Cue's proposal suggestions over time.
DB tableKey fields
plnr_leadsid, plnr_tenant_id, contact_name, email, phone, event_type, event_date, guest_count, budget_min, budget_max, venue, stage, source, notes, created_at, updated_at
lead_activitiesid, lead_id, type (email_sent|call_logged|note_added|stage_changed|proposal_viewed), body, created_by, created_at
30 — P1 retention features (month 3–6)
Eight features that convert trial users to long-term paying subscribers

30.1 — Automated workflow triggers

The single most effective retention feature in every competing CRM. Planners who set up automation don't leave — the workflows are too embedded in their business to migrate. EvntCue's workflow engine sits on top of the existing task and event system.
Trigger types
Event-based: contract signed, deposit received, event date minus X days, stage changed, review submitted, booking confirmed. Time-based: X days after inquiry, X days before event, X days after event. Manual: Plnr clicks "Run workflow" on any lead or event.
Action types
Send email (from Resend, using template): send proposal, send contract, send invoice, send reminder. Create task (from template): assign to Plnr, assign to Orgnz, set due date. Move lead to stage. Trigger Cue prompt: "Draft a follow-up email for this lead." Add note to activity log.
Workflow builder UI: a simple linear chain of trigger → actions, configurable without code. Available on Plnr Pro tier only. Pre-built templates ship at launch: "New inquiry onboarding," "Post-signing welcome," "30-day event countdown," "Post-event review request." Plnrs can duplicate and customize templates or build from scratch.

30.2 — Calendar sync — Google, Apple, Outlook

Two-way calendar sync via OAuth. EvntCue events, task due dates, and booking confirmations appear in the user's personal calendar. External calendar events block EvntCue availability automatically. Critical for Plnrs managing multiple events and Vndrs who use their personal calendar as ground truth for their schedule.
DirectionWhat syncsBehavior
EvntCue → CalendarEvent dates, task due dates, booking confirmations, timeline milestonesCreates calendar events with event name, location (venue), and deep link back to EvntCue event record
Calendar → EvntCueExternal events on the connected calendarBlocks corresponding dates on the vendor availability calendar — shown as "Unavailable" to marketplace search
Implementation: Google Calendar API (OAuth 2.0), Apple EventKit (CalDAV), Microsoft Graph API (Outlook). Sync interval: real-time via webhook for Google, polling every 15 minutes for Apple/Outlook. Stored in calendar_connections table: id, user_id, provider, access_token, refresh_token, calendar_id, sync_enabled, last_synced_at.

30.3 — Branded white-label client portal

Professional Plnrs maintain their own brand identity with clients. When a Plnr invites a Orgnz to EvntCue, the Orgnz should see "Sarah Chen Events," not "EvntCue." This is available on Plnr Pro only and is one of the strongest Pro conversion levers.
Branding options
Upload logo (PNG/SVG, displayed in header). Set primary color (applied to buttons, accents). Custom subdomain: sarah-chen.evntcue.com. Toggle "Powered by EvntCue" footer (visible on free trial, hidden on Pro). All Orgnz-facing emails sent from Plnr's brand name with Reply-To set to Plnr's email.
Scope
Applies only to the Orgnz portal view — Plnr's own dashboard, Vndr portals, and internal tools remain EvntCue-branded. The white-label is the client-facing layer only. The Plnr sees their brand applied in a preview mode before publishing.
Technical
CSS variables injected at the layout level based on plnr_branding table. Subdomain routing via Vercel's wildcard domain support. Logo stored in Supabase Storage. No additional infrastructure required beyond subdomain wildcard config.

30.4 — Visual proposal builder

Cue can draft a proposal (§9), but the Orgnz/client needs to receive a designed, interactive proposal they can browse, select from, and sign — not a text document. The proposal builder produces a shareable link the client opens in their browser: no PDF, no download, no login required to view.
Builder (Plnr/Vndr side)
Drag-and-drop sections: intro block (branded header, event summary), service packages (Good/Better/Best tiers with descriptions and pricing), line item add-ons (optional, each togglable), payment schedule (deposit + milestone payments), terms and conditions (editable text). Cue populates initial content from event record — Plnr edits. Preview in client view before sending.
Client flow (Orgnz side)
Orgnz receives email with proposal link. Opens branded proposal page (white-label if enabled). Selects package tier + optional add-ons. Reviews payment schedule. E-signs with typed name + timestamp (legally binding). Pays deposit inline via Stripe. Booking confirmed automatically. Plnr notified instantly. Lead card in CRM advances to "Deposit collected."

30.5 — Accounting integration — QuickBooks Online and Xero

One-way export of financial records from EvntCue to the Plnr or Vndr's accounting software. Eliminates double-entry. Commission flows export as separate line items for clean P&L reporting. Priority for Plnr Pro and Venue Professional tiers.
What exportsMapped toFrequency
Invoices and deposits collectedInvoice in QBO/Xero with line itemsReal-time on payment received
Vendor payouts (Plnr-managed)Bill/expense in QBO/XeroReal-time on payout triggered
Commission income receivedIncome line item, separate account codeReal-time on commission settled
Platform subscription feesExpense in QBO/XeroMonthly on billing date
Implementation: QuickBooks Online API (OAuth 2.0) and Xero API (OAuth 2.0). Stored in accounting_connections table. Export failures logged and retried — Plnr notified if export fails after 3 attempts. Manual re-export available per transaction.

30.6 — Mobile check-in app (PWA)

Extends the existing PWA (§16) with day-of check-in functionality. No additional app download — accessed via the same PWA. Operated by the Plnr or an event staff member at the door. Works offline with sync on reconnect.
Check-in modes
QR code scan (guest receives QR via RSVP confirmation email) or name lookup (type first few letters, select from list). Both modes show guest name, table assignment, dietary flags, and any special notes immediately on confirmation.
Real-time feed
Live attendance count visible to Plnr, Orgnz, and Catr simultaneously. Catr sees checked-in headcount vs. expected headcount — allows kitchen to adjust service timing. Final count locked 30 minutes after doors open and sent to Catr as a BEO update.
Offline behavior
Guest list pre-loaded in IndexedDB at "Save for event day" trigger (§16/§23). Check-ins recorded locally while offline. Sync queue fires on reconnect. Conflict resolution: server count is authoritative — local additions merge, never overwrite.

30.7 — NPS and post-event vendor surveys

Two distinct survey types triggered automatically after every event. Both feed Cue's vendor performance scoring and EvntCue's internal platform health metrics.
Orgnz NPS survey (24hrs post-event)
Net Promoter Score (0–10): "How likely are you to recommend EvntCue to a friend planning an event?" Single-question NPS. If score ≤ 6: follow-up "What could we have done better?" (open text). If score ≥ 9: follow-up "What did you love most?" + optional testimonial opt-in. Results aggregated into platform NPS dashboard (admin-only).
Per-vendor rating survey (48hrs post-event)
This is the review system from §29.3 — the same survey but framed here as distinct from platform NPS. Orgnz rates each confirmed vendor separately. Results are: (a) published on vendor public profile, (b) fed to Cue performance score, (c) visible to the Plnr in their vendor performance history. Plnr builds a personal vendor "track record" over multiple events.

30.8 — 3D floor plan and room layout tool

Interactive floor plan builder for Venue Professional and Plnr Pro tiers. The decision on build vs. integrate: EvntCue should integrate with AllSeated/Prismm via their API rather than building a spatial planning tool from scratch. AllSeated is best-in-class and already HoneyBook-integrated — EvntCue should match that partnership or offer a competing integration. If API access is not available or cost-prohibitive, build a simplified 2D version first.
Option A — AllSeated/Prismm integration
Embed AllSeated floor plan directly in the EvntCue Venue portal. Floor plan data syncs to the event record. Shareable link appears in the final packet (§23). Vendor service areas visible on plan. Preferred — fastest path to best-in-class spatial planning. Revenue share with AllSeated TBD.
Option B — Native 2D builder (fallback)
Grid-based 2D layout: drag-and-drop tables (round 60", rectangle 6ft, 8ft), chairs, staging, bars, DJ booth, dance floor, buffet stations. Room dimensions entered manually. Export as PDF. No 3D — pure operational tool. Faster to build, sufficient for most private events. Can be built in-house in ~80 engineer-hours.
31 — P2 growth features (year 2)
Five features that diversify revenue and expand marketplace reach after core liquidity is established

31.1 — Two-sided vendor matchmaking

Currently Cue recommends vendors to Orgnzs and Plnrs (one-sided). Two-sided matchmaking flips the model — relevant Vndrs are notified when events matching their profile are posted. This converts a passive marketplace (vendors wait to be found) into an active lead generation channel (vendors are surfaced to relevant opportunities).
How it works
When a new event is created and the event type, date, location, and budget are set, Cue runs a reverse match: which Vndrs in each category have (a) availability on the date, (b) service area covering the venue location, (c) style tags matching the event type, and (d) pricing within the budget range. Top 5 per category receive a notification: "A [event type] in [city] on [date] matches your profile — [budget range] budget. Want to submit a quote?"
Vendor response flow
Vendor taps notification → sees event brief (type, date, location, guest count, budget range — no Orgnz identity revealed) → taps "Submit quote" → Cue drafts an initial quote from their package pricing → vendor reviews and edits → submits. Quote appears in Plnr/Orgnz vendor shortlist automatically. This is the distress booking fast-lane from §24 extended to all normal bookings.

31.2 — Featured listing and promoted placement

Vndrs and Catrs pay for promoted placement in marketplace search results. This is a third revenue stream alongside subscriptions and transaction fees. Strict guardrails prevent the featured system from eroding trust — it must feel like a quality signal, not an ad.
RuleDetail
Max featured slots per category per search2 featured vendors maximum per results page. Never more — prevents the page feeling like paid ads.
EligibilityFeatured slots only available to vendors with: (a) profile completeness ≥ 80%, (b) at least 3 verified reviews, (c) average rating ≥ 4.0. Quality gate prevents buying visibility over performance.
LabelingFeatured badge clearly displayed — "Featured" in small type. Not disguised as organic results. Trust depends on transparency.
Pricing modelMonthly flat fee per category per geography (e.g. $49/mo for featured placement in "Florists — Dallas"). Admin-configurable by market. Billed via Stripe subscription on vendor account.
Ranking within featuredMultiple featured vendors in same category ranked by review score — not by spend. Paying more doesn't buy a higher position among featured vendors.

31.3 — Sponsorship and exhibitor module

For corporate galas, charity events, and conferences hosted on EvntCue. Enables the Orgnz or Plnr to manage sponsor relationships, deliverables, and ROI reporting within the event record — rather than in a separate spreadsheet or email chain.
Sponsor management
Sponsor tiers (configurable: Gold/Silver/Bronze or custom naming). Each tier has: logo rights, digital placement, speaking slot allocation, table allocation, recognition in run-of-show. Sponsor record tracks: company name, contact, tier, payment status, deliverables checklist.
Exhibitor booth assignment
Booth numbers assigned from floor plan (§30.8). Exhibitor sees their assigned location on the event floor plan. Load-in time slot assigned and visible in run-of-show. Equipment requirements (tables, chairs, power outlets) entered by exhibitor and visible to Venue.
Post-event sponsor ROI report
Generated by Cue 48hrs post-event: attendee count, estimated reach, logo placements delivered, speaking slot performance (if feedback collected), overall event NPS. PDF export. Orgnz sends directly to sponsors as fulfillment documentation. Builds repeat sponsorship relationships.

31.4 — Multi-currency support

USD-only at launch. Multi-currency is a Phase 2 requirement for any international expansion. Stripe Connect supports multi-currency settlement natively — the implementation is configuration, not a rewrite.
ComponentImplementation
Display currencyDetected from browser locale or user profile setting. Prices displayed in local currency using live FX rates (Stripe FX API). Display only — settlement always in the vendor's configured payout currency.
Settlement currencyEach Stripe Connect account has a configured payout currency. Vendor sets this at onboarding. Stripe handles FX conversion — EvntCue passes through at Stripe's rate.
Platform fees2.5% platform fee calculated on the settled amount in USD equivalent. Commission flows calculated in USD for consistency in the ledger regardless of transaction currency.
Launch currenciesUSD (launch). CAD, GBP, EUR, MXN (Phase 2 — Month 6). AUD, BRL (Year 2).

31.5 — Event insurance integration

No competitor offers integrated event insurance. Every host faces the risk of cancellation, vendor no-shows, weather, and liability — and currently has to navigate this entirely outside any planning platform. EvntCue closes this gap with a white-label insurance purchase flow embedded directly in the booking confirmation step.
Coverage types offered
Event liability insurance (covers third-party injury/property damage at the event). Cancellation/postponement insurance (refunds deposits and non-refundable costs if event must cancel due to illness, weather, or force majeure). Vendor no-show coverage (partial reimbursement if a confirmed vendor cancels within 72hrs of event). All three available as optional add-ons at booking confirmation.
Revenue model and implementation
Partner with specialty event insurer (Markel Event Insurance, Travelers, or WedSafe). EvntCue earns 10–15% referral commission on each policy sold. Policy purchase embedded in booking confirmation flow — one additional step, not a redirect. Policy document stored in event record and included in final packet (§23). Premium calculated based on event type, guest count, total event value, and location.
32 — Vndr portal
Per-package commission slider — full spec
Each Vndr service package has an independent referral rate slider. The rate represents the percentage of the package booking price the Vndr offers to any Plnr who recommends and books them. It is set per package — not per category, not per day, not account-wide — because different packages carry different margins and the Vndr should control the offer at that level of granularity.

Slider spec — per package

UI — package editor
The slider lives inside the package edit form, below the price field. Range: 0%–20% in 0.5% increments (admin-capped at 20% per v26.1). Default: 0%. Label: "Plnr referral rate." Below the slider: a live payout projection — "At this rate, you offer $[X] per booking." A secondary line: "Your net on a $[price] booking: $[net after platform fee + referral]." No slider = no referral = lowest Cue ranking weight for that package.
Visibility boost indicator
A small signal bar (3 segments: low / medium / high) sits next to the slider. At 0%: "Low visibility to Plnrs." At 1–9%: "Medium." At 10%+: "High — Plnrs see this package first." Honest and transparent — the Vndr knows exactly what the rate does without it feeling like a hidden mechanism.

DB schema — vndr_packages additions

ColumnTypeNotes
referral_rate_pctnumeric default 00.00–20.00. Stored as decimal (15.00 = 15%). Server-validated against admin cap. CHECK constraint: referral_rate_pct >= 0 AND referral_rate_pct <= 20.
referral_rate_capnumericAdmin-set per vendor category on platform_comm_rates. Default 20 (v26.1). Slider UI enforces cap.
referral_amount_last_30dinteger (cents)Materialized view — total referral payouts on this package in last 30 days. Shown as ROI signal in package dashboard.

Plnr marketplace — referral rate display

Plnr view
[Vendor name] · 4.8★ · from $800 · 15% referral on Standard / 10% on Premium. Sort: Best match · Highest rated · Highest referral · Lowest price. Filter: "Referral 10%+" checkbox. Referral badge in rose. Referral rates shown per-package when expanded.
Organizer view — same card
[Vendor name] · 4.8★ · from $800. No referral rate. No badge. No commission language. The field is excluded at the query level — not hidden with CSS. Organizer API response does not include referral_rate_pct.

Payout mechanics

StepTimingWhat happens
Booking confirmed + deposit collectedDay 0commission_flows record: type=vndr_referral, status=pending, amount = package_price × referral_rate_pct
48 hours post-event, no disputeEvent + 2 daysStatus → released. Trustap releases to Plnr.
Dispute opened within 48hrsEvent + 0–2 daysStatus → disputed. Admin reviews, resolved within 5 business days.
Booking cancelled before eventAny timecommission_flow record voided. No referral payout regardless of cancellation reason.
33 — Plnr portal
Service fee manager — full UI spec
The service fee manager is the Plnr's invoicing tool for their professional fees. Entirely separate from commission intelligence — different nav tab, different DB table, different visual treatment. A Plnr who never touches a commission still needs this. It is the financial center of the Plnr-Organizer relationship.

Where it lives in the Plnr portal

Nav placement
Tab called "Fees & invoices" on the event record. Separate from "Commission ledger." Badge count shows unpaid fees. Mobile: swipeable tab within event detail.
Summary strip
Three metric cards: Total billed · Collected · Outstanding. Green for collected, amber for outstanding. Same metric card pattern as other portal dashboards.
Fee list
Each service_fee: description, amount, status pill (Draft / Invoiced / Paid / Refunded), date. Actions: Edit (draft only) · Send invoice · Mark paid (offline) · Refund. Add fee button top-right.

Create / edit fee modal

FieldTypeBehavior
DescriptionText inputShown on invoice. Pre-filled suggestions: "Full-service planning fee", "Day-of coordination", "Design consultation", "Vendor management fee." Plnr edits freely.
Fee typeToggle: Flat / PercentageFlat = enter dollar amount. Percentage = enter rate, system calculates from event total budget live.
Amount / RateNumber inputFlat: dollar field. Percentage: rate field + read-only calculated amount with basis shown: "15% of $28,000 event budget = $4,200."
Payment scheduleSelectSingle payment · 50% deposit + 50% on completion · Custom (up to 3 milestones with amount, due date, description each).
Notes to clientTextarea optionalAppears below fee on invoice. Plnr uses for scope inclusions/exclusions.

Invoice generation and delivery

PDF generation
Server-side via Puppeteer on "Send invoice" tap. Branded with Plnr's logo + colors if white-label enabled (§30.3). Contains: parties, event, fee description, payment schedule, Stripe payment link, terms. Stored in Supabase Storage → invoice_url on service_fees record.
Payment collection
Invoice email (Resend) contains Stripe payment link. Organizer pays by card or ACH. Stripe webhook → status = paid, paid_at populated, Plnr notified. Platform fee 2.5% applies. Plnr nets 97.5% of their fee.

Total income view — commissions + service fees combined

Total Plnr income per event = service fees + commission flows. Example: $2,500 planning fee (service_fees) + $750 florist referral + $400 venue sourcing fee (commission_flows) = $3,650 total. Plnr sees this consolidated. Organizer sees only the $2,500 invoice. The Plnr's income summary card at the top of each event shows both streams, clearly labeled, as separate rows — never merged into one figure.
34 — Venue portal
Venue commission flows — all four inside flow types fully specced
Venues both pay out (to Plnrs who source events) and receive (from vendors operating on their property). All four venue commission flow types are configured through a new "Commission setup" section in the Venue portal — a four-step wizard at first setup, individual toggles thereafter.

Flow 1 — In-house fees: venue_in_house

Fees charged to the Organizer for venue-related services. Not hidden — they appear on the Organizer's contract as line items. But they are revenue the Venue earns on top of room rental and are tracked as commission_flows for reporting.
Cake cutting fee
Enable/disable. Rate per guest (default $3.50). Applied to confirmed guest count at finalization. venue_in_house flow: basis = guest_count × rate.
Corkage fee
Enable/disable. Rate per bottle, max bottles. Venue enters bottle count post-event. Flow basis = bottle_count × rate.
Custom fees
Security deposit, setup/teardown, valet surcharge, coat check. Each as flat or per-guest. Admin can add custom fee types via wizard.

Flow 2 — F&B surcharge: venue_fb_surcharge

Charged to the Catr as a percentage of their F&B revenue when outside catering is allowed. Applies to food and beverage only — not labor. Catr pays from their payout. Surcharge rate shown to Catr during booking inquiry, before confirmation — no surprises.
Venue config
Per space: outside catering policy (allowed / not allowed / allowed with surcharge). If surcharge: rate 0–25%, basis selector (F&B only recommended / total invoice). Default: F&B only.
Catr view
BEO P&L shows: "Venue F&B surcharge: [rate]% = $[amount]" as a cost line. Reduces net automatically. Agreed to at booking confirmation — displayed in inquiry step before acceptance.

Flow 3 — Preferred vendor kickback: venue_kickback

Annual or per-event fee from Vndr to Venue for preferred list placement. Optional for venues. Inside — never disclosed to Organizers or Plnrs. Vndr opts in explicitly and sees the cost on their vendor dashboard. Acceptance logged with timestamp.
Venue config
Kickback type: annual flat or per-event %. Amount or rate per vendor category. Vendor must accept terms to appear on preferred list. Kickback deducted from Vndr payout at settlement.
Vndr view
"Preferred vendor status at [Venue]: $[amount]/year or [rate]% per booking." Explicit opt-in. Vendors who don't pay are still bookable but don't appear on preferred list.

Flow 4 — Plnr sourcing commission: venue_referral

Venue pays a % of their booking fee to the Plnr who sourced the event. Outside commission — Plnr sees it, Organizer does not. Configured per space. Same 48hr post-event escrow as Vndr referrals. Same rose badge treatment in Plnr marketplace.

SettingOptionsNotes
Sourcing rate0–20% of venue booking feeAdmin-capped at 20% for venue flows
BasisRental fee only / Total invoice / CustomRental fee only is standard — excludes F&B and add-ons
Payout48hr post-event escrow via TrustapSame as Vndr referral payout timing
Plnr display"10% sourcing commission" badge on venue card — Plnr view onlyIdentical treatment to Vndr referral rate badge
35 — Organizer portal
Corporate Organizer mode — commission context off
Two distinct types of people use the Organizer portal: a personal Organizer planning their own event (wedding, milestone, party), and a corporate Organizer — an events manager, HR coordinator, or executive assistant planning on behalf of a company. Their logistics needs are identical. Their commission context is not. The corporate Organizer's "Plnr" is a salaried employee. Commission flow disclosures are irrelevant and would be actively confusing.
The flag: organizer_accounts.commission_context boolean default true. When false, all commission-adjacent UI is suppressed throughout the Organizer portal — for every event on that account, permanently until changed. Enforced server-side at the API layer, not with CSS.

What changes when commission_context = false

UI elementPersonal (true)Corporate (false)
Disclosure note on vendor booking"Your planner receives a referral from this vendor." Shown if Plnr disclosed.Not shown. Query that generates note is gated by flag — data not sent.
Plnr hire confirmationShows fee + "This Plnr may also earn referral fees from vendors."Shows fee only. No referral fee mention.
Invoice line itemsService fee + optional commission acknowledgment if disclosed.Service fee only. No commission language anywhere.
Post-event summaryMay show "Your Plnr earned referrals totaling $X" if Plnr disclosed.Not shown. Summary contains logistics and spend data only.
Vendor marketplaceStandard — referral rates are Plnr-only anyway.Identical — no change needed.

How the flag gets set

Onboarding question
After "Tell us about your event": "Who is managing the planning?" → A: "A professional planner or coordinator I hired" (commission_context = true) · B: "My company's events team / I'm coordinating it myself" (commission_context = false) · C: "I'll decide later" (defaults to true, changeable in settings).
Settings toggle
Account Settings → "Planning context." Toggle: "Show referral fee disclosures from my planner." On = true. Off = false. Plain-English: "When off, we won't show you information about referral arrangements between your planner and vendors. Most corporate accounts prefer this." Changeable at any time — takes effect immediately.

Server-side enforcement — not a CSS hide

All API endpoints that could return commission-adjacent data check commission_context before including it in the response. The disclosure note generator, Plnr hire email template, invoice PDF template, and post-event summary generator all accept the flag and return clean output when false. There is no front-end conditional rendering of commission data — it is simply not sent. The Plnr portal is unaffected: Plnrs see full commission detail for all events regardless of their Organizer's setting.
36 — Financial integrity & compliance
23 issues audited — data types, concurrency, tax, regulatory, and schema gaps
A comprehensive audit of every financial assumption in the platform identified 23 issues across five categories. Six are critical — they must be resolved before any financial code is written. This section documents all findings, required fixes, and the updated schema. Issues are numbered to match the audit report.
Build order rule: No financial transaction code ships until issues 1–6 are implemented. Issues 7–10 are legal requirements that must be reviewed by counsel before launch. Issues 11–19 are build-ready specs. Issues 20–23 are confirmations that existing decisions are correct.

Category 1 — Data type integrity (Critical)

All monetary amounts are stored as integer cents. All percentage rates are stored as numeric(5,2). No floating point numbers touch financial data at any layer. This is enforced by DB column types, CHECK constraints, and a PaymentService validation layer.
#IssueFix
1Money stored as untyped / float — bookings.total, deposit_pct, all commission amounts were untyped. IEEE 754 float math corrupts monetary ledgers silently at scale.All monetary columns → integer (cents). All percentage columns → numeric(5,2). Application layer divides by 100 for display. Never store $10.50 — store 1050.
2vndr_packages.referral_rate_pct has no range constraint — an INSERT of 0.15 instead of 15.00 produces a 100× error on every payout from that package.Add CHECK constraint: referral_rate_pct >= 0 AND referral_rate_pct <= 20 (cap reduced from 25 to 20 in v26.1). Add DB comment: "Stored as decimal percentage — 15.00 means 15%." Validate in PaymentService before any calculation.
3Gratuity pool — no schema, no tax classification — the Catr labor module mentions gratuity pool but no table exists. Auto-gratuity (mandatory service charge) is taxable as wages; voluntary tips are taxable to the employee. The distinction is legally required.New tables: gratuity_pools (id, event_id, catr_tenant_id, pool_type enum(auto_gratuity|discretionary_tip), rate_or_amount, total_pool_cents, distributed boolean, created_at) and gratuity_distributions (id, pool_id, staff_id, amount_cents, distributed_at). Advisory label on auto_gratuity: "This is a service charge — may be treated as wages. Consult a payroll advisor."

Category 2 — Concurrency and idempotency (Critical)

Three race conditions exist that can corrupt financial state. All three require database-level solutions — application-level locks are insufficient.
#IssueFix
4No Stripe webhook idempotency — Stripe retries webhooks up to 25 times. Without idempotency keys, a single payment_intent.succeeded processed twice creates duplicate commission records and duplicate payouts.New table: stripe_webhook_events (id = Stripe event.id PK, type, processed_at, status enum(processing|completed|failed)). Handler pattern: INSERT with ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING — if 0 rows inserted, return 200 immediately. All financial writes inside a Postgres transaction scoped to the event ID.
5Instant book double-booking race condition — two Plnrs simultaneously check availability (both see "available"), both proceed to payment, both succeed. Vndr has two confirmed bookings for the same date.Instant book must use SELECT FOR UPDATE on vendor_availability row for the booking date. Pattern: BEGIN → SELECT FOR UPDATE WHERE vndr_tenant_id=X AND date=Y AND status='available' → if locked, INSERT booking → UPDATE availability to 'blocked_booking' → COMMIT. If no rows returned: date taken → surface "Just booked by someone else" to user.
6Booking confirmation and commission_flow creation not atomic — server error between booking INSERT and commission_flow INSERT leaves a confirmed booking with no commission record. Plnr never receives their referral. Payout system has nothing to query.PaymentService.confirmBooking() is a single Postgres transaction: (1) INSERT booking, (2) INSERT commission_flow(s), (3) INSERT vendor_availability block, (4) COMMIT — or rollback everything. Stripe charge uses manual capture: authorize first, capture only after COMMIT succeeds. If COMMIT fails: cancel the PaymentIntent authorization. No partial state is permitted.

Category 3 — Tax configuration (Legal requirement — counsel required)

#IssuePlatform action
7Sales tax — no collection or display infrastructure. In Texas, catering services are taxable. EvntCue is a marketplace (not the seller) and is not required to collect and remit — but invoices must show a tax line and vendors must understand their obligation.Add tax_amount_cents integer default 0 to bookings. Allow vendors to configure their tax rate in settings. Invoice PDF shows: "Tax collected by [Vendor]: $[X]." ToS statement: "EvntCue users are responsible for collecting and remitting applicable taxes in their jurisdiction." P2: TaxJar/Avalara integration for automated tax calculation.
8Texas TABC — Mixed Beverage Gross Receipts Tax (6.7%) + Mixed Beverage Sales Tax (8.25%). TABC-licensed Catrs owe these taxes on every alcohol service. The platform tracks TABC cert upload but has no alcohol revenue field and no tax advisory.Add alcohol_revenue_cents integer default 0 to BEO financial summary. When Catr has TABC cert and records alcohol service: advisory panel: "Your alcohol revenue of $[X] may be subject to Texas Mixed Beverage Tax (6.7% MBGRT + 8.25% MBST). Consult your tax advisor." Advisory only — never calculated or remitted by EvntCue.
9Auto-gratuity vs. voluntary tip — IRS tax treatment differs. Mandatory service charges are employer wages (FICA applies). Voluntary tips are employee income (reported differently). Misclassification is an IRS audit risk for Catrs.gratuity_pools.pool_type enum distinguishes auto_gratuity vs. discretionary_tip (see issue 3). UI labels differ. Tooltip on auto_gratuity: "Mandatory service charges may be treated as wages. Consult a payroll advisor." EvntCue does not file payroll taxes — advisory only.
10venue_fb_surcharge may itself be taxable. In Texas, a surcharge on a taxable service (food) may be subject to sales tax. Catrs who don't account for this undercharge clients.Add is_taxable boolean default false and tax_rate_pct numeric(5,2) default 0 to venue F&B surcharge config. When is_taxable=true: BEO shows advisory: "Venue F&B surcharge of $[X] may be subject to sales tax at [rate]%. Consult your tax advisor." Advisory only.

Category 4 — Regulatory: permits, licenses, occupancy (Build-ready)

#IssueFix
11Temporary event permits — not tracked anywhere. Noise ordinance waivers, temporary food service permits, tent/structure permits, right-of-way permits, fireworks permits. Events proceeding without required permits expose the Orgnz and Plnr to fines and shutdown.New table: event_permits (id, event_id, permit_type, issuing_authority, permit_number, status enum(required|applied|approved|waived|not_required), expiry_date, notes). Event type templates (§26) carry a list of commonly required permits per event type. Cue surfaces these during event setup: "Outdoor events in Dallas over 500 guests typically require a Special Events Permit. Want me to add this to your checklist?" Checklist item only — not a booking gate.
12Venue occupancy limits not enforced at guest count cascade. Orgnz updates guest count above venue capacity — no system check blocks it. Fire code violation at the event is a serious liability.At booking confirmation AND at every guest count cascade: CHECK events.guest_count ≤ venue_spaces.capacity for the booked space. If exceeded: block the update, surface: "This guest count exceeds [Venue]'s permitted capacity of [X]. Contact the venue to discuss options." Venue can configure a soft warning threshold (default 90% of capacity) and a hard block (100%). Both configurable in venue space settings.
13Vndr and Plnr general liability insurance — not tracked. Catr cert tracking is full (§21). Vndrs and Plnrs have no COI requirement or tracking. EvntCue may be named in claims from events it facilitated.New table: vndr_certifications (id, tenant_id, type enum(general_liability|business_license|professional_cert|other), doc_url, expiry_date, verified_by_admin, created_at). For Vndr Pro: general liability COI is a soft requirement — listing remains active but a "No COI on file" badge appears on their marketplace profile card. For Plnr Pro: same soft requirement. Hard gate only for Catrs (food safety non-negotiable). Expiry tracking identical to §21 model.
14EvntCue's marketplace liability — no platform ToS or FinCEN assessment. As a payment facilitator, EvntCue may need FinCEN registration. As a marketplace facilitator, sales tax remittance may be required in some states.Legal question — flag for counsel before launch. Minimum platform actions: (1) ToS: "EvntCue is a technology platform, not a party to any service agreement between users." (2) 1099-K reporting (see issue 19). (3) Document that Stripe Connect KYC is the identity verification mechanism for payouts. (4) Marketplace facilitator sales tax: engage tax attorney for states where EvntCue has nexus.

Category 5 — Schema integrity (Build-ready)

#IssueFix
15bookings table missing critical financial fields. Current schema is dangerously sparse — no deposit_amount_cents, no tax_amount_cents, no platform_fee_cents, no currency, no Stripe IDs, no cancellation fields.Full bookings schema: id, event_id, vndr_tenant_id, package_id, subtotal_cents integer, tax_amount_cents integer default 0, platform_fee_cents integer, vndr_referral_amount_cents integer default 0, deposit_amount_cents integer, total_cents integer, balance_due_cents integer, deposit_pct numeric(5,2), status enum(pending|confirmed|cancelled|completed|disputed), cancellation_policy jsonb (frozen at booking time), currency char(3) default 'USD', stripe_payment_intent_id text, stripe_transfer_id text, ref_number, created_at, confirmed_at, cancelled_at, cancellation_reason, completed_at.
16commission_flows missing status lifecycle. No status field means payout logic, escrow system, and dispute resolution have no state machine to query or update.Add to commission_flows: status enum(pending|released|paid|voided|disputed) default 'pending', released_at timestamptz, paid_at timestamptz, voided_at timestamptz, voided_reason text, dispute_id uuid FK → disputes.
17No disputes table. Disputes are referenced throughout the spec (cancellation flows, review adjudication, commission escrow) but the table doesn't exist. Admin cannot track or resolve disputes.New table: disputes (id, type enum(booking_cancellation|commission|review|payment|vendor_withdrawal), related_id uuid, related_table text, opened_by_tenant_id, status enum(open|under_review|resolved|closed), resolution text, resolved_by_admin_id, opened_at, resolved_at, notes text).
18tenants.type still contained 'host' — now 'orgnz'. The rename must be completed before any migration runs. RLS policies that reference 'host' must be updated simultaneously.Resolved in this version. tenants.type enum now includes 'orgnz'. All RLS policies updated. Route guard updated to orgnz. CSS class updated to pp-orgnz. DB table names host_events and host_tenant_id noted for migration rename to orgnz_events and orgnz_tenant_id in the first schema migration.

Category 6 — 1099-K and contractor compliance (Legal requirement)

#IssueFix
191099-K threshold tracking — no spec or infrastructure. IRS requires payment platforms to issue 1099-K to any payee receiving ≥$600 in a calendar year (effective 2024+). Stripe Connect handles direct charges — but Trustap commission payouts may not be covered.At Vndr/Plnr/Catr onboarding: collect TIN (EIN or SSN) and legal business name — stored encrypted. New table: annual_payments (id, tenant_id, calendar_year integer, total_paid_cents integer, form_1099k_required boolean, form_sent_at timestamptz). Cron job: every January 1, calculate prior-year totals. Flag all tenants where total_paid_cents ≥ 60000 ($600.00). Trigger 1099-K generation via Stripe or manual export. This is a legal obligation — not optional.

Confirmed correct — no changes needed

Issue 20 — Cancellation policy freeze
§24 correctly specifies JSONB frozen at booking time. Now added to bookings schema in issue 15. No other changes needed.
Issue 21 — Financial data offline exclusion
§16 and §23 correctly exclude all financial records from PWA offline bundle. Server-authoritative only. No fix needed.
Issue 22 — Audit log
§16 specifies immutable audit_log. Schema: id, table_name, record_id, operation (INSERT|UPDATE|DELETE), old_values jsonb, new_values jsonb, actor_id, ip_address, timestamp. Archive to cold storage after 90 days. Never deleted.
Issue 23 — Data retention
§16 correctly states 7-year financial record retention, 30-day PII deletion, indefinite commission records. Correct. Build the deletion pipeline as specified.

Landing page — shorthand glossary

The portal shorthand names (Catr, Vndr, Plnr, Orgnz) are a brand feature — they signal membership in a platform that takes events seriously. But they must be defined on first encounter. The landing page carries a persistent legend near the nav or in the hero section:
Catr = caterer  ·  Vndr = vendor  ·  Plnr = planner  ·  Orgnz = organizer  ·  Venue = venue
Styled small (10px), muted, persistent. Not a tooltip — a legend. Works in print, pitch decks, and static marketing. After first encounter, visitors use the terms fluently. That's the brand effect: the shorthand feels like being in on something.

Gate modes — admin-controlled — locked v26.7

Each verification gate (COI, business license, food handler, liquor license, food handler manager certificate, etc.) carries a gate_mode attribute set per-portal, per-region, per-tier by EvntCue platform admin. Three modes:
ModeBehaviorUI surface
SoftUpload optional. Contributes to Trust Score. Surfaces Verified badge tier when gate cleared.Pill labeled SOFT. Trust score impact line: +N% to Trust Score.
RequiredUpload mandatory. Blocks profile from going live. Blocks booking acceptance.Pill labeled REQUIRED in coral. Continue button gated.
ConditionalRequired only if a related condition is true (e.g. liquor license required only if “alcohol service” is in inclusions; food handler required only if “in-house F&B” is in inclusions).Pill labeled CONDITIONAL. Surfaces only when condition met.

Default modes by portal — v1 launch

GateVndrCatrVenuPlnr
General liability COISoftRequiredSoftSoft
Business licenseSoftRequiredSoftSoft
Food handler certificaten/aRequiredSoft (conditional on in-house F&B)n/a
Food handler managern/aRequiredn/an/a
Liquor licensen/aConditionalConditionaln/a

Trust Score weighting — locked v26.7

Verification is a first-class Trust Score component, not a separate badge orbit. Five components:
ComponentWeightSub-mechanic
Profile completeness30%Atmosphere/Signature board (10%), all required fields filled (10%), founding story complete (5%), 3+ spaces or services defined (5%)
Verification25%Each cleared soft gate contributes proportionally; required gates are pass/fail (zero credit if not cleared)
Response time20%Median first-response time within 1 hour to qualified inquiries
Booking completion15%% of accepted inquiries that reach event-day without cancellation
Reviews10%Average post-event Orgnz review score, weighted by recency

User-facing language — locked v26.7

The word “commission” is reserved for internal/schema use only. Venue managers think in fees, passes, and hold-backs — not commissions. User-facing copy uses:
Schema enum (preserved)Internal nameUser-facing label
venue_in_houseIn-house commissionIn-house fees (charged to Orgnz)
venue_fb_surchargeF&B surcharge commissionF&B surcharge (charged to outside Catr)
venue_kickbackVendor kickbackPreferred vendor pass (received from Vndr)
venue_referralPlnr referral commissionPlanner sourcing fee (paid to Plnr)
The DB enum strings remain unchanged. Migration risk = zero. Only the UI copy changes. Surface in the §85 Workstation as “How money moves” or “Earnings & ledger”; never as “commissions” anywhere a venue manager will read it.

Ledger panel surface — locked v26.7

All four flows render in the same dashboard ledger panel (“Earnings & ledger” or “Your earnings”). Each row shows: flow name (user-facing), counterparty direction (From/To Orgnz/Catr/Vndr/Plnr), period total. The panel is the canonical surfacing of §34 in the workstation. Never bury behind tabs or settings.

26.6May 2026Operational resilience pass — admin platform controls. NEW §83 — Cue kill switch + per-touchpoint disables. Two-level control surface: global kill that disables every Cue API call platform-wide, and per-touchpoint disables for the 10 Cue surfaces from §9 + §42 (vendor suggestion engine, mood board narrative reading, auto-generated vendor brief, style conflict detection, Plnr recommendation gate, run-of-show generator, post-event ROI report, outbound proposal drafting, significant-dates re-engagement, day-of monitoring alerts). Each touchpoint specs its graceful degradation behavior — the platform never errors out a page when Cue is unavailable; affordances grey out with hover-tooltips, manual workflows continue. Server-side enforcement is fail-closed: every Cue API call routes through a single cueRequest() wrapper that checks both platform_settings.cue_global_enabled AND the per-touchpoint enabled flag before issuing any Anthropic API call. UI-only disables can be bypassed by malicious clients; server gates cannot. Two-admin-confirmation requirement on global kill (one admin proposes, second admin confirms within 5 minutes — same break-glass pattern as production database access). Per-touchpoint disables are single-admin to keep response fast for known issues. Status page integration: every global kill auto-posts an incident at status.evntcue.com with admin-supplied reason. New tables: cue_touchpoint_state (one row per touchpoint, seeded with all 10), cue_admin_audit_log (append-only, INSERT-only RLS — same immutability pattern as SafeTab waivers per §67). Four new platform_settings columns: cue_global_enabled, cue_global_disabled_at, cue_global_disabled_by_admin_id, cue_global_disabled_reason. Credit consumption pauses when global kill is active — users mid-conversation do not lose credits to messages that won't send. Mental model: Cue degrades like a power grid, not like a circuit breaker — one bad surface dims, the rest stay lit. NEW §84 — Legacy account status — custom monthly pricing override. Forward-compatibility decision built into the schema from day one rather than retrofit later. Eight new tenants table columns: legacy_pricing boolean default false, legacy_monthly_cents integer (CHECK constraint: NULL when flag false, NOT NULL when flag true), legacy_annual_cents integer optional, legacy_stripe_price_id text (Stripe price object ID created at enable time), legacy_pricing_note text (admin context, why this tenant is on legacy), legacy_pricing_approved_by_admin_id uuid, legacy_pricing_approved_at timestamptz (append-only via trigger — same immutability pattern as plnr_engagements.hire_timestamp), legacy_pricing_expires_at timestamptz nullable (NULL = perpetual; cron expire_legacy_pricing nightly flips back to standard on expiring rows). Single billing-path decision function resolveTenantPriceId() — the only place in the codebase that decides which Stripe price applies to a tenant. Hardcoded price IDs anywhere else fail security review. Admin UI at /admin/tenants/[id] with confirmation modal requiring 20-character reason note. Out of scope for v1: per-feature pricing overrides (separate feature-flag system if needed), tenant self-service legacy enable (admin-only forever), public marketing of legacy availability (never advertised), migration tools to legacy from standard (manual admin action only). Future hooks pre-built into schema: tier-locked legacy, cohort-based legacy, auto-renewal legacy — all three buildable on the v1 schema without breaking changes. Monthly reconciliation cron verifies every legacy tenant's Stripe subscription matches their stored legacy_stripe_price_id — drift triggers admin alert. Legacy MRR reported separately from standard MRR for accurate financial forecasting. What's not changing. §19 standard pricing tiers remain canonical default for 99% of tenants. §9 Cue touchpoint design unchanged. §66/§66.1 commission flow logic unchanged. The 10 Cue surfaces continue to exist as defined; this version adds the ability to turn each off, not the surfaces themselves. Cover badge: v26.5→v26.6.
26.5May 2026Vndr portal v1 shipped — the first complete acquisition arc for any portal. §75 rewritten to match what was actually built: six-stage flow (landing → 4-step capture → freemium dashboard preview), pricing reconciled to §19 ($49/mo Pro, not the legacy $29/mo), COI confirmed as soft per §36 issue 13 (was incorrectly described as a hard gate in pre-v26.5 §75), nine role-category grid in Step 1 (collapsed view of §3's 14 categories minus Catr-adjacent and Compliance for the v1 surface), conditional cert reveals (TABC for mixologists/sommeliers, food handler for coffee/snack vendors), Stripe Connect framed as last step not gate. NEW pattern — Signature Board (mood-board reuse). The Vndr portfolio component is the same component as the Orgnz mood board (§5, §47), with the vector reversed. Orgnz says "this is what I want"; Vndr says "this is what I make." Same data structure (mood_boards + mood_board_items), same upload pipeline, same color extraction, same RLS scope. Reduces feature count by one whole portfolio component; lets §47 Upgrade 5 (vision API matching) serve both populations from one infrastructure when it lands. NEW pattern — Owned-only enforcement, three layers. (1) URL paste blocklist matching against 25+ known stock and social-media domains (Pinterest, Instagram, Facebook, TikTok, Unsplash, Pexels, Pixabay, Shutterstock, Getty, iStock, Adobe Stock, Flickr, 500px, Behance, Dribbble, Tumblr, Reddit, Imgur, Google, Bing). (2) Own-domain check against website field with confirmation prompt on mismatch (not hard block — legitimate Squarespace-subdomain cases exist). (3) Affirmative attestation checkbox revealed after first upload, same documented-consent-at-point-of-risk pattern as SafeTab waiver (§67). The rationale beyond legality: borrowed work poisons the matching algorithm. Cleaner training data → smarter Cue → better matches → higher conversion. NEW pattern — four-dimension match fingerprint. Color alone is a degraded signal — two florists can both have coral-and-cream palettes with opposite styles. Cue therefore reads four dimensions in parallel: Color DNA (hue/saturation/range), Style fingerprint (loose vs tight, ornate vs minimal), Value & light (high-key vs low-key, atmosphere), Composition (symmetric vs asymmetric, dense vs sparse). Surfaced back to the Vndr in the Signature Board UI as a transparency move, with a "Tell us what's true" correction affordance. Production implementation calls §47 Upgrade 5 vision API batch matching; v1 prototype uses heuristic readouts from canvas-sampled RGB and luminance. Same four UI panels stay; only the data source swaps. NEW pattern — the "one glance" pricing rule. An earlier draft of the Vndr landing showed commission as a 3-tier table (5%/4%/3% Free vs 3%/3%/2% Pro across booking sizes) plus a separate 2.5% platform fee. Technically accurate, human-unreadable for the artistic population the Vndr portal targets. Replaced with a single take-home calculator: one slider, one big take-home number, two columns showing Free vs Pro, one delta line showing Pro savings and break-even. The headline reads "For every $5,000 you book, you keep $4,488" — and slides as the user moves the input. This rule generalizes to all portals: if it requires a table to explain what someone pays, the table is the bug. Lead with take-home; let the calculator handle exploration. Applies to Orgnz event-cost view, Plnr commission view, Venu booking-net view, Catr post-surcharge margin view. NEW pattern — qualification badges as conversion edge. Inquiries arrive in the Vndr inbox with their qualification status visible: Ready to book (Venu confirmed + signed Venu contract + vendor escrow funded) or Browsing only (Venu pending or no escrow). Surfacing this multiplicity lets Vndrs respond to real leads first — the conversion edge over WeddingWire, The Knot, Thumbtack. The same escrow dollars are read three ways: Orgnz reads as shopping power, Venu reads as qualified intent, Vndr reads as confirmed-event signal. What's open. Vndr CRM, full booking management, calendar / availability blocking UI beyond the mini calendar, reviews UI, payout tracking detail view — all deferred until first 50 booked events generate real usage data. What's not changing. §19 pricing tiers, §3 platform commission rate table, §36 cert tracking model, §47 mood board upgrades roadmap. Cover badge: v26.4→v26.5.
26.4May 2026Financial integrity, legal, and architecture pass — all audit items resolved at code level. NEW §55.5 — Event wallet model. Parallel funding architecture for events above $10K threshold (configurable). Orgnz pre-funds a wallet via one or more contributions; vendors are booked against the wallet at confirmation time. Multi-funder support — Orgnz generates a "Contribute to this event" payment link for family, sponsors, or anyone funding the event without requiring a platform account. New tables (Slice B): event_wallets and wallet_funding_events. New field on bookings: funding_source enum(wallet|direct_charge) for backward compat with deposit/balance flow. Wallet model is Slice B; deposit/balance remains for Slice A. Both flows coexist permanently. Cancellation rule canonicalized. Replaces three contradictory rules with single canonical: deposit forfeited per vendor policy, vendor can offer override (binding once recorded, 72-hour Orgnz acceptance window), 5% cancellation processing fee retained by EvntCue from forfeited amount, Stripe + 2.5% non-refundable. Force majeure exception: held escrow returns to wallet, no 5% fee, Stripe + 2.5% still non-refundable. Force majeure narrowly defined (NWS advisory, government order, declared public health emergency, war/terrorism, venue catastrophic loss) with explicit exclusions and 72-hour vendor response window with default-Orgnz on non-response. Platform fee structure clarified. 2.5% applied at booking confirmation against booking value. Earned at the moment EvntCue does the matching/contracting/escrow setup work — non-refundable on cancellation. Stripe processing (2.9% + $0.30) is NOT a commission_flow — it's vendor expense on EvntCue's P&L, shown separately on receipts. The stripe_processing enum value referenced in v25 audit is removed. Sales tax marketplace facilitator posture. Replaces "advisory only" with active collection model. Texas Tax Code §151.0242 and equivalent statutes in 30+ states make EvntCue a marketplace facilitator with collection and remittance obligations. Stripe Tax integration mandatory before live transactions. Co-Plnr no-double-dip rule. 2.5% applies once at original Orgnz charge. Internal Plnr-to-Plnr settlements (co_plnr_split, lead-to-co referral) do not incur a second platform fee. New flag commission_flows.is_internal_settlement with CHECK constraint forcing all co_plnr_split rows to TRUE. 1099-K threshold made admin-configurable. Hardcoded $600 federal threshold replaced with platform_settings.form_1099k_threshold_federal_cents, form_1099k_threshold_year, form_1099k_state_overrides JSONB. TABC advisory copy rewritten. "May be subject to" hedging replaced with direct statement of obligations: TABC-permitted businesses owe MBGRT (6.7% on permittee gross receipts) and MBST (8.25% itemized to customer). Both Comptroller forms named. SafeTab marketing language constrained. "Defense is valid" claim replaced with "creates evidentiary record" framing. Explicit non-warranty added. NEW platform_copy table. Versioned legal/advisory copy with attorney_reviewed flag, jurisdiction tagging, supersession via effective_until, partial unique index for one-active-per-key. Helper functions upsert_platform_copy() and mark_copy_reviewed(). Rounding standardization. New canonical calc_fee_cents(basis_cents, rate_pct) with explicit half-up via FLOOR(x + 0.5). IMMUTABLE + PARALLEL SAFE. All inline ROUND() calls migrate to this function. Subtraction-based split for §66.1 EvntCue/Plnr shares guarantees no rounding drift. Nightly verify_fee_reconciliation() with $1 absolute drift threshold. Wrapper functions: compute_marketplace_fee_split_tiered() handles Listed/Pro tier rates atomically. Tests live in separate file 013_rounding_tests.sql. RLS SECURITY DEFINER pattern established. RLS on commission_flows hardened: no direct writes from any role, reads explicitly exclude Orgnz (§08 commission-blind enforced at DB layer). All cross-RLS operations route through SECURITY DEFINER functions with fail-closed auth checks. Functions: cancel_booking() (owning Orgnz/admin only, row-locked, handles standard + force majeure), amend_cancellation() (admin override path), offer_partial_refund() (vendor only, idempotent — rejects re-offers), release_escrow_dual_confirm() (either party records, both required, race-free via FOR UPDATE). Helper functions current_tenant_id() and current_role_claim() fail-closed on missing JWT (no NULL bypass). Forward-dependency stub return_escrow_to_wallet() routes force-majeure refunds to pending_manual_refunds table until wallet model ships. Migrations 013, 014, 015 — production-grade. All additive. 013 = rounding standardization (calc_fee_cents + wrappers + reconciliation, schema-qualified, IMMUTABLE flags correct). 014 = RLS SECURITY DEFINER pattern (cancel_booking, amend_cancellation, offer_partial_refund, release_escrow_dual_confirm + RLS lockdown + schema introspection at sections 0c/0d that aborts cleanly if columns don't match). 015 = copy fixes + double-dip flag + bookings_with_alcohol_tax view (no STORED generated columns to avoid table rewrite + function-coupling lock-in). Strict ordering: 013 must run first because 014 and 015 reference calc_fee_cents. All explicit BEGIN/COMMIT removed (would break Supabase migration runner's outer transaction). Existing 12 migrations untouched. Tests in 013_rounding_tests.sql — 22 assertions verifying rounding, edge cases, §66.1 splits, all pass. Schema introspection in 014 verifies live schema before functions deploy — aborts with clear error if mismatch. Bug count progression: first draft 16 bugs caught in self-audit; second pass 0 bugs. 26.3Apr 2026Hybrid model refinement + Venue UI spec added. §66.1 fee rate change: EvntCue residual on Plnr-mediated post-hire events reduced from 2% to 1.5%. This gives Pro Plnrs an even stronger value proposition (Plnr earns 6.5% on Listed Vndr bookings instead of 6%; 4.5% on Pro Vndr bookings instead of 4%). §66.1 Solo gate change — Option B replaces Option A: the "1 active event at a time" cap on Plnr Solo is removed. Solo Plnrs can now run unlimited events. The new Solo gate is structural — Solo Plnrs earn 50% of the post-hire marketplace-fee share and 50% of post-hire Vndr/Venue referrals, with the other 50% going to EvntCue. Pro Plnrs earn 100% of both. New enum values on bookings.fee_split_mode: plnr_post_hire_pro and plnr_post_hire_solo replace v26.2's single plnr_post_hire. New schema field plnr_engagements.plnr_tier_at_hire enum(solo, pro) — frozen at engagement creation, used to route the booking computation. Anti-gaming rule: a Plnr cannot upgrade for one billing cycle to capture higher share retroactively on existing engagements; existing engagements keep their original tier; only new engagements pick up the new tier. Re-engagement flow with mutual Orgnz consent allows mid-event tier changes when scope legitimately grows. §66.1 worked example expanded from 3 columns to 4 — self-managed, post-hire Pro, post-hire Solo, pre-hire — showing $1,375 / $3,803 / $3,615 EvntCue earnings on a $40K wedding under each scenario. The Solo column actually nets EvntCue more than self-managed because Solo's 50/50 captures revenue from referrals that wouldn't exist without a Plnr at all. DFW revenue model recomputed: at 50 events/month with 60% Plnr-mediated mix (70% of those Pro, 30% Solo), v26.3 hybrid earns ~$112K/month versus v26.2's ~$107K and pure §66's ~$118K. The 1.5% residual is more generous to Pro Plnrs than v26.2's 2%; the Solo gate recovers most of that concession from Plnrs who haven't yet upgraded. §19 Plnr tier matrix updated: Solo no longer capped at "1 active event at a time" — now reads "Unlimited" with the commission share row showing 50/50 split. New row: "Vndr/Venue referral share (post-hire)" — 50% Solo / 100% Pro. Solo → Pro upgrade math added: on a typical $40K event, upgrade adds ~$2,400 in earnings; Pro pays back in the first event of the month for any active Plnr. §08 cross-reference updated with new 1.5% residual. 26.2Apr 2026Hybrid commission model added — one new section, one re-tiered table, two cross-references. New §66.1 — Hybrid commission model: the marketplace fee rate now varies by whether a Plnr is engaged on the event. Self-managed events (no Plnr) keep the full 8%/6% marketplace fee per §13. Plnr-mediated events (post-hire) drop the marketplace fee through to the Plnr — EvntCue retains a 2% residual to cover platform infrastructure. Plnr-mediated pre-hire bookings split the marketplace fee 50/50 between EvntCue and Plnr, matching §66's existing pre-hire rule for the Vndr referral slider. Trigger field: events.plnr_engagement_id (already exists, no new schema for the trigger itself). New schema fields: bookings.fee_split_mode enum(self_managed, plnr_pre_hire, plnr_post_hire) and commission_flows.fee_split_mode mirror, both computed at booking confirmation and frozen. Worked example on a $40K wedding shows EvntCue earns $3,000 self-managed, $1,500 post-hire Plnr, $3,615 pre-hire Plnr (the pre-hire mode actually nets EvntCue more than self-managed because the 50/50 splits on Vndr and venue referrals add new revenue streams). DFW-scale revenue model recomputed: at 50 events/month with 60% Plnr-mediated mix, hybrid earns ~$107K/month versus pure §66's ~$118K/month — a 9% revenue concession in exchange for Plnrs as a strategic acquisition channel. §19 Plnr tier matrix re-tiered: Plnr Solo (free) now includes profile + Stripe Connect payment gateway + scheduling + 1 active event + commission intelligence on that event + marketplace-fee share per §66.1. Pro ($69/mo or $599/yr) unlocks the acquisition and scale tools: full CRM (§43), outbound proposals + e-signature (§43), Co-Plnr collaboration (§44), Plnr marketplace apply, run-of-show generator, post-event ROI report, disclosure manager, and unlimited events. Critical change: Solo Plnrs now earn marketplace-fee share on the events they mediate — the Pro subscription does not gate commission earnings, only the workflow tools that help a Plnr scale beyond solo work. Solo is positioned as a fully functional operating layer, not a trial. §08 cross-reference added: commission_flow type enum table now notes that platform_marketplace_fee rate splits per §66.1 on Plnr-mediated events. TOC updated: §66.1 added immediately after §66. Cover badge updated v26.1→v26.2. What's not in this version: the §66 vendor-upload passive referral mechanic remains Phase 2 (separate addendum, §66.2 when specced). Existing commission_flows rows are backfilled with fee_split_mode = 'self_managed' as default; no rate or recipient changes for any historical event. Migration is additive and non-destructive.

25.8Apr 2026SafeTab — responsible service waiver (§67): New section fully specced. SafeTab is a conditional alcohol service waiver system — legally binding digital consent checkpoint inserted between complimentary drink tickets and the cash bar. Two operating modes: event-linked (SMS to guest on EvntCue guest list, bartender screen confirms green) and walk-up/standalone (QR code, no EvntCue account required, works for any licensed establishment). Four legally binding elements documented: identity (DL hash), informed consent (attorney-reviewed versioned waiver text), affirmative action (typed legal name or WebAuthn biometric), immutable timestamp log (INSERT ONLY RLS — no UPDATE, no DELETE, ever). Five transport methods with system actions: rideshare, designated driver (names driver + logs driver SMS), hotel/on-site, taxi, other. Full schema: safetab_waivers table with 22 fields including guest_phone_hash, dl_hash, waiver_version, signed_name, drinks_after_waiver, waiver_token (JWT, 10-min expiry), biometric_confirmed. Portal touchpoints: Catr (primary, day-of bartender screen), Venue (can mandate as event requirement), Plnr (visibility only), Orgnz (post-event summary only). Cue integration: pre-event checklist prompt, day-of monitoring alert, post-event waiver summary card. Standalone SaaS model: SafeTab Free ($0, 50 waivers/mo) / SafeTab Bar ($49/mo) / SafeTab Enterprise ($149/mo). TAM: every TABC-licensed establishment in Texas (~55,000 licenses) and equivalent in 50 states. Launch sequence: Phase 0 attorney review (TX-1.0 waiver copy) → Phase 1 EvntCue Catr native → Phase 2 safetab.io standalone → Phase 3 Enterprise + API. Strategic note: SafeTab is a documented consent at the point of risk platform — drunk driving is the entry point, the architecture is reusable across any regulated transaction requiring documented risk acknowledgment. Cover chip updated. TOC updated to 67 sections. Vndr capacity model: concurrent_max INTEGER DEFAULT 1 added to tenants table. Booking conflict check updated to COUNT(active_bookings) ≥ concurrent_max. Vndr portal copy updated. Landing page v5 + mobile: Orgnz/Plnr positions swapped, Vndr dropped on mobile, logo mark removed from center, Cue pill repositioned.

17.0Apr 2026Three interconnected updates based on extended Plnr role research and design review of v16.0. §3 reverted and corrected: Commission rate table rebuilt as granular vendor types (40+ rows) with a new role_category display column. Architecture clarification added: role categories (Audio & Music Experience, Visual Production, etc.) are UI grouping labels only — the commission engine reads granular vndr_type per booking, never the role category. This corrects a fundamental architecture error introduced in v16.0 where role categories were incorrectly implied as commission buckets. A single event can have DJ + live band + ceremony string quartet as three separate bookings at three separate commission rates — collapsing them into one category bucket would have made that impossible to bill correctly. §9 updated: 10th Cue touchpoint added — Plnr recommendation gate.
