59 — Plnr hired mid-event — commission flow
Orgnz books vendors, then hires a Plnr. Here is exactly who earns what and when the line is drawn.
The hire date is the hard cutoff. Everything booked before the Plnr is hired belongs to the Orgnz-direct relationship. Everything booked after belongs to the Plnr-managed relationship. This line never moves retroactively and cannot be overridden without a formal booking reassignment (which requires vendor consent). EvntCue and Stripe earn their fees on every transaction regardless of which side of the line it falls on.
The rule in one sentence: Plnr earns referral commission only on vendor bookings they originate after their hire date. Pre-hire bookings are permanently Orgnz-direct. EvntCue earns 1% on every charge through the platform regardless. Stripe earns their processing fee on every charge regardless.

Phase 1 — Orgnz books vendors directly (no Plnr yet)

Orgnz uses Cue to find and book vendors themselves. Commission structure is identical to §58 — EvntCue 1% at each charge, Stripe processing fee at each charge, vendor commission dial at payout. No Plnr referral line exists because no Plnr is on the event.
PartyEarnsExample — Vendor A: $3,000
EvntCue1% of deposit + 1% of remaining$7.50 at deposit, $22.50 at final = $30.00
Stripe2.9%+$0.30 per charge$22.05 at deposit, $65.55 at final = $87.60
Vendor A (10% dial)Total minus dial$2,700.00 net payout
PlnrNothing — not hired yet$0.00

Phase 2 — Plnr hired, hire date recorded

Orgnz hires a Plnr through the platform. A plnr_engagements record is created with the exact hire timestamp. This timestamp is immutable — it is the permanent reference for every commission calculation on this event. The Plnr gains access to the full event record including pre-hire vendor bookings, which they can manage operationally. They cannot earn commission on those bookings.
The Plnr charges the Orgnz a service fee for their planning work (flat or percentage, set on their profile). This fee runs through EvntCue like any other booking — Stripe takes processing, EvntCue takes 1%, Plnr receives the rest.
PartyEarnsExample — Plnr fee: $3,500
EvntCue1% of Plnr service fee charge$35.00
Stripe2.9%+$0.30 on Plnr fee charge$101.80
PlnrFee minus Stripe and EvntCue cuts$3,363.20

Phase 3 — Plnr books vendors on behalf of Orgnz

All vendor bookings made after the hire timestamp route through the Plnr relationship. At payout the Plnr earns their referral rate on the total booking value. The vendor commission dial and the Plnr referral rate both deduct from the vendor’s payout — they stack. The vendor sees the full combined deduction percentage before accepting any inquiry routed through a Plnr.
PartyEarnsExample — Vendor C: $5,000, 10% dial, 8% Plnr referral
EvntCue1% of each charge + vendor dial commission$12.50 deposit fee + $37.50 final fee + $500.00 dial = $550.00
Stripe2.9%+$0.30 per charge$36.55 deposit + $109.05 final = $145.60
PlnrReferral rate on total booking value at payout$400.00 (8% of $5,000)
Vendor CTotal minus dial minus Plnr referral$4,100.00 net payout
Vendor disclosure rule: When a booking inquiry is routed through a Plnr, the vendor’s inquiry card must display: “This booking includes a [X]% Plnr referral fee. Combined with your [Y]% commission dial, [Z]% will be deducted from your payout.” Vendor must acknowledge this before the inquiry is sent. No surprises at payout. If combined deductions exceed 25%, a second confirmation step is required: “Your total deduction on this booking is [Z]%. Confirm you accept these terms.”

Pre-hire vendor reassignment — the rule

Vendors booked before the Plnr hire date are permanently Orgnz-direct. The Plnr manages them operationally — they appear on the event record, the Plnr can communicate with them, update their timeline slots, and coordinate day-of. But the commission structure on those bookings does not change. No reassignment mechanism exists by design. This protects vendors who accepted a booking without a Plnr commission in the terms, and eliminates any dispute about retroactive earnings.
If Orgnz wants Plnr to earn on pre-hire vendors: The only path is cancellation and rebooking through the Plnr after hire. This requires vendor consent to the new terms and restarts the booking flow. EvntCue does not provide a retroactive reassignment tool. This is intentional — ambiguity here is expensive.

Full event money flow — one event, all phases

Vendor A — $3,000 (10% dial)Orgnz direct$30 fees + $300 dial$87.60$0$2,700
Vendor B — $2,000 (10% dial)Orgnz direct$20 fees + $200 dial$58.30$0$1,800

Commission attribution logic at payout: IF bookings.plnr_engagement_id IS NULL → no Plnr referral, vendor_payout_cents = amount_cents - commission_amount_cents. IF bookings.plnr_engagement_id IS NOT NULL → calculate plnr_referral_amount_cents = ROUND(amount_cents × engagement.referral_pct / 100), vendor_payout_cents = amount_cents - commission_amount_cents - plnr_referral_amount_cents. Both paths insert rows into commission_flows. Atomic — all or nothing.
60 — Venue preferred vendors & Plnr waiver requests
Venues define who works in their space. Plnrs have a formal path to bring their own people.
Preferred vendor lists are a standard feature of real-world venue contracts. EvntCue formalizes this as a platform feature — venues set their preferences per space, Cue respects those preferences in its recommendations, and Plnrs have a structured waiver request flow rather than an awkward phone call. The waiver system protects venue relationships while giving Plnrs the professional tool they need.

Three tiers of venue preference

Required — exclusive
Venue contract mandates this vendor. No substitution permitted under any circumstance. Examples: in-house catering, proprietary AV system vendor, exclusive bar service. Cue does not surface other vendors in this category for this venue. The inquiry button routes only to the required vendor. No waiver option is shown — the UI does not offer it.
Preferred — waiver possible
Venue strongly recommends these vendors based on familiarity with the space, relationship history, or insurance requirements. Other vendors can be used but require a formal waiver. Cue surfaces preferred vendors first with a “Venue preferred” badge. Non-preferred vendors appear below with a “Waiver required” badge. The Plnr sees a “Request waiver” button on non-preferred vendor cards.
Suggested — open field
Soft recommendation only. Vendors who’ve worked the space before and the venue is happy to highlight. No waiver needed to use anyone else. Cue surfaces suggested vendors with a subtle “Works here often” badge. Any vendor bookable freely. This tier exists so venues can surface trusted partners without creating friction for Plnrs.

Venue preferred Plnrs

Venues can also maintain a preferred Plnr list — Plnrs they’ve worked with successfully and trust with their space. When an Orgnz browses venues, preferred Plnr names appear on the venue profile: “Planners who know this venue.” This is a discovery feature for Orgnzs and a credibility signal for Plnrs — not a restriction. Any Plnr can work any venue. Preferred status just surfaces them earlier in Orgnz searches for a Plnr.

Waiver request flow — step by step

1. Plnr selects non-preferred vendor
Plnr taps a vendor in a category where the venue has a Preferred vendor. System intercepts: “[Venue] prefers [Vendor X] for photography. You can request a waiver to use [Selected Vendor].” Two buttons: “Use preferred vendor” or “Request waiver.”
2. Plnr submits reason
Plnr selects a reason type (required field) and adds optional notes. Reason options: Client relationship, Budget constraint, Specialized requirement, Preferred vendor unavailable, Other. The reason is sent to the venue and stored permanently on the waiver record regardless of outcome.
3. Venue receives notification
Venue portal shows a waiver request card: event name, date, category, Plnr name, requested vendor, reason. Two actions: Accept or Decline (with optional note). 48-hour response window shown as a countdown. If no response within 48 hours, waiver auto-grants and both parties are notified.
4a. Venue accepts
Waiver status = granted. Plnr receives notification. Booking proceeds normally with the non-preferred vendor. The waiver record is attached to the booking permanently — visible to venue and Plnr, not to Orgnz unless they ask.
4b. Venue declines
Waiver status = declined. Plnr notified with venue’s reason. Plnr must choose the preferred vendor or escalate to Orgnz for a decision. No booking can proceed in this category until either a waiver is granted or a preferred vendor is selected.
4c. No response — auto-grant
If venue does not respond within 48 hours, waiver auto-grants. Status = auto_granted. Both parties notified. Venue silence = implicit approval. This protects Orgnz and Plnr timelines from being held hostage by venue inaction. Venues who consistently ignore waiver requests lose credibility signal in the platform.
Required tier has no waiver path. If a category is marked Required, the waiver request button does not exist in the UI. The only path to using a different vendor in a Required category is to renegotiate the venue booking terms directly — outside the platform. EvntCue does not mediate Required tier overrides. If an Orgnz insists on a non-required vendor in a Required category, they are in breach of their venue contract and that is between them and the venue.

Commission interaction with preferred vendors

Preferred vendor status does not change commission rates. A preferred vendor who has a commission dial set earns the same as any other vendor. A venue may have a separate kickback or referral arrangement with their preferred vendors — this is captured in commission_flows as venue_kickback or venue_fb_surcharge (already specced in §58). These internal arrangements are invisible to Orgnzs and Plnrs. A waiver vendor carries no commission penalty — the waiver is about the venue relationship, not the money.

Cue integration: When Cue generates vendor recommendations for a Plnr session, it receives the venue_space_id for the event. Cue’s system prompt includes the preference tier for each vendor category: “Required: [vendor list]. Preferred: [vendor list]. For any vendor not on the preferred list in a preferred category, append a waiver_required flag to the recommendation card.” Cue never recommends a non-required vendor in a Required category — that filter happens before the prompt, not inside it.
61 — EvntCue Live — gap specs
Three day-of features missing from §56. Required before Live ships.
§56 covers the Plnr operational layer completely. These three additions cover vendor-to-vendor communication, the guest-facing experience, and the automated post-event trigger chain that closes the loop between day-of execution and financial settlement.

Gap 1 — Vendor-to-vendor direct messaging

§56 gives the Plnr broadcast and direct message capability. What it doesn't give is vendor-to-vendor communication — and on a real event, vendors need to talk to each other. The florist needs to coordinate with the venue on setup timing. The photographer needs to know when the catering team is clearing tables. The AV vendor needs to sync with the DJ on soundcheck. Currently there is no structured path for this — they call each other's cell phones, which means the Plnr loses visibility and the event record loses the conversation.
Scoped messaging only
Vendors can only message other vendors confirmed on the same event. No cross-event visibility. No cold contact capability. The messaging channel opens when EvntCue Live activates (24 hours before event) and closes 4 hours after the event end time. Outside those windows, normal inquiry flow applies.
Plnr visibility
All vendor-to-vendor messages on a live event are visible to the Plnr in a read-only thread view. Plnr cannot be excluded from any day-of communication on their event. This is not surveillance — it is operational awareness. Message log is preserved on the event record permanently.
No Orgnz visibility
Vendor-to-vendor messages are not visible to the Orgnz. They are operational coordination, not client communication. The Orgnz sees vendor check-in status and timeline position — not the sausage being made. This keeps the Orgnz experience clean and confident.

Schema — vendor messaging

ColumnTypeNotes
live_vendor_messages
idUUID PK
event_idUUID FK events NOT NULL
sender_tenant_idUUID FK tenants NOT NULLSending vendor.
recipient_tenant_idUUID FK tenants nullableNULL = broadcast to all vendors on event. Set = direct to one vendor.

sent_atTIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
RLS: Sender reads own messages. Recipient reads messages addressed to them. Plnr reads ALL messages on their events. Orgnz reads none. Enforcement at the RLS layer — not just application layer.

Gap 2 — Guest-facing day-of experience

Guests need two things on event day: where to go, and where to sit. Currently EvntCue has no guest-facing interface at all — guests exist only as a count and a dietary flag. This gap closes that. The guest experience is deliberately minimal — a simple web app accessible via QR code or text link. No download required. No account needed.
Digital check-in
Guest scans QR code at venue entrance. Enters their name or confirmation code. System marks them as arrived. Plnr sees live headcount in real time. Catr sees confirmed vs expected covers update automatically — BEO headcount adjusts live. No paper list. No clipboard.
Seating lookup
After check-in, guest sees their table assignment and a simple venue map if the Orgnz uploaded one. No full seating chart exposed — just their table. Simple, fast, eliminates the seating board line at the entrance. Works offline on guest device once loaded.
Event timeline (public)
Optional. Orgnz can enable a simplified guest-facing timeline: "Ceremony begins at 5:00pm. Cocktail hour 5:30pm. Dinner 7:00pm." Plnr-controlled. If Plnr delays ceremony by 12 minutes, the guest timeline updates automatically — guests see "Ceremony begins at 5:12pm" without anyone making an announcement.

guest_timeline_enabledBOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSEOrgnz controls whether public guest timeline is shown.

Gap 3 — Post-event automated trigger chain

When EvntCue Live marks an event as completed, a chain of automated actions must fire in sequence. Currently none of this is specced. The trigger is the Plnr tapping "End event" or the system auto-completing when the event end time passes. Everything below happens automatically — no manual action required from any party.
Step 1 — Dual confirmation requests
Within 15 minutes of event completion: both Orgnz and each vendor receive a confirmation request. "Confirm service delivered?" One tap. This starts the 72-hour escrow release clock. If both confirm before 72 hours — instant payout. If neither confirms by 72 hours — auto-release fires. Logged to booking_status_log.
Step 2 — Memory page generated
Automatically created from existing event data. event_memory_pages row inserted. Slug generated from event name and date. Vendor credits populated from confirmed bookings. Orgnz notified: "Your event memory page is ready — share it or keep it private." Default is public. One tap to make private. No manual work required.
Step 3 — Review requests
24 hours after event completion: Orgnz receives review request for each confirmed vendor. Simple 5-star rating with optional note. Vendor trust scores update immediately on submission. Review requests expire after 14 days — past that window, no review can be submitted for that booking.
Step 4 — Cue debrief
Cue generates a post-event debrief from the issue log, timeline deviations, vendor check-in times, and any broadcast messages. Delivered to the Plnr only: "Here's what happened, here's what to watch for next time at this venue." Builds a personal institutional memory that lives in the Plnr portal.
Step 5 — Final packet
Full event record compiled and available for download: run-of-show as executed, vendor contact list, BEO, budget final, issue log (Plnr only), guest checkin report, message log. Cached locally for 90 days then archived. Orgnz and Plnr each get the version appropriate to their role.
Step 6 — Referral prompt
7 days after event: Orgnz receives a single referral prompt — not a marketing email, a personal message from Cue: "How did it go? If you know someone planning an event, your referral link gives them a free planning session with Cue." One send. Never repeated. No drip sequence. Respects the relationship.

Schema — post-event trigger chain

Table / fieldTypeNotes
live_events.completed_atTIMESTAMPTZ nullableSet when Plnr taps "End event" or system auto-completes. This is the master trigger timestamp for the entire chain.
live_events.trigger_chain_statusJSONB DEFAULT {}Tracks completion of each step: {confirmation_sent: bool, memory_page_created: bool, reviews_sent: bool, debrief_generated: bool, packet_ready: bool, referral_sent: bool}. Updated as each step completes. Idempotent — safe to re-run if a step fails.
post_event_referralsNew tableid, event_id, orgnz_tenant_id, referral_code, sent_at, clicked_at nullable, converted_at nullable. One row per event. Never sent twice.
Build priority: Gap 1 (vendor messaging) ships with EvntCue Live Phase 2. Gap 2 (guest check-in) ships in Phase 2 as a companion feature — it requires the RSVP system to be live first. Gap 3 (post-event chain) is the most important and should ship at the same time as EvntCue Live — without it, escrow release is manual and memory pages never get created. The trigger chain is what closes every loop the platform opens.
62 — Floor map, BEO, and room set specification
The three documents a Plnr lives by on event day. All live inside EvntCue.
These three documents are currently carried on paper, texted as photos, or emailed the morning of. EvntCue consolidates them into the event record, makes them available to every portal that needs them, and keeps them current. The floor map and BEO are pre-event documents. The room set checklist is a day-of operational tool that confirms the physical space matches what was contracted.

1 — Floor map

The Plnr uploads the venue’s existing floor plan as a PNG or PDF. This is V1 — an annotation layer on top of an existing image, not a drag-and-drop room builder. The Plnr adds labels: table numbers, station names, zone labels (ceremony, cocktail, reception, service). The underlying furniture positions are fixed — they reflect what the venue actually has. Labels can be edited at any time before the event. On event day the map is read-only.
Upload + annotate
Plnr uploads venue floor plan (PNG or PDF, max 20MB). Browser renders it as a base layer. Plnr taps any point to place a label: table number, station type, zone name. Labels are stored as coordinate + text pairs relative to image dimensions — they scale correctly on any screen size. Labels are color-coded by type: guest tables (rose), service stations (teal), beverage (gold), ceremony (slate).
Portal visibility
All portals confirmed on the event see the same floor map. Catr sees it to plan their service flow. Venue uses it to confirm furniture placement matches contract. Vndr sees it to know where to place decor and florals. Orgnz sees it to understand the room layout. Nobody can edit the Plnr’s labels except the Plnr. Admin can always edit.
V3 room builder
Future version: drag-and-drop furniture from a library (rounds, rectangles, high tops, stages, dance floors) onto a blank canvas. Plnr builds the room from scratch, exports as PDF, shares with venue. Requires significant front-end investment. Not V1 or V2 — but the data model supports it from day one because labels are coordinate-based, not static.

Floor map schema

event_floor_maps

plnr_tenant_idUUID FK tenants NOT NULLPlnr who uploaded.
file_urlTEXT NOT NULLSupabase Storage URL. PNG or PDF.
file_typeENUM(png, pdf) NOT NULL
width_pxINTEGER NOT NULLOriginal image dimensions for coordinate scaling.
height_pxINTEGER NOT NULL

created_atTIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
floor_map_labels
idUUID PK
map_idUUID FK event_floor_maps NOT NULL
label_textTEXT NOT NULLe.g. "Table 14", "Buffet 1", "Bar A", "Ceremony Zone"
label_typeENUM(guest_table, buffet, beverage, dessert, condiment, ceremony, service, bar, stage, other) NOT NULLControls color coding on render.
x_pctNUMERIC(6,4) NOT NULLX position as percentage of image width (0.0–1.0). Scales to any screen.
y_pctNUMERIC(6,4) NOT NULLY position as percentage of image height.
created_atTIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()

2 — BEO (Banquet Event Order)

The BEO is the pre-service reference document. It lists what was contracted and confirmed. It is not the minute-by-minute run of show — that lives separately. The BEO answers: what tables, what linens, how many covers, what menu, what times. Every Catr, Venue, and Plnr on the event has access. Orgnz has read-only access. The BEO is generated automatically from confirmed booking data and the Plnr edits it to finalize. It is locked 48 hours before the event — no changes after that without admin override.
BEO contents — auto-populated
Event name · date · venue · event type
Cover count (confirmed guests from RSVP)
Dietary breakdown (vegan, GF, allergy flags by count)
Table types and counts (see linen summary below)
Linen colors and styles per table type
Menu — courses, items, service style (plated/buffet/family)
Service timeline — first course time, entrée time, dessert time
Bar service — type, open/close times, TABC confirmation
Kitchen notes — prep flags, timing sensitivities
Catr contact + lead server name
Plnr contact
Linen summary — by type not by table
Confirmed as a summary per station/table type:

2 buffet tables × 8ft rectangular — black skirted
50 guest rounds × 132" — ivory box pleat
4 beverage stations × 6ft — white tablecloth clipped
2 dessert stations × 6ft — blush skirted
2 condiment stations × 4ft — black tablecloth
1 head table × 8ft rectangular — ivory skirted

This is the Plnr’s confirmation checklist when the rental delivery arrives. One glance against the BEO confirms if anything was shorted before dressing begins.

BEO schema additions

ColumnTypeNotes
event_beo
idUUID PK
event_idUUID FK events UNIQUE NOT NULLOne BEO per event.
cover_countINTEGER NOT NULLConfirmed covers from RSVP system at BEO lock time.
dietary_summaryJSONB{vegan: 2, gluten_free: 5, allergy: 7, other: [...]}
table_summaryJSONBArray of {type, count, size, linen_color, linen_style}
menuJSONBArray of {course, items[], service_style, timing_notes}
service_timelineJSONBArray of {label, time} — first course, entrée, dessert, etc.
bar_serviceJSONB{type, open_time, close_time, tabc_confirmed: bool}
kitchen_notesTEXT nullableFree text. Plnr-edited.
locked_atTIMESTAMPTZ nullableSet 48 hours before event. No edits after this without admin override.
locked_byUUID FK users nullable
last_edited_atTIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()

3 — Room set sequence and dry set safety check

The room set sequence is the Plnr’s day-of operational checklist. It follows a strict physical order because each phase depends on the previous one being correct. You cannot dress a table that isn’t placed correctly. You cannot run a safety check through a room that isn’t fully dry set. The sequence is enforced in the UI — each phase is locked until the previous one is confirmed complete.
Phase 1 — Furniture placement
All furniture confirmed placed, spaced, and squared to the room. Buffet tables, guest tables, high tops, beverage stations, service stations, condiment stations, dessert stations, guest check-in tables, head table, cake table, gift table. Spacing between tables confirmed (minimum 60" for ADA). Furniture squared to room walls — not eyeballed, measured or laser-leveled. This phase is confirmed by the Plnr with a photo or a tap. No dressing begins until this is done.
Phase 2 — Linen
Tablecloths applied per BEO linen summary. Size confirmed per table type (132" on a 60" round, 90"×156" on an 8ft rectangle). Clips applied. Skirting, box pleat, or alternate covering applied per contract. Linen summary ticked against physical count — if a size is wrong or missing, it surfaces here before the room is half-dressed. Plnr confirms each table type complete, not each individual table.
Phase 3 — Equipment placement
Chaffers, heat lamps, decor, centerpieces, silverware, glassware, rental equipment placed per floor map. Equipment rental checklist ticked as each item is confirmed on site. If rental delivery is shorted an item it surfaces here. Heat lamps placed and confirmed minimum 18" clearance from any linen. This is the last phase before dry set safety check.
Phase 4 — Dry set safety check
Room is fully set, no food out. Plnr walks the room and confirms: all aisles minimum 60" wide (ADA), no trip hazards (cables taped, no exposed edges), all fire exits clear and unobstructed, emergency exit signage visible, AED location confirmed, heat lamp clearance from linens confirmed, bar area clear of obstructions, kitchen pass-through clear. This is the last checkpoint before vendors begin final dressing and food comes out.

Equipment rental checklist schema

ColumnTypeNotes
equipment_rental_items
idUUID PK
event_idUUID FK events NOT NULL
vndr_tenant_idUUID FK tenants nullableRental company if a registered vendor. NULL if external.
item_nameTEXT NOT NULLe.g. "Full-size chaffer", "Heat lamp", "Cocktail round high top"
categoryENUM(chaffer, heat_lamp, linen, tabletop, furniture, decor, av, bar, other)
quantity_contractedINTEGER NOT NULLWhat was ordered.
quantity_receivedINTEGER nullableWhat actually arrived. Set by Plnr on delivery confirmation.
confirmed_on_siteBOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSEPlnr tap to confirm item is placed and accounted for.
shortage_noteTEXT nullableSet if quantity_received < quantity_contracted. Logged to issue log automatically.
confirmed_atTIMESTAMPTZ nullable
The dry set moment is the most important checkpoint in the entire event day. No food is out. Every piece of equipment is in place. The room looks exactly as it will look when guests walk in minus the food. This is the moment to find every problem — a table in the wrong place, a linen the wrong size, a heat lamp too close to a tablecloth, a fire exit blocked by a service cart. After this moment, changes become exponentially harder. The UI should reflect this: the dry set safety check is the last locked gate before the live event phase opens.
63 — EvntCue Live Comm — phone as day-of communication device
No walkie-talkies. No group texts. One channel, built into the platform.
Every confirmed vendor and the Plnr carries a phone. EvntCue Live Comm turns those phones into a coordinated communication system scoped to the event, logged to the event record, and closed when the event ends. No external apps. No WhatsApp threads that disappear. No radio batteries to die.

Option A — Voice messages (Phase 2)

Hold to talk
One persistent button at the bottom of the Plnr day-of dashboard. Always visible regardless of which tab is active. Tap and hold to record a voice message. Release to send. A dropdown to the left selects the recipient: All vendors, Catr only, AV only, Photography, Florist, Venue, or any individual vendor confirmed on the event. Faster than typing in a loud room.
Talking indicator
While the Plnr is recording, a red "Talking" bar appears at the top of the screen with the recipient name and animated audio waveform. Recipients see a push notification with the audio message. They tap to listen, tap to reply. Every message is timestamped and logged to the event record permanently.
Text fallback
Text input sits alongside the hold-to-talk button. Same recipient dropdown. Same logging. Some environments are too loud for voice playback — text is always available as an alternative. SMS fallback fires automatically if a vendor has lost app connectivity.

Option B — Live audio channel (Phase 3)

Plnr-initiated channel
Plnr opens a live audio room from the dashboard. All confirmed vendors on the event receive a push notification: "Plnr has opened a live channel — tap to join." Vendors join voluntarily. The Plnr can speak to all joined vendors simultaneously. Functions like a walkie-talkie system but through the app. Built on WebRTC — no third-party service required.
Sub-channels
Plnr can break into sub-channels: Catr channel (Plnr + Catr lead only), AV channel, all-hands. Useful for service timing calls that don't need to involve every vendor. Vendors can only join channels the Plnr has opened — they cannot initiate a channel themselves. This keeps the Plnr in control of communication flow on the event.
Signal loss fallback
If a vendor loses app connectivity during the live channel, the system automatically sends them an SMS with the last message content. Venues with thick walls or basement spaces create dead zones — the fallback ensures no critical cue is missed. Offline bundle (cached run-of-show and vendor contacts) remains accessible regardless of connectivity.

Build order

Option A (voice messages) ships with EvntCue Live Phase 2 — it is an audio attachment on the existing message system and requires no new infrastructure beyond push notification delivery. Option B (live audio channel) is a Phase 3 feature requiring WebRTC implementation. The hold-to-talk button and recipient dropdown are present in the UI from day one — Option A populates them with voice messages, Option B upgrades them to a live channel without changing the interface.
Decision locked: Plnr-initiated only. Vendors can join a channel the Plnr opens, but cannot initiate one themselves. This keeps communication flow under Plnr control on event day. The Plnr is running the event — the communication system reflects that authority.
64 — Plnr day-of dashboard — full specification
Phone-first. One hand. Every decision a Plnr makes on event day, supported.
The Plnr day-of dashboard is a phone-optimized interface that activates with EvntCue Live 24 hours before the event. It is the single source of truth for the Plnr throughout the event day — from the moment they wake up and review event details, through load-in, room set, service, and strike. Five tabs, one persistent communication bar at the bottom, one always-visible countdown to guest-ready time.

Tab order — locked

Client · Vendors · BEO · Timeline · Issues. This order reflects actual Plnr priority on event day. The client relationship is first. Vendor coordination is second. The operational document (BEO) is third. The minute-by-minute flow is fourth. Problems are last — because issues are exceptions, not the primary workflow.

Tab 1 — Client

Contact client button
Always visible at the top of the Client tab. One tap opens a direct message to the Orgnz. Not buried in a menu. The client's name is shown: "Contact Garza." This is the fastest path to the person whose event this is. Available at all times regardless of event phase.
Client requests — by run of show position
Every client request organized by when it affects the event — not chronologically, not by category. Setup requests appear at the top. Requests tied to cocktail hour appear at that cue. Requests tied to toasts appear at that cue. Two types: Pre-event (blue tag, came in during planning) and Day-of (orange tag, received morning of). Each request has a checkmark the Plnr taps when addressed. Checked items strike through.
Client requests also appear inline on the Timeline tab at the exact cue they affect. The Plnr sees the peonies reminder when they reach cocktail hour in the timeline, the filet-only note when they reach entrée service. They don't have to remember — the system surfaces it at the right moment.

Tab 2 — Vendors

Vendor cards — tap to expand
Each confirmed vendor shows as a card with their check-in status dot (green/amber/red) and current status. Tapping a vendor expands their full briefing: role and responsibilities for this event, numbered set instructions, numbered strike instructions, and a direct message button. Set and strike instructions are defined by the Plnr or EvntCue using standard category templates, then customized for the specific event. The vendor sees their final instructions — not the template history.
Final walkthrough confirmation
Sits at the bottom of the Vendors tab. After the dry set safety check is complete, the Plnr sends a timestamped walkthrough confirmation. Always goes to the Orgnz. Plnr optionally copies the venue coordinator and/or Catr lead. Optional photo attachment. The message reads: "[Orgnz name] — your Plnr has completed the final walkthrough. The room is set, all vendors are in place. Your event is ready." Timestamped. Lives permanently on the event record.

Tab 3 — BEO

Cover count with batch notification
Plus and minus controls adjust the operational cover count. Changes batch — the Plnr taps "Notify Catr" when ready, not on every individual change. The notification shows the delta from the confirmed count (e.g. "−3 from confirmed 247"). Catr receives the updated count with a timestamp. The financial record does not move. The BEO updates. The kitchen knows. This is purely operational — it exists because guests no-show and unexpected plus-ones walk in.
Menu in service order
Menu courses ordered by service time per the run of show — not by course number, not alphabetically. Whatever is happening next is at the top. During cocktail hour, passed apps are front and center. When first course loads, it moves to the top. Each course card shows the service time and allergen flags at a glance. Tapping a course expands the full dish list with allergens.
Allergens per dish — big and obvious
When a guest asks "does this have nuts?" the Plnr opens the course and sees the answer in two seconds without calling the kitchen. Allergens are displayed as large colored flags per dish: red for severe (TREE NUTS, SHELLFISH), orange for gluten, purple for dairy, teal for shellfish, gold for soy. Safe dishes show a green "No major allergens" confirmation. Guest counts per allergen are shown. Pre-plated special dishes are identified and labeled. The Plnr answers confidently. No radio call. No running to the kitchen.

Tab 4 — Timeline

Single scrolling flow from load-in through venue clear. Everything above the current position is done. The current cue is highlighted in rose. Everything below is coming. Tapping a cue card opens a drill-down checklist for that phase. Client requests appear inline at each relevant cue. Ripple adjustments appear as orange banners when the Plnr marks a delay.
Timeline drill-downs
7:00A Load-in: vendor arrivals + equipment rental delivery checklist (qty contracted vs received, shortage flagged). 9:00A Furniture: placement, spacing, squared to room, client-specific positioning noted. 10:00A Linen: summary by type — counts, sizes, styles confirmed. 11:00A Equipment: chaffers, heat lamps (18" clearance), centerpieces, silverware placed. 12:00P Dry set safety: ADA aisles, trip hazards, fire exits, AED, heat lamp clearance, kitchen pass-through, Plnr sign-off. Each drill-down opens inline below the cue card and closes with the X button.
Ripple alerts
When the Plnr marks a delay, a ripple alert banner appears at the top of the Timeline tab showing what shifted and by how much. All downstream vendor cue times adjust automatically. All affected vendors receive personalized push notifications. The Plnr acknowledges the ripple and the banner dismisses. The adjusted times show inline on each affected cue in orange.

Tab 5 — Issues

Each open issue shows with timestamp, description, and smart routing suggestion based on issue category. Florist issue → suggests Florist. Catering issue → suggests Catr. AV issue → suggests AV. Venue/space issue → suggests Venue. Rental shortage → suggests Rental Co. Plnr always has the option to override and message anyone. "Log issue" creates the record. "Log + message" creates the record and opens the message in one tap. Resolved issues show the response and can be cleared.

Persistent bottom bar

Always visible regardless of active tab. Three elements: recipient dropdown (All vendors / individual vendor), hold-to-talk button (54px circle, center), text input + send button. Hold the button and speak — release to send. The talking bar appears at the top of the screen while transmitting. The recipient dropdown controls who receives both voice messages and text messages. This bar does not disappear when the Plnr scrolls, changes tabs, or opens a drill-down.

Vendor set and strike instructions — data model

EvntCue maintains standard instruction templates per vendor category (AV, Catr, Florals, Photography, Venue, Rental). Each template contains a numbered list of standard set and strike steps for that category. When a Plnr creates a booking, the template pre-populates. The Plnr customizes for the specific event — adds event-specific notes, adjusts timing, removes inapplicable steps. The vendor sees only the finalized instructions, not the template. Both EvntCue and the Plnr can define and edit these instructions. Instructions are locked 24 hours before the event when EvntCue Live activates.
Table / fieldTypeNotes
vendor_event_instructions
idUUID PK
event_idUUID FK events NOT NULL
booking_idUUID FK bookings NOT NULLTies instructions to a specific vendor booking on this event.
vndr_tenant_idUUID FK tenants NOT NULL
role_summaryTEXT NOT NULLPlain text description of this vendor's role and responsibilities on this event.
set_instructionsJSONB NOT NULLArray of {step: int, instruction: text}. Numbered list. Plnr-editable.
strike_instructionsJSONB NOT NULLArray of {step: int, instruction: text}.
template_categoryENUM(av, catr, florals, photography, venue, rental, other)Which standard template was used as the base.
locked_atTIMESTAMPTZ nullableSet when EvntCue Live activates. No edits after this.
created_byUUID FK users NOT NULLPlnr or EvntCue admin who created or last edited.
updated_atTIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()

Menu allergen data model

The allergen display is a safety feature, not a convenience feature. A guest with a severe nut allergy who receives the wrong plate because the Plnr couldn't find the information fast enough is a liability event. The BEO allergen display must be readable in a loud room at 7PM with ambient lighting — large flags, high contrast, instant answer. This is non-negotiable in the UI spec.
65 — Landing page — full specification v2
The planning clock that builds itself. Three layers of drill-down before a single form field.
The landing page is EvntCue's first impression and its primary acquisition tool. It does not lead with a signup form. It leads with an experience — a planning clock that animates based on the specific event type and date the visitor selects. By the time the email gate opens, the visitor has already seen their personalized planning timeline. They are not signing up for a product. They are claiming a plan Cue already built for them.
Live file: evntcue-landing-drilldown.html — deployed to Vercel. Source at jasoncorbin506-maker/EvntCue.

Layer 1 — Category selection

Six category pills displayed in the hero section. Each pill has a color-coded dot and label. Categories: Love & Weddings (#D4778A rose), Cultural (#8b5cf6 violet), Celebrate (#f97316 orange), Corporate (#14b8a6 teal), Social & Formal (#C9A96E gold), Life Moments (#506898 slate). Selecting a category reveals Layer 2 beneath the hero.

Layer 2 — Event type selection

Eight specific event types per category slide open in a tray below the category pills. Examples: Love & Weddings → Wedding, Elopement, Vow Renewal, Engagement Party, Bridal Shower, Rehearsal Dinner, Destination Wedding, Mexican-American Wedding. Cultural → Quinceañera, Bar Mitzvah, Bat Mitzvah, Diwali Celebration, Eid Gathering, Lunar New Year, Holi Festival, Cultural Heritage Gala. Each category has 8 event types tailored to that category. Selecting an event type reveals the clock section.

Layer 3 — Date selection and urgency engine

Six date tiles appear inside the clock section: 7 days, 1 month, 3 months, 6 months, 12 months, 12+ months. Selecting a tile fires the urgency engine and animates the planning clock. The urgency level determines everything: badge color, clock hand color, milestone language, CTA copy, and email gate messaging.
Urgency levels
12+ months → calm (teal) · badge: "Plenty of time" · milestones: full planning arc

3–6 months → soon (gold) · badge: "Moving fast" · milestones: accelerated, some urgency

1 month → urgent (orange) · badge: "Move now" · pulsing animation · milestones: emergency compressed

7 days → critical (red) · badge: "Emergency mode" · rapid animation · CTA: "Get emergency help from Cue now" · email gate: "Your emergency plan is being assembled"
Clock animation
Canvas-rendered circular timeline. 8–9 milestone dots arranged around the clock face. The hand sweeps from 12 o'clock position clockwise, lighting each milestone dot as it passes. The "Today" marker is highlighted with a glow ring. Hand color matches urgency level. Labels appear outside the ring — abbreviated to fit. Milestones are event-type specific: a Quinceañera clock looks different from a Corporate Event clock.

Milestone sets — by urgency and event type

Each urgency level has milestone templates per event category: Wedding/cultural celebration, Corporate, Celebrate (birthday/shower/graduation), Cultural (religious observance), Social/Formal (gala/fundraiser), Life Moments (celebration of life/reunion). The milestone language shifts with urgency — "Book venue" at 12 months becomes "Venue — book now" at 3 months becomes "Venue — TODAY 🔥" at 1 month becomes "Call Cue — emergency 🚨" at 7 days. The sub-label under each milestone also shifts: "Mo 2–3" at calm becomes "This week" at soon becomes "Today" at urgent becomes "Immediately" at critical.

Info capture — guest count and budget

After the clock animation completes, the info capture section slides open. Guest count chips: Under 50, 50–100, 100–250, 250–500, 500+. Budget slider: logarithmic scale from $1K to $500K+. Default position: $45,000 (DFW avg $40,129 × 1.12). Slider fill color matches the current urgency level. Preview bar assembles the visitor's selections as colored chips: event type (rose), guest count (teal), date (gold), budget (violet).

CTA and email gate

CTA button unlocks when all three inputs are complete: event type selected, date selected, guest count selected. Button copy and color adapt to urgency: calm = rose "Build my planning timeline with Cue", urgent = orange "⚡ Build my urgent timeline with Cue", critical = red pulsing "🚨 Get emergency help from Cue now". Tapping the CTA opens the email gate inline. Email submitted → landing_capture_sessions row created with event_type, guest_count, date_horizon, budget_estimate, email, urgency_level, created_at. Session expires in 2 hours. Auth flow consumes session and pre-fills new event record.

Portal strip

Below the clock section, four portal cards: Plnr (teal pentagon constellation), Catr (gold triangle constellation), Vndr (orange fork constellation), Venue (blue arch constellation). Each routes to supply-side onboarding. Glossary bar at the bottom: Orgnz=organizer · Plnr=planner · Vndr=vendor · Catr=caterer · Venue=venue. Always visible.
66 — Commission flow — final locked model
Every dollar accounted for. Four scenarios.
This section supersedes §58 and §59 for commission-flow rules and is now the canonical source for Plnr pricing and the vendor commission slider cap. The commission model was revised after the initial spec to better respect Plnr economics. The founding intent: EvntCue earns fairly for the infrastructure it provides without cutting deeply into the professionals who make the platform valuable.
v26.1 reconciliation — propagated. Previous earlier sections (§08, §13, §19, §32) carried legacy values: Plnr Pro $79/mo monthly-only and a 0–25% vendor commission slider cap. These have been propagated to match §66: Plnr Pro is $69/mo or $599/yr, slider cap is 20%. §66 remains the canonical source — if §08, §13, §19, or §32 ever drift again, treat §66 as authoritative.

Platform fee

2.5% on every Orgnz charge — deposit and remaining balance. Applied at charge time, before escrow. This is EvntCue's primary revenue stream. It applies to all money movement through the platform regardless of whether a Plnr is on the event. The 2.5% rate is positioned well below the market average (Airbnb ~15%, Fiverr ~20%, marketplace avg ~5%) as a deliberate launch strategy. Year 2 target: raise to 3% once value is proven.

Stripe processing fees

2.9% + $0.30 per charge. Non-refundable. Applied on deposit charge and remaining balance charge separately. Stripe keeps their fee regardless of cancellation. This is disclosed to Orgnz at booking confirmation and is not negotiable.

Vendor commission dial

0–20% voluntary. Set by vendor before accepting any inquiry. Disclosed to vendor before accepting — no surprises at payout. Withheld at payout, not charged separately. This is EvntCue's secondary revenue stream and a placement signal: higher dial = better placement in Cue recommendations. Not collected on cancelled bookings.

Plnr subscription

$69/month flat. Annual option: ~$599/year (approximately 28% discount). Subscription gives the Plnr access to the full Plnr portal, commission intelligence, EvntCue Live Plnr dashboard, and passive referral tracking. The subscription is separate from and in addition to any referral commissions the Plnr earns.

Plnr commission rules — locked

Pre-hire vendors — 50/50 split
When an Orgnz books vendors before hiring a Plnr, those bookings have no Plnr engagement ID. When a Plnr is subsequently hired, the vendor dial commission on those pre-hire bookings is split 50/50 between EvntCue and the Plnr. The Plnr inherits and manages those vendor relationships — they earn something for that. EvntCue earns something for the platform bookings that already happened. This split is calculated at payout.
Post-hire vendors — Plnr keeps 100%
Any vendor booked after the Plnr's hire timestamp is a post-hire booking. The Plnr keeps 100% of their referral commission on post-hire bookings. EvntCue earns only the 2.5% platform fee on the Orgnz charge. The hire timestamp is immutable — it cannot be changed retroactively. bookings.plnr_engagement_id = NULL means no Plnr commission ever on that booking.

Plnr service fee

The Plnr's service fee to the Orgnz runs through the platform like any other booking. EvntCue earns 2.5% on that charge. Stripe takes their fee. The Plnr nets the remainder. This is the same platform fee that applies to all money movement — no special rate for Plnr service fees.

Co-Plnr — Option C locked

When a co-Plnr is added mid-event, the lead Plnr and co-Plnr negotiate their split directly via plnr_collab_agreements. EvntCue stays out entirely. EvntCue earns only the 2.5% platform fee on the co-Plnr's service fee charge — nothing from the referral split. This is the cleanest model: professionals negotiate with professionals, the platform facilitates without taxing the relationship.

Vendor upload passive referral Phase 2 — not in locked v1

When a Plnr uploads their preferred vendors into the EvntCue platform, those vendors become discoverable by Orgnzs who are booking without a Plnr. When one of those uploaded vendors gets booked independently through the platform, the Plnr who uploaded them earns a passive referral credit — even though they are not on that event. This is not a free month of subscription. It is: "Your vendors, your network, your passive income." The referral credit accrues and offsets future subscription payments or pays out monthly above a minimum threshold.
Status — open. The mechanic is committed in principle but the rules (credit %, payout threshold, accrual period, anti-gaming logic) are not yet specced. This is the only true open item in §66 and is moved to Phase 2 — it is not part of the locked v1 launch model. Final spec will be added in §66.1 after the supply-side onboarding metrics from §50 inform the credit %.

Cancellation fees

Orgnz cancels: EvntCue retains 5% of total booking value. Stripe keeps processing fees from all charges made. Remainder refunded to Orgnz. Vendor dial commission not collected — no payout, no withholding. Vendor cancels: EvntCue retains $0. Stripe keeps processing fees. Orgnz receives full refund minus only Stripe fees. Vendor trust score takes penalty. Late vendor cancellation (under 30 days to event) triggers escalated penalty and possible suspension review.

Annual subscription

$69/month × 12 = $828 full price. Annual at ~$599 is approximately 28% off. Paired with the passive referral mechanic, the annual commitment makes sense for active Plnrs who are uploading vendors and building their network on the platform. The passive income potential scales with time on the platform — annual subscribers benefit more.

Revenue model at DFW scale

At 50 events/month at DFW average spend of $40,129: platform fee generates ~$50,000/month. Vendor dial commission (avg 8%, 50/50 on pre-hire) adds ~$8,000/month. 20 active Plnr Pro subscriptions add $1,380/month. Total: ~$59,380/month. Infrastructure costs under $1,000/month early stage. First hire threshold: ~100 events/month (~$118K/month revenue). The 20-acre Texas farm with a house and some animals — achievable at approximately 0.2% of the DFW annual wedding market. Raise platform fee to 3% in year 2 — at that scale no vendor or Plnr will notice.
Founding intent — locked in the record. This platform was built to provide a comfortable life, not a yacht or a mansion. A 20-acre farm with a house and some animals. If it grows huge, most of the money goes to good people and charity work. That is the mission. Every pricing decision in this section flows from that intention — charge fairly, earn honestly, and don't cut into the professionals who make the platform worth using.
66.1 — Hybrid commission model · v26.2
Plnrs in the system without much penalty. Self-managed events fund the platform.
§66 sets the canonical commission rules. §66.1 adds a single architectural lever: the marketplace fee rate varies by whether a Plnr is engaged on the event. Self-managed events keep the full 8%/6% marketplace fee that funds the platform. Plnr-mediated events drop most of the marketplace fee through to the Plnr — EvntCue keeps a thin 1.5% residual to cover platform infrastructure on those events when a Pro Plnr is engaged. Solo Plnrs (free tier) earn half that share, with the other half flowing to EvntCue. The Vndr pays the same total either way. The Orgnz pays the same either way. Only the recipient of the marketplace fee changes.
Why this exists. Plnrs are the orchestrators of every event they touch. A platform that takes the same cut whether a Plnr does the work or not is a platform that taxes the relationship. The hybrid model makes Plnr engagement a strategic acquisition channel: every Plnr who signs up becomes a tax break for the Vndrs they bring in, while the platform's revenue from non-Plnr events stays intact. The trigger is a single field: events.plnr_engagement_id — nullable. Null means self-managed. Populated means Plnr-mediated.

The two modes — fee table

FlowSelf-managed eventPlnr-mediated · post-hire (Pro)Plnr-mediated · post-hire (Solo)Plnr-mediated · pre-hire
platform_fee (Orgnz charge)2.5%2.5%2.5%2.5%
platform_marketplace_fee · Vndr Listed (8% total)8% → EvntCue1.5% → EvntCue · 6.5% → Plnr4.75% → EvntCue · 3.25% → Plnr4% → EvntCue · 4% → Plnr (50/50)
platform_marketplace_fee · Vndr Pro (6% total)6% → EvntCue1.5% → EvntCue · 4.5% → Plnr3.75% → EvntCue · 2.25% → Plnr3% → EvntCue · 3% → Plnr (50/50)
vndr_referral (slider)Not collected (no Plnr to receive)100% → Plnr (per §66)50% → Plnr · 50% → EvntCue50% → EvntCue · 50% → Plnr
venue_referralNot collected (no Plnr to receive)100% → Plnr (per §66)50% → Plnr · 50% → EvntCue50% → EvntCue · 50% → Plnr
The Solo gate — v26.3 lock. Solo Plnrs (free tier) earn 50% of the post-hire marketplace-fee share and 50% of the post-hire vendor/venue referrals. The other 50% goes to EvntCue. This replaces v26.2's "1 active event" gate. Free Plnrs can run as many simultaneous events as they want — Solo is a real operating layer, not a trial. The penalty for staying free is structural: you earn half of what a Pro Plnr earns on the same event. The Pro upgrade ($69/mo) pays back in the first hour of the first event for any Plnr running >1 event/month. This is the single cleanest commission gate in the industry — no usage limits, no feature traps, just a straight 50/50 share split that resolves the moment the Plnr subscribes.
Pre-hire vs post-hire — the timestamp rule (from §66, extended). The 50/50 split rule that §66 established for the vndr_referral slider now extends to the marketplace fee. A booking is "pre-hire" if it was confirmed before events.plnr_engagement_id was populated. A booking is "post-hire" if confirmed after. The hire timestamp is immutable. Bookings stay in the bucket they were confirmed in — you cannot retroactively reclassify pre-hire bookings as post-hire by hiring a Plnr later. This is the same anti-gaming rule §66 already enforces; we just apply it to one more flow type.

Worked example — $40K wedding, four scenarios

BookingSelf-managedPlnr post-hire (Pro)Plnr post-hire (Solo)Plnr pre-hire
Orgnz spend$40,000$40,000$40,000$40,000
Platform fee (2.5%)$1,000 → EvntCue$1,000 → EvntCue$1,000 → EvntCue$1,000 → EvntCue
Marketplace fee on $25K Vndr spend (Listed avg 8%)$2,000 → EvntCue$375 EvntCue + $1,625 Plnr$1,188 EvntCue + $812 Plnr$1,000 EvntCue + $1,000 Plnr
Vndr referrals ($5K×15% + $20K×10%)$0 (no Plnr)$2,750 → Plnr$1,375 EvntCue + $1,375 Plnr$1,375 EvntCue + $1,375 Plnr
Venue referral ($4,800×10%)$0 (no Plnr)$480 → Plnr$240 EvntCue + $240 Plnr$240 EvntCue + $240 Plnr
EvntCue total$3,000$1,375$3,803$3,615
Plnr commission earnings$0$4,855$2,427$2,615
Read the four columns: self-managed is EvntCue-only (no Plnr to share with). Plnr post-hire Pro is the giveaway — EvntCue earns the least ($1,375), Plnr earns the most ($4,855), the platform is functioning as a Plnr-friendly system at full strength. Plnr post-hire Solo is the gentle gate — EvntCue actually earns more here ($3,803) than in any other column because the Solo split funnels half the marketplace and referral revenue back. The Solo Plnr still earns $2,427 on this event with zero subscription cost — half of Pro, but more than $0. Pre-hire is the timing rule from §66 — bookings confirmed before the Plnr was hired split 50/50 regardless of Plnr tier, because at confirmation time there was no Plnr to pay the full share to.
The Solo → Pro upgrade math, made concrete. A Solo Plnr running this exact wedding earns $2,427. The same wedding under Pro earns $4,855 — a $2,428 delta. The Pro subscription costs $69/month or $599/year. Upgrading recovers its annual cost in the marketplace-fee delta of a single $40K wedding. Any Plnr running more than 1 event/year is leaving money on the table by staying on Solo. The Solo tier exists to onboard, not to retain.

Strategic implications

For Plnrs
The hybrid model is the strongest "why I use EvntCue and not HoneyBook" argument the industry has. A $69/mo subscription that pays back in passive marketplace-fee share on every Vndr booking is a different value proposition than any competitor offers. HoneyBook charges 3% for processing alone with no marketplace share. EvntCue charges 2.5% and pays the Plnr a marketplace cut.
For EvntCue
Revenue per event drops on Plnr-mediated bookings — but the Plnr now becomes an evangelist and a vendor-acquisition channel. The math works at scale because Plnrs bring volume. A Plnr running 8 events/month at $1,500 EvntCue revenue each ($12K/month) is more valuable than 5 self-managed events at $3,000 each ($15K/month) once you factor in the vendors and Orgnzs that Plnr brings to the platform.
For Vndrs
Identical fee structure either way. The 8% Vndr Listed / 6% Vndr Pro marketplace fee they pay on every booking is unchanged. The Vndr does not need to know whether the event is Plnr-mediated or self-managed at fee-calculation time. Internal accounting handles the routing. This protects Vndr UX and keeps the Vndr’s payout math predictable.

DB schema additions

FieldTypeNotes
events.plnr_engagement_iduuid nullableReferences plnr_engagements(id). Null = self-managed. Populated = Plnr-mediated. Already exists per §66 — §66.1 does not add new schema for the trigger itself.
plnr_engagements.engaged_attimestamptz NOT NULLThe hire timestamp. Immutable post-creation. Used to classify bookings as pre-hire or post-hire.
plnr_engagements.plnr_tier_at_hireenum(solo, pro) NOT NULLNew in v26.3. The Plnr's subscription tier at the moment of hire. Frozen on this engagement. If the Plnr upgrades to Pro mid-event, the engagement keeps the original tier — but a Plnr can opt to "refresh" the engagement (logged separately) which re-runs the tier check. Anti-gaming: a Plnr cannot simply upgrade for one billing cycle to capture a higher share retroactively.
bookings.confirmed_attimestamptz NOT NULLAlready in the §36 bookings schema. Used as the comparison point for the pre-hire / post-hire classification.
bookings.fee_split_modeenum(self_managed, plnr_pre_hire, plnr_post_hire_solo, plnr_post_hire_pro)Updated in v26.3. Computed at booking confirmation time and frozen. Drives the marketplace fee routing. Cannot be changed retroactively. Indexed for finance reporting. v26.2 enum values plnr_post_hire are split into plnr_post_hire_solo and plnr_post_hire_pro.
commission_flows.fee_split_modeenum, mirrors bookingsUpdated in v26.3. Copied from the parent booking at flow creation time. Lets finance reports group revenue by mode without joining bookings.

Computation logic — at booking confirmation

When a booking is confirmed, PaymentService.confirmBooking() computes the fee split mode in a single transaction:
1. Fetch events.plnr_engagement_id for the event.
2. If null: booking.fee_split_mode = 'self_managed'. INSERT commission_flows: 8% (Listed) or 6% (Pro) platform_marketplace_fee → EvntCue. Done.
3. If populated: fetch plnr_engagements.engaged_at AND plnr_engagements.plnr_tier_at_hire.
4. Compare booking.confirmed_at to engaged_at:
   • confirmed_at < engaged_at → fee_split_mode = 'plnr_pre_hire'. Split 50/50 regardless of tier.
   • confirmed_at >= engaged_at AND plnr_tier_at_hire = 'pro' → fee_split_mode = 'plnr_post_hire_pro'. EvntCue keeps 1.5% residual; Plnr earns 6.5% (Listed) or 4.5% (Pro) plus 100% of referrals.
   • confirmed_at >= engaged_at AND plnr_tier_at_hire = 'solo' → fee_split_mode = 'plnr_post_hire_solo'. EvntCue keeps 4.75% (Listed) or 3.75% (Pro); Plnr earns 3.25% (Listed) or 2.25% (Pro) plus 50% of referrals.
5. INSERT commission_flows rows with rates from the §66.1 fee table, setting fee_split_mode on each.
6. Commit transaction. The mode is now frozen on this booking forever.

Revenue model at DFW scale — hybrid v26.3

Assume 50 events/month at DFW average spend of $40,129. Mix: 40% self-managed (20 events), 60% Plnr-mediated (30 events). Of the Plnr-mediated, assume 70% are Pro tier (21 events) and 30% are Solo (9 events) — a realistic Pro conversion rate after 12 months of platform maturity.
SourceSelf-managed (20)Pro-mediated (21)Solo-mediated (9)Monthly total
Platform fee (2.5%)$20,000$21,000$9,000$50,000
Marketplace fee residual$40,000 (8% of $25K avg)$7,875 (1.5% of $25K avg)$10,688 (4.75% of $25K avg)$58,563
Plnr Pro subscriptions (~21 active)—$1,449—$1,449
Referral splits captured (Solo + pre-hire)——~$2,200 (50% of $4,800 avg referrals)~$2,200
EvntCue monthly revenue———~$112,212
v26.3 vs v26.2 vs pure §66 — comparison. Pure §66 (no hybrid) at the same 50 events/month: ~$118K/month. v26.2 hybrid (2% residual, no Solo gate): ~$107K/month. v26.3 hybrid (1.5% residual, Solo gate captures 50% from un-converted free Plnrs): ~$112K/month. The 1.5% residual is more generous to Pro Plnrs than v26.2's 2%; the Solo gate recovers most of that concession from Plnrs who haven't yet upgraded. Net: v26.3 gives Pro Plnrs a stronger value proposition without sacrificing platform revenue meaningfully. The 5% revenue gap vs pure §66 is the price of an industry-leading Plnr-friendly position.

Solo → Pro conversion mechanics

When a Solo Plnr upgrades to Pro:
  • Future events get the Pro split. Any new plnr_engagements created after the upgrade have plnr_tier_at_hire = 'pro'. New bookings on those engagements compute under plnr_post_hire_pro.
  • Existing engagements keep their original tier. If the Plnr is mid-event when they upgrade, the engagement's plnr_tier_at_hire stays solo. Bookings under that engagement continue to compute under the Solo split. This is the anti-gaming rule — a Plnr cannot upgrade for one billing cycle, capture the higher share retroactively on a $200K wedding, then downgrade.
  • The Plnr can manually "re-engage" on an existing event if both they and the Orgnz consent (logged in audit trail). Re-engaging creates a new plnr_engagements row with the new tier; the old engagement is closed. New bookings from re-engagement onward compute under Pro. Old bookings stay at Solo. This handles the case of a Plnr who legitimately wants to upgrade mid-event because the scope grew.
  • Downgrading from Pro to Solo works the same way in reverse: existing engagements keep pro, new engagements get solo.

What §66.1 does not change

  • The 2.5% platform fee is unchanged. It still applies to every Orgnz charge regardless of mode.
  • Stripe processing fees (2.9% + $0.30) are unchanged — Stripe takes their cut on every charge.
  • The Vndr referral slider (0–20%) is unchanged. Vndrs set per-package rates the same way.
  • Service fees (Plnr’s professional fee to the Orgnz) are unchanged. They live in service_fees, the platform earns 2.5% on them.
  • Co-Plnr splits are unchanged. EvntCue stays out of Plnr-to-Plnr negotiations entirely.
  • Cancellation rules from §66 are unchanged. 5% Orgnz cancellation retention applies regardless of mode.
  • RLS rules are unchanged. The Orgnz still never sees any commission flow row regardless of mode.

Migration note

All commission_flows rows created before v26.2 must be backfilled with fee_split_mode = 'self_managed' as the default — historical events did not have the hybrid distinction. New events created from v26.2 onward use the live computation. The migration is additive and non-destructive; no existing flows change rate or recipient.
67 — SafeTab — responsible service waiver
Conditional alcohol service with legally documented consent — inside EvntCue and as a standalone SaaS product.
Every catered event with an open bar carries the same liability chain: bartender over-serves → catering company exposed → venue exposed → host exposed. Texas TABC Dram Shop Act creates civil and criminal liability when a server knowingly continues to serve an intoxicated person. SafeTab inserts a documented consent checkpoint between complimentary drink tickets and the cash bar — shifting moral and legal posture from passive service to affirmative, recorded reasonable care.
The core insight: Every other drink-ticket system counts drinks. SafeTab conditions continued service on a documented safety commitment. The bartender doesn't decide when to stop — the guest decides how they're getting home. That decision is recorded, timestamped, and immutable.

Product identity

Inside EvntCue: SafeTab — a native feature of the Catr and Venue portals, available to any event with alcohol service. Standalone: SafeTab — an independent SaaS product licensed to any bar, venue, or catering company with no EvntCue account required. Domain: safetab.io. The two products share identical waiver infrastructure and schema. The standalone version simply has no event_id or tenant_id — it operates on a safetab_account_id instead.

Two operating modes

ModeContextGuest identificationWorks without EvntCue?
Event-linkedGuest is on the EvntCue event guest list. Catr or Venue portal triggers SafeTab after comp tickets are exhausted.SMS to guest's number on file. Guest opens link on their own phone — no app required.No — requires active EvntCue event.
Walk-up / standaloneNo guest list. Any bar or venue. QR code printed and laminated at the bar or on a table tent.Guest scans QR with phone camera. Enters name and mobile number directly in the waiver flow.Yes — fully independent. Works for any licensed establishment.

What makes it legally binding — four required elements

A digital waiver is enforceable when it satisfies all four of the following. SafeTab is designed around these requirements from the ground up. Attorney review of waiver copy is required per jurisdiction before launch — Texas first.
#ElementHow SafeTab satisfies it
1Identity — the signing party can be proven to be who they claimDriver's license scan at first drink ticket establishes identity. DL number is hashed (SHA-256 with salt) and stored — not the image. No PII retained beyond the hash. On walk-up flow: phone number + device fingerprint provides corroborating identity signal.
2Informed consent — clear language stating what is being agreed toAttorney-reviewed waiver text states: "I acknowledge that I have arranged safe transportation home and that this establishment is relying on this representation before serving me additional alcohol. I understand this acknowledgment is logged and may be used in any proceeding related to this event." Full text versioned in safetab_waivers.waiver_version — the exact copy shown at signing is preserved forever.
3Affirmative action — passive checkbox is not sufficientGuest must type their full legal name as the signature field. On mobile, Face ID or fingerprint biometric confirmation is offered as an alternative (WebAuthn). No tap-through. No pre-checked boxes.
4Immutable timestamp log — tamper-evident record suitable for litigationAll waiver records: INSERT ONLY RLS policy. No UPDATE, no DELETE, ever — not even by admin. Postgres row-level security enforced at the database level, not the application layer. Every subsequent drink served after signing increments drinks_after_waiver — creating a full service record tied to the acknowledged waiver.
Attorney review required: Waiver copy must be reviewed per jurisdiction before SafeTab is marketed as liability-shifting. Texas TABC Dram Shop Act language is the first target. The documented reasonable care defense is valid even before attorney sign-off — but the marketing claim requires legal validation. This is a one-time cost per state, not ongoing. Budget: $500–$2,000 per jurisdiction.

Transport method — why it matters

Requiring a transport method selection transforms a generic acknowledgment into a specific commitment. It also creates actionable safety data and — importantly — a stronger legal record. A guest who selects Uber/Lyft and then drives drunk has made a demonstrably false representation. A guest who selects "designated driver" and names that person has created a third-party witness record.
Transport methodSystem actionLegal weight
Rideshare (Uber / Lyft)Optional deep-link to rideshare app opens after signing. Cue can optionally prompt at event end: "Need a ride home?"Strong — specific service named, actionable commitment.
Designated driverGuest names the driver and enters their phone number. Driver receives courtesy SMS: "[Guest] has listed you as their designated driver tonight at [Venue]. Safe travels."Strongest — creates a corroborating third-party record. Driver SMS is logged.
Hotel / on-site accommodationGuest enters room number. Venue portal can optionally cross-reference against a hotel block guest list if one exists.Strong — verifiable against venue records.
Taxi / car serviceNo additional action. Logged as stated method.Moderate — stated commitment, no verification.
OtherFree-text field (max 120 chars). Guest describes arrangement.Moderate — on record but unverified.

The bartender flow — event-linked mode

The bartender never makes a judgment call about when to stop. SafeTab makes the decision structural.
1. Comp tickets exhausted
Catr portal (bartender's screen) shows guest has used their allotted tickets. A SafeTab button appears. The bartender taps it — this action is logged with bartender tenant ID and timestamp.
2. Guest receives SMS
Guest's phone number on file receives: "[Venue] is opening the cash bar. Before we continue, we ask that you confirm your safe transportation home. Takes 30 seconds. [link]" The link is a one-time-use JWT that expires in 10 minutes.
3. Guest completes waiver on their own phone
Full waiver text displayed. Transport method selected. Driver named if applicable. Full legal name typed. Optionally: Face ID / fingerprint via WebAuthn. Guest submits. Record written to safetab_waivers — INSERT ONLY.
4. Bartender screen confirms green
Bartender's screen shows a green confirmation token: guest name + signed timestamp. Cash bar service may proceed. Every subsequent drink served is logged against the waiver via drinks_after_waiver increment.
5. Guest declines to sign
If the guest does not complete the waiver within 10 minutes, the bartender's screen shows "Waiver not completed — cash bar not available for this guest." The bartender is protected. No judgment required.

The bartender flow — walk-up / standalone mode

No EvntCue event required. A QR code is printed — laminated table tent, bar mat insert, or displayed on a small screen at the point of service. Guest scans with their phone camera. No app download required — pure mobile web.
QR code setup
SafeTab standalone dashboard generates a persistent QR code for the venue or event. The QR encodes a URL: safetab.io/w/[account_slug]/[optional_event_code]. Code is static — never changes for a given venue. Reprint once and it works forever.
Guest self-identifies
Guest enters first and last name, mobile phone number. Optional: DL scan for identity corroboration (prompted, not required). Device fingerprint captured silently via browser API.
Waiver and transport selection
Identical to event-linked flow. Attorney-reviewed waiver text. Transport method selected. Typed name signature. Submit. Guest receives SMS copy of their signed waiver for their own records.
Bartender confirmation token
Bartender's SafeTab dashboard (open on their POS tablet or phone) shows a live feed of completed waivers: guest name, time signed, transport method. Green badge. Service may proceed.

token_expires_attimestamptz nullableCron job clears expired unsigned tokens.
created_attimestamptz not null default now()
RLS — INSERT ONLY. This is non-negotiable.
CREATE POLICY "insert_only" ON safetab_waivers FOR INSERT WITH CHECK (true);
CREATE POLICY "tenant_read" ON safetab_waivers FOR SELECT USING (tenant_id = auth.uid() OR safetab_account_id = auth.uid());
No UPDATE policy. No DELETE policy. Not even for admin — admin uses a read-only reporting view. If a waiver record must be disputed, a dispute record is created in a separate table. The original waiver is never touched. This is the foundation of the legal defensibility. A developer who adds an UPDATE policy has broken the product.

EvntCue integration — portal touchpoints

PortalWhere SafeTab appearsNotes
CatrBartender day-of screen. After comp ticket count is exhausted, SafeTab trigger appears. Waiver log visible in Catr event dashboard post-event.Primary home. Catr is the licensed service provider — most exposed to TABC liability.
VenueVenue can require SafeTab as a condition of any event with alcohol service. Appears in venue event requirements checklist. Venue sees aggregate waiver log for all events at their space.Venue can mandate use as part of their standard F&B agreement — creates a platform-level safety standard.
PlnrPlnr can enable SafeTab during event setup if they are coordinating bar service. Appears in Plnr day-of checklist as a confirmed/pending item.Plnr visibility only — they don't operate the waiver, but they can confirm it's active.
OrgnzOrgnz sees SafeTab as an active safety feature on their event summary. Post-event: Cue can surface a summary — "14 guests signed SafeTab waivers. All selected rideshare or designated driver."Orgnz has no operational control — they see the summary only. Cannot view individual guest waiver records (privacy).

Cue integration

Pre-event
When Cue detects an event with alcohol service (has_alcohol = true on events table), it automatically surfaces SafeTab to the Catr and Venue portals in the event setup checklist: "This event includes alcohol service. SafeTab is recommended — it takes 2 minutes to enable and creates a documented reasonable care record for every guest."
Day-of
Cue monitors the real-time waiver completion rate during the event. If a significant number of guests have not completed waivers but drinks_after_waiver is climbing on completed ones, Cue alerts the Catr operator: "8 guests are being served past their comp tickets without a SafeTab waiver on file. Tap to send bulk SMS."
Post-event summary
Cue generates a SafeTab summary card in the post-event report: total waivers signed, transport method breakdown (rideshare X%, designated driver Y%, hotel Z%), designated driver SMS confirmations sent, total drinks served after waiver. This summary is stored on the event record and can be produced in any future legal proceeding.

Standalone business — strategic rationale

The total addressable market for SafeTab standalone is every TABC-licensed establishment in Texas — approximately 55,000 licenses — and every equivalent licensed establishment in the 50 states. The EvntCue TAM is private events. The SafeTab TAM is every bar that has ever been sued under a Dram Shop Act. These are different buyers, different sales motions, and different price sensitivity. The products share identical infrastructure. The marginal cost of standing up SafeTab standalone is a domain, a landing page, and a Stripe billing account.
The higher-level insight: SafeTab is a documented consent at the point of risk platform. The drunk driving use case is the most emotionally compelling entry point — but the architecture is reusable. Extreme sports waivers, cannabis dispensary sales, prescription pickups, and any regulated transaction where a vendor needs documented acknowledgment of risk before proceeding are all addressable with the same infrastructure. SafeTab is the first product. The platform is larger than one use case.

Launch sequence

PhaseActionDependency
0 — LegalAttorney review of waiver copy for Texas TABC jurisdiction. Produce waiver version TX-1.0. Budget $500–$2,000.Required before any marketing claim about liability shifting.
1 — EvntCue nativeBuild SafeTab into Catr portal day-of screen. Event-linked SMS flow. INSERT ONLY schema. Waiver log in Catr dashboard.Catr portal day-of screen (§56) must exist. EvntCue Live must be active.
2 — Standalone QRBuild safetab.io landing + walk-up QR flow. Free tier. SafeTab Bar billing via Stripe.Can be built independently of EvntCue Catr portal. Shared schema, separate auth context.

68 — Terminology standards — user-facing language
Professional language across all portals. No word on any user-facing surface should make the platform feel transactional or exploitative.
The revenue architecture of EvntCue involves referral commissions, venue kickbacks, and platform fees. These are legitimate and disclosed — but the language used to describe them in the UI determines whether users feel like participants in a professional ecosystem or marks in a commission scheme. This section locks the user-facing terminology for all portals. The database table stays commission_flows — that is internal plumbing, never visible to any user.
Founding principle: The Four Seasons doesn't call it a commission. They call it a preferred vendor arrangement. The money is the same. The language tells a completely different story about the relationship.

Substitution table — locked

Old / internal termUser-facing replacementWhere it appears
KickbackPartnership yield (Venue earnings ledger) · Partnership rate (Venue settings slider)Venue portal only. Never shown to Orgnz.
Commission (Plnr referral)Referral earn (Plnr ledger) · Referral rate (Vndr slider label)Plnr portal earnings tab · Vndr package settings
Commission (platform)Platform feeBooking confirmation · Orgnz receipt · Vndr payout breakdown. This term is kept — it is accurate and neutral.
Commission flowsNever user-facing. DB table name only.Internal schema: commission_flows. Zero UI instances.
F&B surchargeKitchen rate or F&B facility rateVenue portal earnings · Catr booking summary
Commission dial / sliderReferral rate sliderVndr package settings page
Commission intelligenceReferral intelligence or Arrangement visibilityPlnr portal section headers · Cue tooltips

Visibility rules — who sees what

PortalSees referral/partnership rates?Language used
OrgnzNever. Zero visibility into any arrangement.Orgnz sees only booking totals and platform fee on receipts.
PlnrYes — their own referral earns only."Referral earn" on ledger. "Referral rate" in Vndr settings context.
VndrYes — their own rate slider only."Referral rate" on package settings. "Referral earn" on payout breakdown.
VenueYes — their partnership yield from preferred vendor bookings."Partnership rate" on vendor settings. "Partnership yield" on earnings ledger.
CatrNo rate UI. Catr earns flat booking payments.Catr sees booking value and platform fee deduction only.
73 — Catr portal — UI spec
The licensed food professional's command center. Certification-gated. Day-of focused. SafeTab native.
The Catr portal serves licensed catering operations — any business or individual serving food at an event. Hard gate: must hold valid food handler certification, general liability insurance, and where applicable, TABC certification before the profile goes live. The portal is structured around two modes: pre-event setup and day-of operations.

Sidebar navigation

Event Mode (EvntCue Live) · BEO View · SafeTab · Guest Dietary
Finance section

Dashboard — hero metrics (P1)

MetricWhat it showsVisual

Upcoming eventsCount of confirmed bookings within 30 daysNumber · next event date chip
Menu coverage% of active menu items with photos + dietary tagsProgress arc · "incomplete" call to action if under 80%
