Cue panel — Catr-specific intelligence

Cue surfaces: COI expiry warnings (30-day, 14-day, 7-day escalation), TABC expiry if applicable, upcoming events missing BEO acknowledgment, SafeTab activation reminder when has_alcohol = true on a booked event, and guest dietary flag summaries ("3 guests with nut allergy confirmed for Garcia Wedding — Apr 12").

Certification gate — hard requirements

CertRequired?Expiry trackingGate behavior
Food Handler CertificationYes — all CatrsYes — 30/14/7 day Cue alertsProfile hidden from search until uploaded and verified
General Liability Insurance (GL)Yes — all CatrsYesCannot accept bookings without active GL on file
TABC CertificationYes — if serving alcoholYesSafeTab cannot be activated without valid TABC. Venue can require as condition of preferred list.
Health Department PermitSoft — recommendedYesTrust score boost when present. Not a hard gate at launch.

Menu builder (P1)

Menu items organized by course/category. Each item: name, description, price-per-head or flat, dietary tags (vegan, gluten-free, kosher, halal, nut-free, dairy-free, shellfish-free), photo upload. Items can be grouped into packages. Packages have minimum guest count and pricing tiers. Dietary tag data flows directly to BEO and guest dietary summary view on day-of.

BEO view (day-of)

Read-only event BEO surfaced on the day-of screen. Shows: event name, venue, guest count, dietary breakdown (auto-summarized from RSVP data), timeline/service windows, notes from Plnr or Venue. Catr acknowledges BEO receipt — this acknowledgment is timestamped and logged. BEO is not shared with Orgnz (per §2 resolved decisions).

SafeTab integration (day-of)

When has_alcohol = true, the SafeTab button appears on the bartender day-of screen after comp ticket count is exhausted. Full flow per §67. Waiver log accessible in Catr event dashboard post-event. Aggregate waiver summary available for any legal proceeding.

Earnings breakdown

Booking value · Platform fee deduction (2.5%) · Stripe processing fee deduction · Net payout. No referral/commission language in Catr portal — Catr earns straight booking payments. Payout schedule: 48 hours post-event confirmation, via Stripe Connect or Dwolla (Month 3).
74 — Orgnz portal — UI spec
The event organizer's home. Freemium. Mood-board-first. No commission language anywhere.
The Orgnz portal is the consumer-facing heart of EvntCue. It serves both personal event organizers (wedding couples, quinceañera families, bar mitzvah parents) and corporate coordinators. Freemium with limits. The entire experience is built around the mood board as the emotional anchor — vision first, logistics second.

Onboarding — P1 (4 steps + mood board seed)

StepWhat happensDesign note
0.5 — Vision seed"Show Cue your vision." Upload 3 images or pick from curated style cards (10 aesthetic directions). This happens before naming the event.Full-bleed emotional moment. No form fields. Just images. Sets the mood board foundation and colors every Cue recommendation downstream.

Cultural variant is optional but unlocks significant Cue intelligence.

Dashboard — P2 layout

The mood board is the full-width hero at the top of the dashboard — above stat cards, above Cue, above everything. It functions like the album cover of the event. The color palette pulled from the board provides subtle tinting across the entire dashboard (if board is blush/burgundy, dashboard accent shifts toward those tones). Below the mood board hero: hero metrics row, Cue panel, then event management sections.

Cue panel — Orgnz-specific intelligence

Cue surfaces to the Orgnz: upcoming booking deadlines ("Your venue requires final guest count by Mar 15"), task reminders from the planning checklist, SafeTab summary post-event ("14 guests confirmed safe transport"), budget warnings, and vendor confirmation status. Cue never surfaces commission rates, partnership yields, or referral arrangements to Orgnz — ever.

Vendor booking section

Grid of vendor category cards: Venue, Catering, Photography, AV/Lighting, DJ/Entertainment, Florals, Hair & Makeup, Transportation, Officiant, Cake/Desserts. Each card shows: booked (teal ✓) / inquiry pending (amber) / not started (grey). Tapping an unbooked category opens the marketplace filtered to that category, event type, date, and guest count. Tapping a booked vendor opens the booking detail and messaging thread.

What Orgnz never sees

Hard rule: No referral rates, no partnership yields, no platform fee breakdowns beyond their own receipt, no commission flows of any kind. The Orgnz experience is: choose vendors, confirm bookings, pay, enjoy their event. The professional layer is invisible to them by design.
75 — Vndr portal — UI spec · v26.5
The vendor's first-twenty-minutes flow: landing, four-step capture, freemium dashboard. Owned work only. Four-dimension match fingerprint.
The Vndr portal serves any service vendor that is not a caterer or venue — Photography & Media, Florals & Design, Audio & Music, Visual Production & Lighting, Décor & Rentals, Dessert & Bar, Personal & Beauty, Interactive Entertainment, Transportation & Logistics. Pricing per §19: Listed (free) with full marketplace functionality plus tiered booking commission, or Professional ($49/mo · $39/mo annual) with reduced commission and Pro tooling. Free tier earns from day one — Pro is an earnings unlock, not a paywall around basic functionality.
The freemium-with-payment thesis. Vndrs come to EvntCue to set up shop, not to dream-shop. Profile capture happens up front — the asymmetry from §74 (where Orgnz captures profile after the timeline build, mid-flow) is intentional. Vndrs are applying to be on the platform; Orgnzs are exploring it. Both flows are correct for their populations. Front door of a business, not a paywall.

Signature Board — mood-board reuse pattern

The Vndr portfolio component is the same component as the Orgnz mood board (§5, §47), with the vector reversed. Orgnz says "this is what I want"; Vndr says "this is what I make." Same data structure (mood_boards + mood_board_items), same upload pipeline, same color extraction. The Cue matching engine reads both sides and matches on aesthetic alignment, not just category and rate.
One investment, two utilities. Reusing the mood board means the same image-handling code, RLS scope, and color-DNA extraction serves both Orgnz wishlists and Vndr portfolios. When §47 Upgrade 5 lands (vision API batch matching), it serves both populations from one infrastructure.

Owned-only enforcement — three layers

LayerMechanismWhat it blocks
1. URL paste blocklistHardcoded domain match on paste. Pinterest, Instagram, Facebook, TikTok, Snapchat, Threads, X/Twitter, Unsplash, Pexels, Pixabay, Shutterstock, Getty, iStock, Adobe Stock, Flickr, 500px, Behance, Dribbble, Tumblr, Reddit, Imgur, Google, Bing.Stock photos, social media saves, Pinterest mood boards, search-engine image results
2. Own-domain checkPaste URL domain matched against the website field from Step 2. Mismatches trigger a confirmation prompt rather than a hard block — legitimate cases exist (Squarespace subdomains, white-labeled portfolio hosts).Most accidental wrong-domain pastes
3. Affirmative attestationCheckbox revealed after first upload: "I made these images, or I have explicit permission from the photographer and any people pictured to display them on my EvntCue profile." Same documented-consent-at-point-of-risk pattern as SafeTab waiver (§67).The remaining edge cases legally; soft moat against future disputes
Why it matters beyond legality: the matching algorithm learns each Vndr's aesthetic from these images. Borrowed work poisons the signal — a florist who fills their board with Pinterest pulls gets matched to organizers expecting work the florist doesn't actually produce. Cleaner training data → smarter Cue → better matches → higher conversion → more vendors join → cleaner training data. Compounding loop.

Four-dimension match fingerprint — replaces color-only matching

Color alone is what the eye sees first; style is what the eye recognizes. Two florists can both have coral-and-cream palettes — one does loose garden English, the other does tight modernist installations. Same color DNA, opposite aesthetic. Matching on color alone would put both florists in the same bucket and the Orgnz would feel that mismatch the moment they saw the portfolio. Cue therefore reads four dimensions in parallel — surfaced back to the Vndr in the Signature Board UI as a transparency move, with a "Tell us what's true →" correction affordance.
DimensionWhat it measuresExtraction method
Color DNAHue temperature, saturation, lightness range, palette breadthVision API + canvas color sampling. Five swatches surfaced; tags like warm · saturated · pale.
Style fingerprintLoose vs tight, organic vs geometric, ornate vs minimal, classical vs maximalistVision API tagging. Returns aesthetic categories like romantic · garden · loose & abundant or modernist · refined · negative-space.
Value & lightBright/airy vs moody/dramatic, high-key vs low-key, warm/cool temperature, atmosphereLuminance histogram + Vision API atmosphere tags. Surfaced as a Moody↔Bright bar plus tag string like bright · airy · high-key.
CompositionSymmetric vs asymmetric, dense vs sparse, scale of subject, framingVision API composition tags. Tag strings like open frames · negative space · clean lines.
Implementation note — production vs prototype. The shipped v1 uses heuristic readouts derived from canvas-sampled RGB and luminance values for the prototype prompt feedback. Production replaces this with the §47 Upgrade 5 vision API batch call. Same four UI panels stay; only the data source behind them swaps from heuristic to genuine vision tags. The "Cue got it wrong? Tell us what's true →" affordance preserves vendor agency over the algorithm's read of them — same trust-building pattern that runs through the rest of the platform.

Take-home calculator — replaces the rate-tier table

An earlier draft of the landing showed Vndr commission as a 3-tier table (5%/4%/3% Free vs 3%/3%/2% Pro across booking sizes) plus a separate 2.5% platform fee. This was technically accurate and human-unreadable for the artistic population the Vndr portal targets. Replaced with: one slider, one big take-home number, two columns showing Free vs Pro, one delta line. The headline reads "For every $5,000 you book, you keep $4,488" — and slides as the user moves the input. The math is the proof, not the pitch.
The "one glance" rule. Every place pricing appears in EvntCue should pass the one-glance test. A vendor reading the page should never have to compute. Lead with the take-home; let the calculator handle exploration. Same pattern applies to the Orgnz "what does this event cost" view, the Plnr "what's my commission" view, the Venu "what does this booking net me" view, and the Catr "what's my margin after surcharges" view. If it requires a table to explain what someone pays, the table is the bug.

Soft document gates — never hard, contra Catr

Per §36 issue 13, Vndr COI is a soft requirement — listing remains active without it but a "No COI on file" badge appears on the marketplace card; uploading flips that to "Verified" and unlocks +18 trust score points. This contrasts with Catr (§21), where insurance + food handler + TABC are hard gates because food safety is non-negotiable. The Vndr portal copy frames the COI as an upgrade incentive, not a barrier: "Your profile goes live the moment you finish this step. Documents add a Verified badge that helps planners pick you with confidence — nothing here blocks you from being listed."
DocumentGate typeTriggerSurface
General liability COISoft — +18 trust, Verified badgeAll Vndrs (recommended for all)Step 4 default; surfaced in dashboard trust ring as the largest unfilled reward
Business licenseOptional — Verified badgeIf discipline requires one in TXStep 4 secondary
TABC certificationConditional — surfaces only if applicableIf Step 1 sub-type is Mixologist or SommelierStep 4 reveal-on-condition; tagged "Conditional · TABC"
Food handler certificationConditional — surfaces only if applicableIf Step 1 sub-type is Coffee cart, Late-night snack, or any food-prep roleStep 4 reveal-on-condition; tagged "Conditional · Food handler"

Inquiry inbox — qualification badges as conversion edge

Every vendor platform sells leads. Most platforms can't tell vendors which leads are real. EvntCue can — because the same escrow dollars get read three different ways: the Orgnz reads them as shopping power, the Venu reads them as qualified intent, the Vndr reads them as a confirmed-event signal. Surfacing this multiplicity in the Vndr inbox is the conversion edge over WeddingWire, The Knot, and Thumbtack.
BadgeWhen it appearsWhat it tells the Vndr
Ready to bookVenu confirmed + signed Venu contract + vendor escrow fundedReal lead. Respond fast — these close 3–5x faster than directory leads.
Browsing onlyDate + budget set, but Venu pending or no escrow yetSoft inquiry. Polite quick reply; don't hold dates. Cue surfaces the gap.
The "Why this lead is real" trust card on the inquiry detail surfaces the underlying signals: Venu confirmation status, vendor escrow status, Plnr presence, signed-contract status. Without these badges, EvntCue inquiries look the same as any other channel's. With them, Vndrs learn fast that EvntCue prospects close at a different rate.

Dashboard panels — what ships in v1

Profile views
First 24 hours · listed. Progress bar against expected baseline. Cue commentary if conversion is unusually low or high.
Inquiries waiting
Total count + breakdown of Ready to book vs Browsing only. Click-through to inbox.
Trust score
/100 with the largest unfilled reward surfaced (e.g. "+18 if you upload your COI"). Drives behavior toward the Verified badge without nagging.
Booked this month
$0 on day one. First payout 48 hrs after first event. Empty state copy explains the timing.
Inbox · incoming inquiries
Inquiry rows with name + qualification badge + meta + trust line + amount. Empty state explains Cue is matching to events that fit category and area.
Trust score (detail)
Coral arc + rolling sub-scores: profile complete · Stripe connected · service area · COI · first booking. Sums to 100.
Signature board · what you make
Horizontal strip of up to 12 image tiles + Color DNA palette strip below. Cue commentary explains the matching read.
Your packages
Each package: name, price, description, planner referral rate visualization (slider value rendered as a fill bar).
Calendar · next 30 days
7-column mini calendar with three states: Booked (coral), Hold (amber), Open (default). Sync action for external calendar.

Asymmetry vs Orgnz capture — the front-door analogy

Compare the Orgnz capture flow (§74) and the Vndr capture flow (§75): both end at a profile, but the path is opposite. Orgnz captures profile after the timeline build (Step 4.5) because Orgnzs are dream-shopping — they need to see what's possible before being asked to commit. Vndrs are doing the opposite: they've come to set up shop. Asking a vendor to register before showing what's possible is the front door of a business, not a paywall. Same platform; opposite acquisition gravity. The Venu portal (§75.1) follows the Vndr pattern: capture profile up front, because Venus also are applying to be on the platform.

What's intentionally not in v1

Deferred: Vndr CRM dashboard, full booking management screens, calendar / availability blocking UI beyond the mini calendar, reviews UI, payout tracking detail view. The freemium dashboard preview shows the shape of these — actual implementation comes after first 50 booked events generate enough data to design against real usage patterns.
75.1 — Venue portal — UI spec · v26.3
The space owner’s control room. Spaces, schedules, and the four commission flows in plain sight.
The Venue portal serves any operator of physical event space — banquet halls, hotels, restaurants with private rooms, outdoor venues, country clubs, museums, breweries. Unlike Catr (which is certification-gated) or Vndr (which is referral-driven), Venues are evaluated on capacity, location, and the photographic quality of their spaces. The portal is structured around two primary mental models: the calendar (when is each space booked?) and the commission setup (what fees flow in and out?). Everything else organizes around those two anchors.
The Venue portal’s core problem. Venue managers run multiple physical spaces with overlapping schedules, vendor relationships negotiated separately for each, and a layered fee structure (in-house fees, F&B surcharges, kickbacks, sourcing commissions) that is currently tracked across spreadsheets, contracts, and phone notes. The Venue portal collapses all four into a single layer with one calendar source of truth and one commission setup wizard. The four flow types from §34 are first-class objects in the UI — never buried in settings.

Sidebar navigation

Business section
Dashboard · Inquiries (badge) · Bookings · Calendar · Messages (badge)
Spaces section
Spaces · Photos & Tour · Capacity & Layouts · Inclusions & Restrictions
Commission setup
In-house Fees · F&B Surcharge · Preferred Vendors · Plnr Sourcing
Operations section
Day-of · BEO Acknowledgments · COI Verification · Catr Approval Queue

Public Profile · Reviews & Trust Score · Insurance & Permits · Availability Rules

Dashboard — hero metrics

MetricWhat it showsVisual

Cue panel — Venue-specific intelligence

Cue surfaces, in priority order: (1) Inquiries unanswered >24 hours — drafts a response based on the space, date, guest count, and similar past inquiries. (2) COI/permit expiry on upcoming events — 30/14/7-day escalation with one-tap message-to-Catr request. (3) Calendar conflicts when an inquiry overlaps with a confirmed booking on the same space. (4) Underutilized spaces — when a space’s booking rate falls below 30% of comparable Venues in the market, Cue suggests pricing or photography updates. (5) Kickback opt-in opportunities — when a Vndr who is not on the preferred list books at this Venue 3+ times, Cue suggests inviting them to the preferred list with a draft message. (6) Plnr sourcing alerts — when a Plnr sources a booking, Cue surfaces the commission flow setup and the 48-hour escrow status.

Spaces — the heart of the portal

Each space is a top-level object. Venues commonly have 3–8 spaces (Grand Ballroom, Garden Terrace, Library, Boardroom, Patio, etc.) with different capacities, layouts, and price tiers. Each space carries its own commission configuration — outside catering allowed in the Garden Terrace but not the Grand Ballroom, for example. Spaces are managed independently but roll up to the Venue dashboard for aggregate views.
FieldTypeNotes
NameRequired text"Grand Ballroom" — appears in marketplace, contract, BEO
Capacity (seated / standing / cocktail)3 integersDrives guest count cascade per §36 — bookings hard-blocked above hard threshold
Square footageIntegerUsed by Cue layout suggestions and floor plan tool
Rental rateFlat or tiered (weekday/weekend/holiday)Stripe price object created per tier
PhotosMin 5, max 30First photo is the marketplace card image — Cue flags low-quality or wrong-aspect images
Layouts availableMulti-select: theater, banquet, U-shape, cabaret, reception, classroom, customFloor plan tool seeds layouts; each layout has its own capacity
InclusionsTags: tables, chairs, linens, AV, parking, valet, kitchen access, etc.Drives overlap detection in §3 — Cue flags if Vndr also quoting included items
RestrictionsTags: noise curfew, no open flame, no rice/confetti, etc.Surfaced to Plnr/Catr at booking inquiry; logged in BEO
Outside catering policyenum(allowed, not_allowed, allowed_with_surcharge)If allowed_with_surcharge: drives the F&B surcharge flow per §34

Booking calendar — the other anchor

Multi-space calendar in two views: (1) Day grid — vertical timeline per space showing inquiries (amber), holds (gray dashed), confirmed bookings (teal solid), maintenance blocks (slate). (2) Month grid — heatmap density per space, click any cell to see the booking detail. The calendar is the source of truth for availability — public marketplace queries hit this calendar via cached availability windows. Note: when an inquiry comes in for a space-and-date that conflicts with an existing hold, Cue surfaces the conflict before the inquiry reaches the inbox — the Venue manager doesn’t accidentally double-book by responding to a conflicting inquiry first.

Inquiry inbox — funnel-aware

Inquiries arrive from three sources: marketplace (Orgnz or Plnr browsed and contacted), Plnr-mediated (Plnr proposing a venue to their hired Orgnz), and direct (someone followed a SEO-indexed venue page). Each inquiry shows the source, the event details (date, guest count, type, est. budget), the requested space, and any pre-quote questions. The Venue manager has four actions on each inquiry: Quote (sends rate + availability hold), Decline (with reason — date unavailable, capacity mismatch, restriction conflict), Hold for 7 days (places a soft hold on the calendar), or Refer to another space (redirects within the venue’s spaces). Quote actions trigger a Stripe deposit invoice and convert the hold to a booking once paid.

Commission setup wizard — first run, four steps

The first time a Venue manager opens commission setup, a 4-step wizard walks them through the four flow types from §34. Each flow is independent — a Venue can enable any combination. Default state: all four off. Once configured, individual toggles are accessible in Commission Setup → [Flow Type] without re-running the wizard.
StepFlow typeWhat the Venue configuresDefault if skipped
1venue_in_house — In-house feesCake cutting on/off (rate per guest), corkage on/off (rate per bottle, max bottles), custom fees (security deposit, setup/teardown, valet, coat check). Each as flat or per-guest, applied per space.All off — Venue charges only the rental rate
2venue_fb_surcharge — F&B surchargePer space: outside catering policy (allowed / not allowed / allowed_with_surcharge). If surcharge: rate 0–25%, basis (F&B only recommended / total invoice). Default basis is F&B-only — applies surcharge only to food and beverage revenue, not labor (per §08 dual-basis catering commission model).Outside catering not allowed by default — Venue’s in-house F&B is the only option
3venue_kickback — Preferred vendor listKickback type: annual flat or per-event %. Amount or rate per vendor category. Define which categories are open to preferred status. Vendors must explicitly opt in — wizard generates the invitation message template.No preferred list — all marketplace Vndrs are bookable equally
4venue_referral — Plnr sourcing commissionPer space: sourcing rate 0–20% (capped at 20% per §34). Basis selector: rental fee only (default), total invoice, or custom. 48-hour post-event escrow via Trustap. Rose badge appears on the Venue’s card in Plnr marketplace.No sourcing commission — Plnrs see the Venue but earn nothing on bookings

Commission ledger — read view

A unified view of every commission_flows row associated with this Venue, grouped by event. Columns: event name, date, flow type (with color-coded chip), counterparty, basis amount, rate, flow amount, status (pending / released / disputed). Filterable by flow type, date range, and counterparty. Exportable as CSV per §80 reporting spec. Critical UX note: the Orgnz never sees this view — RLS hard-blocks Orgnz queries from returning commission_flows rows where they are not the counterparty (and even then, only venue_in_house rows). The Plnr sees only their own outside flows. The Venue sees all four flow types where they are the to_party or from_party.

BEO acknowledgment workflow

When a Catr or Plnr finalizes a BEO for an event taking place at this Venue, the Venue receives an acknowledgment request in the Operations section. The Venue manager reviews the BEO for accuracy on space assignment, layout, guest count vs. capacity, F&B service style, and timing. Acknowledgment is logged with timestamp. If the Venue declines, a structured rejection (with reason + suggested fix) is sent back to the BEO author. The Venue cannot edit the BEO directly — the BEO is a Catr/Plnr document — but the Venue’s acknowledgment is a hard gate before day-of operations begin.

Catr approval queue (preferred-list venues only)

For Venues that have configured outside catering as allowed_with_surcharge: every Catr who books a Catr-led event at this Venue passes through an approval queue. The Venue reviews the Catr’s certifications (food handler, GL insurance, TABC if alcohol), the menu (for kitchen-load and equipment compatibility), and the proposed timeline (for venue staffing alignment). Three actions: Approve (Catr is added to the approved list for this space; future bookings auto-pass), Approve with conditions (e.g. "no fryer in this kitchen," "load-in via service entrance only"), or Decline (with reason — Catr can resubmit after addressing).

Day-of view

Mobile-first read view of today’s events at this Venue. Each card shows: event name, space, Plnr or Orgnz contact, Catr contact, expected guest count, service start/end times, BEO link, special instructions (allergies, dietary restrictions, ceremony cues). Cue surfaces alerts: COI not received, dietary flag changes since last sync, weather-related concerns for outdoor events. Venue manager can mark setup complete, ceremony complete, breakdown complete — these timestamps feed §47 vendor performance scoring. This screen is built for thumb use on a phone — 44px minimum touch targets, single-column cards, no horizontal scroll.

Public profile — what the Orgnz/Plnr sees

The Venue’s public-facing page lives at /venue/[slug] — SEO-indexed, server-side rendered. Shows: hero photo gallery (drawn from spaces’ photo libraries), venue description, full space directory with capacities and starting prices, layouts available, inclusions and restrictions per space, location map, reviews aggregate, "Request inquiry" CTA. What is intentionally not shown: commission rates, F&B surcharge percentages, kickback structures, sourcing commission rates. None of these are visible on the public page or in the Orgnz API response. They appear only in the Plnr marketplace view (sourcing commission badge, per §34) or the Vndr dashboard (kickback opt-in, per §34).

Trust score components — Venue-specific

ComponentWeightSource
Response time to inquiries25%Median time from inquiry receipt to first response, last 90 days
Booking completion rate25%% of confirmed bookings that completed without dispute, last 12 months
Review average20%Aggregate review score from Plnrs and Orgnzs, last 12 months
BEO acknowledgment timeliness15%% of BEOs acknowledged within 72 hours of receipt
COI compliance rate10%% of events with all required certificates of insurance on file at event date
Profile completeness5%Photo count, descriptions, layouts defined, restrictions documented

Reports tab — see §80

Four CSV exports auto-generated 48 hours post-event per §80: space utilization, partnership yield, commission flow health, and COI compliance. Built for venue managers and their finance teams, designed to import directly into QuickBooks or Sage Intacct without preprocessing. Reports are downloadable manually or scheduled for monthly email delivery.

Build status

Sidebar navigation + dashboard heroP0To buildMirrors §73 Catr structure with Venue-specific metrics

Booking calendar (day + month views)P0To buildSource of truth for availability — public marketplace reads from it

Day-of mobile viewP1To buildPhone-first per §10 mobile strategy

Trust score + reviewsP2To buildCompounds with platform data — depth grows over time
Reports tab + CSV exportsP2PartialCSV structures locked in §80 — UI surface to build
The Venue UI’s strategic role. Venues are the supply-side anchor of the marketplace — without venue density, the platform cannot function. The portal’s design optimizes for two things: (1) response time to inquiries, because Venue conversion is gated on speed (Cue drafts the response, the Venue manager taps to send) and (2) commission setup clarity, because the four flow types from §34 are confusing in spreadsheets and crystal clear in a 4-step wizard. If the Venue portal does these two things well, the rest of the platform’s liquidity flywheel turns. If it doesn’t, no amount of Plnr or Orgnz acquisition matters.

v26.7 lessons baked in

  • Six-stage acquisition arc mirrors Vndr/Catr structure. Stages: Landing → Type → Profile → Spaces & Pricing → Money flows + Verification → Welcome dashboard. Locked.
  • Atmosphere Board collapse pattern per §47. Once 6+ photos + attestation, collapse to thumbnail strip + Cue read; Edit board button re-expands.
  • Editable pill rows for inclusions and restrictions. Suggested set + × on each active pill + “+ Add your own” inline draft form. Custom inclusions can carry an optional price (rose pill, italic price tag, future quote integration via title attribute).
  • Floor plan upload (v1) — per-layout upload cells (PDF or image), checkmark on uploaded state. Drag-drop builder deferred to Phase 2 per §57.
  • Multi-space onboarding — Hotel / Country club / Museum-Cultural-University / Mixed-use venue types auto-populate 3 spaces in Step 3 with smart placeholders by type.
  • Tax-exempt entity flow — Government and Non-profit entity selections surface a tax-exempt block (auto-checked for Government, optional for Non-profit) plus EIN field. Surfaces on contracts and 1099-K reporting.
  • Trust Badge — circular SVG crest, 4-point star centered, “EVNTCUE · VERIFIED VENUE ·” inscribed perimeter. Three tiers: Verified (bay blue) / Top Venue (silver) / Premier (gold). Tier track on welcome dashboard. Hero-anchored on dashboard.
  • Trust Score breakdown panel per §21 weighting. Verification (25%), Profile (30%), Response (20%), Booking completion (15%), Reviews (10%). Tier track shows progress to next tier.
  • Financial metrics with sample data on welcome dashboard — labeled “Sample · what a busy month looks like”. Real ledger sits below as the zero state. Demo-as-teacher pattern: literacy before data.
  • 4-state inquiry taxonomy on welcome dashboard sample inquiry: Ready to book (teal) / Quote sent (bay blue) / Browsing only (gold) / Capacity mismatch (rose, with Cue redirect suggestion).
  • Hero copy locked: “Deposits, not inquiries.” Subcopy: “Stop chasing unvetted leads. EvntCue sends you booked clients — vetted, with deposits already in escrow. List free. Reply. Get paid.”
  • Topbar chrome: 4-point star icon + EvntCue wordmark (italic Cormorant Evnt + plain Cue) on the left. Role pill (VENU bay blue) and step indicator on the right. Brand left, role right, step rightmost.
  • Comparison strip on landing — six competitors with feature dimensions: PartySlate (discovery only), Eventbrite Venues (built for ticketed events), HoneyBook (CRM tool, no marketplace demand), The Knot Pro (pay first, hope leads come), Tripleseat (powerful, per-seat cost wall). EvntCue framed as “Free to claim · deposits in escrow / Inquiries arrive qualified.”
  • “Venue” → “Venu” in user-facing copy. All UI labels, page titles, button labels, and role copy use “Venu” per §18 naming convention. The schema enum venue is preserved (no DB migration needed).

Workstation lineage — see §85

The freemium acquisition arc captured here is the front door. Every onboarding decision has a destination in the Workstation: Atmosphere Board → public profile + Cue match input. Floor plan upload → BEO Layout section. Custom inclusions → BEO Inclusions section. Money flows enabled → Earnings ledger panel. Verification gates → Trust Badge tier. See §85 Workstation Architecture for the full schema-to-screen lineage and the six-surface build order.
76 — Reporting — global decisions locked
Decisions made and locked across all portal reporting. These apply universally unless a portal-specific section overrides.

Core decisions — locked

DecisionLocked answerRationale
Report generation triggerAuto-generated 48 hours after event close. Also available on-demand at any time.48h gives time for post-event edits (actual food cost, labor hours) before the report locks. On-demand covers mid-event and pre-event planning needs.
Cue narrationEvery report view opens with a Cue narrative panel. Plain language. Headline insight first, supporting data below. Benchmarks included where meaningful (industry avg, DFW peer group, portal percentile).Raw numbers without context are noise. Cue turns them into decisions.
Export formatsPDF (for sharing, filing, printing) and CSV (for financial software). Both always available on every report. Never one without the other.PDF is a photograph. CSV is the data itself. Accountants, QuickBooks, Wave, FreshBooks all need CSV.
CSV cost field sign conventionIncome fields: positive. Cost fields: negative. Net fields: calculated sum. Consistent across all four portals that track costs.Signs must be consistent so CSVs import cleanly into any bookkeeping software without transformation. A positive food cost would require manual sign-flipping — unacceptable.
event_id as spineEvery CSV export from every portal uses event_id (EvntCue internal UUID) as the primary key. All CSV files from the same portal can be joined on event_id.When a user hands four CSVs to their accountant, the accountant can join them. This is the difference between data and usable data.
Period selectorThis month · This quarter · Year to date · Last year · Custom range. Defaults to YTD. Persistent per session.Consistent across all portals — the same muscle memory everywhere.
Report viewsOverview · By event · Post-event summaries · CSV specs. Tab-based. Consistent across all portals.Same navigation pattern across every portal — learn once, use everywhere.
QuickBooks / Wave / FreshBooks compatibilityAll revenue CSVs map cleanly to standard bookkeeping import formats. Field names documented in the CSV Specs view inside the app. Cue provides explicit import instructions per software.If the CSV doesn't import on the first try, it's a bad CSV. We own the import experience end to end.
Post-event summary auto-email48h after event close: auto-email to the portal user with PDF summary attached and link to full report in-app. Opt-out available in notification settings.Most users won't log in to check. Proactive delivery removes the friction of remembering.
1099-K trackingAll portal users receiving payments through EvntCue are tracked in annual_payments. When threshold is crossed ($600 in 2025 IRS rules), user is flagged and notified. EvntCue files 1099-K via Stripe. Applies to Vndr, Catr, Plnr, Venue.Legal obligation. Non-negotiable. Stripe handles the mechanics — EvntCue surfaces the status in the portal's finance section.
Commission language in exportsCSV field names use internal terminology (referral_earn_withheld, platform_fee, partnership_yield) but column headers in the downloaded file use plain English labels. PDF reports use fully plain language — no jargon.The CSV field name is for the developer and the schema. The column header is for Rosa's accountant who has never heard of EvntCue.

Landing screen — readiness dashboard

DecisionLocked answer
What Catr sees on loginReadiness dashboard — not a metrics dashboard. The chef's board, not the accountant's spreadsheet.
Hero cardFull-width next event hero. Three panels: event facts (date, covers, contact, money, bar status) · day-of timeline at a glance · readiness checklist with live progress bar. Tapping anywhere on the hero goes to the BEO.
Readiness checklist itemsBEO acknowledged · Menu confirmed · Labor plan set · Dietary flags reviewed · TABC renewal status (if alcohol). Tapping an incomplete item marks it done — progress bar updates live.

Upcoming events stripNext 3 events with readiness flags. Green checks and red alerts at a glance.
Right columnEarnings (with margin, not just revenue) · Trust score · Cert strip. Secondary context — not the first thing she sees.
Metrics demotedRevenue, trust score, etc. moved to right column and Analytics page. Not the landing experience.

BEO — event detail page

DecisionLocked answer
NavigationDashboard → tap any event → BEO. No intermediate page. The BEO is the event detail page.
SPA architectureDashboard and BEO are two views in one file. Fade + slide transition. Sidebar stays constant. Back button returns to dashboard.
Sidebar stateWhen in BEO: "Garcia Wedding · BEO" sub-item appears under Bookings, highlighted. Dashboard nav de-highlighted.
BEO content — read vs. editableRead + annotate model. Core event data (name, date, venue, covers, menu, dietary) is read-only — set at booking. Editable: timeline notes (per-row), labor plan (all fields), food cost actual, other costs, internal notes. Private notes are Catr-only — not visible to Plnr or Venue.
BEO sectionsHero header · Day-of timeline · Covers & meal selection · Dietary requirements + seat assignments · Confirmed menu · Labor plan · Cost & margin · Bar service + SafeTab · Notes & instructions (Plnr note · Venue note · Catr internal)
Live calculationsMeal count total updates as she edits counts (full / over / short indicator). Labor cost auto-calculates from staff × hours × rate. Margin bar updates as food cost and other costs are edited. Color: teal >35% · amber 20–35% · red <20%.
Acknowledge buttonTopbar right. On click: button state changes to "✓ BEO Acknowledged" + greyed. Confirmation strip slides in at top with timestamp. Plnr notified automatically.
Print BEOTopbar button. Calls window.print(). Future: proper print stylesheet.

Menu builder

DecisionLocked answer
Flow philosophyItem-first, not form-first. Start with "Add a dish." Cue surfaces structure progressively as items accumulate. No step wizard at entry.
Service styleSet once on profile — not Step 1 of the builder. Six types: Full service · Cocktail & passed · Buffet & stations · Dessert & sweet · Bar service only · Custom per event. Multi-select.
Menu sectionsCatr-named. No forced course structure. They name their own sections (Passed appetizers, Taco station, Dessert table). A dessert-only Catr never sees "Mains."
Cue triggersAfter 3 items: offer to organize into sections. After 6 items + organized: offer to build packages. Both are one-tap accepts or dismissible.
Dietary tagsSix: Vegan · GF · Kosher · Halal · Nut-free · Dairy-free. Dim until activated (tapped). Flow automatically to BEO dietary summary and guest dietary view on day-of.
PackagesBundle sections with per-head price and minimum guest count. One featured package. Cue offers to suggest packages after enough items exist.
Plnr previewButton generates a read-only view of what planners see — packages first, then itemized menu below.

Direct booking (in-app — not a second login)

DecisionLocked answer
ArchitectureIn-app booking mode toggle. Rosa stays Rosa. A "Direct booking" section lets her create events when she holds the client relationship. No second login, no second identity.
Direct events in the ecosystemDirect events still live in EvntCue. Can invite other vendors. Still generate a BEO. Catr owns the client relationship instead of a Plnr.
Future considerationThis is the wedge into a sixth user type — the independent operator who does everything. A "Pro" tier across portal types. Filed for roadmap consideration, not MVP scope.

Analytics & reporting

DecisionLocked answer
Report auto-generation48 hours after event close. Also available on-demand.
Cue narrationEvery report view. Plain language. Benchmark context (industry avg, DFW peer group). Headline insight first.
Four CSV exportscatr_revenue_by_event · catr_labor_by_event · catr_dietary_by_event · catr_safetab_by_event. All link via event_id. Locked field structures per §77.
Post-event auto-emailPDF summary emailed 48h after close. Opt-out in notification settings.
Tax software compatibilityQuickBooks Online · Wave · FreshBooks. Import instructions from Cue in CSV Specs view. Costs as negative fields — no transformation required.
83 — Admin platform controls — Cue kill switch + per-touchpoint disables
A platform-wide off switch for Cue, plus per-touchpoint granular disables. Failure isolation, not just emergency response.
Cue is the AI surface across all five portals. When the underlying API has an outage, when a prompt-injection vulnerability surfaces, when a model upgrade introduces unexpected behavior, or when a single touchpoint malfunctions in a brand-damaging way, the platform needs the ability to disable Cue surgically — without taking down the rest of EvntCue. This section specs a two-level control surface: global kill (everything off, every portal, every touchpoint) and per-touchpoint disable (turn off the broken touchpoint, leave the rest running).
The principle. An AI feature that cannot be turned off is a liability, not an asset. Every Cue surface — vendor matching, mood-board reading, run-of-show generation, post-event ROI, the Plnr recommendation gate — is a place where a model failure or API outage can produce wrong, embarrassing, or harmful output. The kill switch isn't optional infrastructure; it's the same category of must-have as a database backup or an SSL certificate.

Global kill switch — what "off" actually means

What stopsWhat stays runningWhat users see
All new Cue API calls across all portalsEvery non-Cue feature: bookings, escrow, Stripe, BEOs, calendars, RLS, marketplace searchCue UI replaced with graceful degradation state — never error-out the page
Credit consumption pausesExisting credit balances remainUsers mid-conversation do not lose credits to messages that won't send
In-flight Cue requests cancelled (best-effort)Already-completed Cue responses persist in conversation historySpinner/typing indicators clear; no half-sent state
Cue-driven proactive notifications haltTransactional notifications (bookings, payments, expiries) continue normallyStatus banner across all portals: "Cue is temporarily unavailable. We're on it."
Cue-dependent UI elements disabledManual workflows for everything Cue would have automatedAffordances grey out with hover-tooltip: "Currently offline — manual entry available"

Per-touchpoint disables — the nine Cue surfaces from §9 plus §42

Each Cue touchpoint can be independently toggled. If the post-event ROI report has a bug but vendor matching is fine, the admin disables only the broken touchpoint. The global kill flips every per-touchpoint toggle to off in one action, but per-touchpoint state is preserved so flipping global back to on restores the prior per-touchpoint configuration.
TouchpointSection refGraceful degradation when disabled
Vendor suggestion engine§9, §26Marketplace search returns results sorted by basic ranking (rating, distance, price) without Cue's six-factor weighting
Mood board narrative reading§47 Upgrade 1Mood board displays without aesthetic-summary annotation; vendor matching falls back to category-only
Auto-generated vendor brief§47 Upgrade 2Inquiry form shows blank text field with "Describe your vision" placeholder; Plnr/Orgnz writes their own brief
Style conflict detection§47 Upgrade 4Mood board accepts contradictory directions silently; conflicts surface only at first vendor meeting
Plnr recommendation gate§42All Orgnzs proceed in self-managed mode; no Plnr suggestion shown after budget
Run-of-show generator§9Plnr builds run-of-show manually from blank template
Post-event ROI report§9Plnr/Vndr sees raw numbers in Earnings tab; no narrative summary
Outbound proposal drafting§43Plnr writes proposals manually; mood board image picker remains functional
Significant-dates re-engagement§43Plnr CRM displays upcoming dates without draft outreach messages
Day-of monitoring alerts§9BEO surfaces flags inline; no proactive Cue alerts

Schema

Table / columnTypeNotes
platform_settings.cue_global_enabledboolean default trueThe master kill switch. False disables every Cue API call platform-wide. Toggled only by admin; logged in audit trail.
platform_settings.cue_global_disabled_attimestamptz nullableTimestamp of last global disable. Null when active.
platform_settings.cue_global_disabled_by_admin_iduuid nullableAdmin user who last toggled global state.
platform_settings.cue_global_disabled_reasontext nullableFree-text reason — surfaces in user-facing banner if set.
cue_touchpoint_statenew tableOne row per touchpoint. Columns: touchpoint_key (text PK, e.g. vendor_suggestion, plnr_gate), enabled boolean default true, disabled_at timestamptz, disabled_by_admin_id uuid, disabled_reason text. Seeded with all 10 touchpoints from §9 + §42.
cue_admin_audit_lognew tableAppend-only log of every admin toggle (global or per-touchpoint). Columns: id, admin_id, action enum(global_disable, global_enable, touchpoint_disable, touchpoint_enable), touchpoint_key nullable, reason, created_at. RLS: admin-only read; INSERT-only write (no UPDATE, no DELETE — same immutability pattern as SafeTab waivers per §67).

Server-side enforcement — fail-closed

Every Cue API call routes through a single server-side wrapper function — cueRequest(touchpoint_key, prompt, context) — which checks platform_settings.cue_global_enabled AND cue_touchpoint_state[touchpoint_key].enabled before issuing any Anthropic API call. If either is false, the wrapper returns a structured "disabled" response that the UI renders as graceful degradation. The kill switch must be enforced at the wrapper, not at the UI — UI-only disables can be bypassed by a malicious client; the server gate cannot.

Admin UI — placement and access

The admin platform-controls panel lives at /admin/platform/cue. Two sections: (1) Global kill switch — single large toggle with "Disable Cue platform-wide" / "Enable Cue platform-wide" labels, requires confirmation modal with reason field, shows last-toggled timestamp and admin name. (2) Per-touchpoint grid — 10 toggle rows, each with a "Why?" link that opens the §-reference and degradation behavior. Both sections show real-time status indicators (green dot = active, amber dot = degraded, red dot = disabled).
Access control. Only users with users.role = 'admin' can view or modify these controls. Two-admin-confirmation requirement on global kill (one admin proposes, second admin confirms within 5 minutes) — same break-glass pattern as production database access. Per-touchpoint disables are single-admin to keep response fast for known issues.

User-facing degradation copy

When Cue is globally disabled, every portal shows a non-dismissible status banner above the topbar: "Cue is temporarily unavailable — your data and bookings are unaffected." The banner uses warm amber tones, not red, to signal "known issue, contained" rather than "platform broken." If a reason is set in cue_global_disabled_reason and is user-safe (admin-flagged before display), it appears below: e.g., "We're upgrading Cue's matching engine. Back online by 4pm CT."
Per-touchpoint disables surface inline at the affected feature only. The Cue chip in the topbar continues to function for non-disabled touchpoints. The mental model: Cue degrades like a power grid, not like a circuit breaker. One bad surface dims; the rest stay lit.

Status page integration

EvntCue maintains a public status page at status.evntcue.com. Every global kill or significant per-touchpoint disable automatically posts an incident on the status page with the admin-supplied reason. Resolved incidents auto-update when the toggle returns to enabled. This builds the same trust pattern that AWS, Stripe, and GitHub use — transparency about degradation increases user confidence rather than decreasing it.
84 — Legacy account status — custom monthly pricing override
Grandfather pricing, partner deals, edge cases. Built into the schema from day one.
Every multi-tenant SaaS eventually needs custom pricing for specific tenants — early supporters who locked in a founding rate, strategic partners with negotiated terms, edge cases that don't fit the standard tier matrix, refunds-as-credit-toward-next-month arrangements. Building this in from the schema layer is cheap; bolting it on later means a billing-system rewrite. The legacy account flag is a forward-compatibility decision, not a feature for v1 launch.
The principle. Standard tier pricing per §19 is the default for 99% of tenants. The legacy flag exists for the 1% — and forces every billing path through a single decision: "is this tenant on standard pricing or override pricing?" That decision lives in one place, evaluated once per billing cycle, with full audit trail. Without this structure, custom pricing requests get handled as one-off Stripe edits with no audit trail and no consistency.

Schema additions to tenants table

ColumnTypeDefaultNotes
legacy_pricingbooleanfalseMaster flag. When true, billing path uses override price object instead of standard tier price.
legacy_monthly_centsinteger nullableNULLCustom monthly amount in cents. Required when legacy_pricing = true. CHECK constraint: must be NULL when flag is false, must be NOT NULL when flag is true.
legacy_annual_centsinteger nullableNULLOptional custom annual amount. If NULL when flag is true, monthly billing is the only option for that tenant.
legacy_stripe_price_idtext nullableNULLThe Stripe price object ID for this tenant's custom price. Created in Stripe at the moment the legacy flag is enabled. Stored here for billing-path lookup.
legacy_pricing_notetext nullableNULLAdmin context. Why is this tenant on legacy pricing? Examples: "Founding member — locked at $19/mo." "Strategic partner — DFW Wedding Association — negotiated $0/mo for 12 months." "Refund-as-credit — see ticket #4821."
legacy_pricing_approved_by_admin_iduuid nullableNULLAdmin user who approved the legacy status. Required when flag is true.
legacy_pricing_approved_attimestamptz nullableNULLTimestamp of approval. Cannot be modified after set — append-only via trigger.
legacy_pricing_expires_attimestamptz nullableNULLOptional expiry. NULL means perpetual; a date means revert to standard pricing on that date. Cron job expire_legacy_pricing runs nightly to flip flag back to false on expiring rows.

Billing-path decision — single function

All Stripe subscription creation and update calls route through resolveTenantPriceId(tenant_id), which returns either the standard tier price ID from §19 or the tenant's legacy_stripe_price_id. This function is the only place in the codebase that decides which price applies. Calling Stripe APIs with hardcoded price IDs anywhere else is a security review failure.
function resolveTenantPriceId(tenant_id, billing_period = 'monthly') {
  const tenant = await db.tenants.findOne({ id: tenant_id });

  // Legacy pricing path
  if (tenant.legacy_pricing) {
    if (!tenant.legacy_stripe_price_id) {
      throw new Error('Legacy flag set but no price ID — schema constraint violated');
    }
    return tenant.legacy_stripe_price_id;
  }

  // Standard pricing path — §19 tier matrix
  return STANDARD_PRICE_IDS[tenant.type][tenant.plan][billing_period];
}

Admin UI — placement and workflow

The admin tenant-detail page at /admin/tenants/[id] includes a "Legacy pricing" panel below the standard tier display. When the flag is off, the panel shows a single "Set custom pricing" button. Clicking it opens a modal:
FieldRequiredBehavior
Custom monthly rate (USD)YesEnter dollars; backend stores cents. Validates > 0.
Custom annual rate (USD)NoOptional. If empty, tenant is monthly-only.
Reason / contextYesFree text, minimum 20 characters. Becomes legacy_pricing_note.
Expires onNoDate picker. Empty means perpetual.
Confirmation checkboxYes"I understand this overrides standard tier pricing for this tenant. The change will take effect on the next billing cycle."
On submit, the backend (1) creates a Stripe price object via Stripe API, (2) updates the tenant's existing subscription to the new price ID with proration_behavior: 'none' so the change applies on the next cycle without retroactive credit, (3) sets all eight legacy fields atomically in a transaction, (4) writes a row to tenant_admin_audit_log.

What's intentionally not in scope

Out of scopeWhy
Per-feature pricing overridesStandard plan + custom rate covers 99% of cases. Per-feature pricing is a feature-flag system, not a pricing system. Build separately if needed.
Tenant self-service legacy enableAdmin-only forever. A tenant who could flip themselves to legacy pricing would defeat the entire point.
Public marketing of legacy availabilityLegacy pricing is for known partners and edge cases, not a sales lever. Never advertised.
Migration tools to legacy from standardManual admin action only. Removes the temptation to mass-migrate tenants for revenue-shaping reasons that conflict with the §19 pricing thesis.

Reporting and reconciliation

Admin reporting includes a "Legacy pricing roster" view: every tenant with legacy_pricing = true, their custom rate, expiry date if any, approving admin, and reason note. Monthly reconciliation cron job verifies that every legacy tenant's Stripe subscription matches their legacy_stripe_price_id — drift triggers an admin alert. Total legacy MRR is reported separately from standard MRR for accurate financial forecasting.

Future hooks — pre-built but not surfaced in v1

The schema supports use cases not yet built: (1) Tier-locked legacy — a legacy tenant remains on a specific plan tier (e.g. "Pro features at Solo price") via a separate legacy_plan_lock column not yet added. (2) Cohort-based legacy — multiple tenants on identical legacy pricing (e.g. all founding partners at $19/mo) referenced by a shared legacy_cohort_id. (3) Auto-renewal legacy — annual rates that auto-renew at custom rate rather than reverting to standard. All three are buildable on top of the v1 schema without breaking changes.
85 — Workstation architecture (added v26.7)
The daily product. The thing the venue manager opens at 8am Monday and closes at 6pm Friday. The SaaS that justifies the subscription. Specced as six surfaces that compose into one product.

The principle

The event record is the gravity well. Every venue’s daily life is anchored to specific upcoming events. Inquiries get promoted to events. Quotes hang off events. BEOs are of events. Payments schedule against events. Communications thread through events. Vendor coordination happens for events. Reviews get written about events. The Workstation is structured as orbits around the event record, not as features bolted to a dashboard. Get the event detail view right and the rest of the product’s information architecture falls into place. Get it wrong and every other screen has to compensate.

The six surfaces

SurfaceJobKey tablesRelationship to event record
1 · Event DetailThe gravity well. Where 80% of working hours happen. Five-tab record: Overview / BEO / Comms / Payments / Tasks.events, beo_documents, event_communications, payment_schedules, tasks, event_participants, run_of_showIS the event record. Other surfaces orbit around it.
2 · Calendar & PipelineAbove-the-event navigation. Multi-space day/week/month grid. Pipeline view: stages from inquiry to confirmed.events, spaces, holds, booking_status_logLists events. Click an event → opens Event Detail.
3 · Inquiry TriageThe inbox. New inquiries land here with qualification badges. Cue-drafted first responses. Promote to event.inquiries, event_participants, cue_draftsInquiries become events. Triage → promote → opens Event Detail.
4 · ReportingCross-event analytics. Per §76 global reporting decisions. CSV exports keyed on event_id. Cue narrative leads each report view.Aggregates over events, annual_payments, all four §34 fee flowsReports across events. Drill-down opens Event Detail filtered to one event.
5 · Admin / SettingsTenant config. Spaces, fees, vendor preferred-list, integrations, gate-mode toggles, user/role permissions, billing.tenants, spaces, tenant_fee_config, tenant_users, integrations, verification_gate_configConfigures the rules that govern Event Detail behavior.
6 · Cue Assistant SurfaceCross-cutting. Where Cue drafts replies, surfaces follow-ups, flags anomalies, narrates reports. Not a tab — a presence threaded through every other surface.cue_drafts, cue_followups, cue_anomalies, cue_narrativesActs on events. Cue UI surfaces in every other workstation surface.

Build order — locked v26.7

OrderSurfaceWhy this position
1Event DetailThe gravity well. Without this, the other five have nothing concrete to point at. Every schema-to-screen lineage decision compounds from here.
2Calendar + PipelineSame population (whoever opens the workstation needs to see what’s happening this week). Shares pattern language with Triage. Build together.
3Inquiry TriageWhere new bookings enter the system. Now that Event Detail exists, Triage has a concrete “promote to event” destination.
4ReportingAggregates over events. Needs Event Detail’s data shape locked first.
5Admin / SettingsConfiguration surface. Can be built in parallel with anything but doesn’t unblock anything else.
6Cue Assistant SurfaceThreads through everything. Designs only crystallize once the surfaces it threads through exist. Build last.

Cross-portal scope

Each surface has portal-specific variants. The Workstation isn’t four separate workstations; it’s one architectural pattern with four content-and-permission variants. A Vndr Event Detail and a Venu Event Detail share component vocabulary, RLS scope, and Cue surface conventions; they differ in tab content (Vndr has no BEO; Venu has no booth setup logistics) and in default views. Each handoff specifies its own portal scope. Never build a portal-specific workstation surface without confirming the four-portal pattern.

Schema-to-screen lineage — first artifact of every workstation session

Before drawing a rectangle in any workstation session, produce a schema-to-screen lineage map for that surface. For Event Detail: every column in events, beo_documents, event_communications, payment_schedules, tasks, event_participants maps to a tab and a UI element. RLS scope identified per role. This map is the brief that prevents the workstation from becoming a thousand small compromises against the schema.

Drift policy

If a Workstation session’s design conflicts with this masterdoc, the masterdoc wins until the session produces a written exception ratified by the next masterdoc revision. The handoff prompts enforce this by instructing future Claude to read the masterdoc first, write the plan in writing, refuse to ship code that conflicts with locked decisions. Drift is inevitable across multi-session work; this is the governance that catches it.
